The Role of Biographical Indexes in Hanafi Iftaa Studies
Biographical index of scholars cited in Adab al-Fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how a biographical index contextualizes scholarly authority in fatwa manuals and explain its relevance to Hanafi iftaa methodology.

Core Idea
Biographical indexes ground fatwa methodology in scholarly lineage, linking rulings to their transmitters.

This lesson explores the biographical index from Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Mufti, a Shafi'i classic on fatwa etiquette. Although the source is Shafi'i, the structure and purpose of such indexes are universal in Islamic jurisprudence. Understanding who these scholars were and why they are cited helps you evaluate the authority of transmitted opinions in Hanafi fatwa practice. We'll examine the index's layout and the type of information it provides, then apply it to a hypothetical fatwa scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the index's purpose
Recognize that this index is a quick-reference tool for the main text's citations. It provides essential biographical data to assess a scholar's reliability and school affiliation.
In Hanafi iftaa, biographical verification (jarh wa ta'dil) is crucial for accepting a riwayah.
2
Parse a sample entry
Take Ibn Abi Layla's entry: full name, kunya, nisba, scholarly rank (Tabi'un), death date. Note the quotes from contemporaries that attest to his knowledge.
Pay attention to the pattern: name → lineage → scholarly context → death → references.
3
Relate to Hanafi iftaa needs
A Hanafi mufti encountering a citation from Ibn Abi Layla uses this index to determine his era (Tabi'un) and thus the strength of a mursal report or his opinion on a matter.
Even if the original work is Shafi'i, the biographies often include scholars respected across madhhabs.
4
Apply to a fatwa context
Imagine a case where a mufti must decide between two transmitted opinions – one from Ibn Abi Layla and one from a later scholar. The index helps weigh seniority and rigor.
This is an example of how biographical indexes support the usul al-iftaa process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهرس الأعلام
التعريف بالأعلام الواردة فى آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى
-١ ابن أبي ليلى : هو عبد الرحمن بن يسار المعروف بابن أبي ليلى الأنصارى، الأوسى، أبو عيسى، الكوفي، من أجلة التابعين . قال عطاء بن السائب، عن عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلي : " أدركت عشرين ومائة من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كلهم من الأنصار، إذا سئل أحدهم عن شيء أحب أن يكفيه صاحبه". قال عبدالملك بن عمير : "لقد رأيت عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى في حلقة فيها نفر من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يستمعون الحديثه وينصتون له فيهم البراء بن عازب . قال محمد بن سيرين : جلست إلى عبد الرحمن ابن أبي ليلى، وأصحابه يعظمونه كأنه أمير " . قال ثابت البناني : "كنا إذا قعدنا إلى عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى قال لرجل : اقرأ القرآن، فإنه يدلني على ما تريدون، نزلت هذه الآية كذا"، وهذه الآية كذا. مات سنة ٨٣/٨٢هـ . (راجع : تهذيب الكمال : ٣٥٢/١١، وسير أعلام النبلاء : ٢٤٥/٥)
- ابن برهان : هو أبو الفتح أحمد بن على بن برهان (بفتح الباء) الحنبلي ثم الشافعي، ولد ببغداد في شوال سنة تسع وسبعين وأربع مائة، وتفقه على الغزالي، والكيا، والشاشي وبرع في المذهب، وفي الأصول، وكان هو الغالب عليه، وله فيه التصانيف المشهورة : "البسيط" و "الوسيط" و "الوجيز" وغيرها . رحل إليه الطلبة . من البلاد، واستغرق نهاره وبعض ليله في إقرائهم، ودرس بالنظامية شهراً ثم عزل، وكان ذكيا يضرب به المثل في حل الإشكال، توفى سنة عشرين وخمسمائة، وقيل: غير ذلك. (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٢٠٧/١)
- ابن الصباغ : أبو نصر عبد السيد بن أبي ظاهر محمد بن عبد الواحد ابن محمد البغدادي المعروف بابن الصباغ. أخذ عن القاضي أبي الطيب وبرع حتى رجحوه في المذهب على الشيخ أبي إسحاق، وكان خيرا ، دينا ، درس بالنظامية أول ما فتحت، وذلك في سنة تسع وخمسين وأربع مائة ثم عزل بعد عشرين يوما بالشيخ أبي إسحاق، وذلك لأنها بنيت لأجل الشيخ فلم يجب إلى ذلك، وامتنع من الخروج من المسجد الذي يدرس فيه، وهو المسجد الذي بدرب الزعفرانى وكان الشافعي يدرس فيه . قال ابن خلكان ولد رحمه الله سنة أربع مائة وتوفى يوم الثلاثاء، الثالث عشر من جمادى الأولى سنة سبع وسبعين قال : وقيل : بل توفى يوم الخميس، منتصف شعبان ، من السنة المذكورة، ودفن يوم الأربعاء بداره ثم نقل إلى بناب حرب. (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوی : ۲/ ۱۳۰ ، ۱۳۱)
- ابن الصلاح : عثمان بن عبد الرحمن بن عثمان ابن صلاح الدين بن تقی الدين، أبو عمرو الكردي، الشهرزوری ،النصري الشرخانی، الفقيه الشافعي المعروف بابن الصلاح، ولد سنة ٥٧٧ وتوفى سنة ٦٤٣ ، من تصانيفه الأحاديث الكلية"، في ۲۹ حديثًا، "أدب المفتى والمستفتى"، "تعليقه على شرح الوسائل للغزالي الرحلة الشرقية" ، "صلة الناسك في صفة المناسك" ، "فوائد الرحلة"، "كتاب في أصول الحديث"، "الفتاوى" و "نكت على علوم الحديث " . (هدية العارفين : ٦٥٤/١)
- ابن المنذر : هو أبو بكر محمد بن إبراهيم بن المنذر النيسابوري، نزيل مكة شرفها الله تعالى- أحد الأئمة الأعلام، لم يقلد أحدا في آخر عمره، قال الشيخ أبو إسحاق: توفى إما سنة تسع أو عشر وثلاثمائة، وله تصانيف كثيرة، منها "الإجماع و الأشراف" و "الإقناع" . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٣٧٤/٢)
Index of Biographies
Definition of the prominent figures appearing in Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
-1 Ibn Abi Layla: He is Abdur Rahman bin Yasar, known as Ibn Abi Layla al-Ansari, al-Awsi, Abu Isa, al-Kufi, one of the great Tabi'un. Ata bin al-Sa'ib said from Abdur Rahman bin Abi Layla: 'I met one hundred and twenty of the Companions of the Prophet (ﷺ), all of them from the Ansar; when any of them was asked about something, he would prefer that his companion suffice him.' Abd al-Malik bin Umayr said: 'I saw Abdur Rahman bin Abi Layla in a circle in which were a number of the Companions of the Prophet (ﷺ) listening to his hadith and becoming silent before him, among them al-Bara bin Azib.' Muhammad bin Sirin said: 'I sat with Abdur Rahman bin Abi Layla, and his companions honored him as if he were an amir.' Thabit al-Bunani said: 'When we sat with Abdur Rahman bin Abi Layla, he would say to a man: Recite the Quran, for it guides me to what you want; this verse was revealed about such-and-such, and this verse about such-and-such.' He died in the year 82/83 AH. (Refer: Tahdhib al-Kamal 11/352, Siyar A'lam al-Nubala 5/245)
- Ibn Burhan: He is Abu al-Fath Ahmad bin Ali bin Burhan (with fatha on ba), al-Hanbali then al-Shafi'i. He was born in Baghdad in Shawwal 479 AH. He studied under al-Ghazali, al-Kiya, and al-Shashi, and excelled in the madhhab and in usul, the latter being predominant over him. He authored famous works: al-Basit, al-Wasit, al-Wajiz, and others. Students traveled to him from various lands. He spent his days and part of the night teaching them. He taught at the Nizamiyya for a month then was dismissed. He was intelligent, and proverbs were made about his ability to solve problems. He died in 520 AH, and some say otherwise. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 1/207)
- Ibn al-Sabbagh: Abu Nasr Abd al-Sayyid bin Abi Zahir Muhammad bin Abd al-Wahid bin Muhammad al-Baghdadi, known as Ibn al-Sabbagh. He studied under Qadi Abu al-Tayyib and excelled until they preferred him over Shaykh Abu Ishaq. He was good, religious. He taught at the Nizamiyya when it first opened, in 459 AH, then was dismissed after twenty days in favor of Shaykh Abu Ishaq, because it was built for the Shaykh, but he did not respond, so he refused to leave the mosque where he taught, which is the mosque in Darb al-Za'farani where al-Shafi'i used to teach. Ibn Khallikan said: He was born in 400 AH and died on Tuesday, 13 Jumada al-Ula 477 AH, and it was said: on Thursday, mid-Sha'ban of the same year, and was buried on Wednesday in his house then transferred to the cemetery of Harb. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 2/130-131)
- Ibn al-Salah: Uthman bin Abd al-Rahman bin Uthman Ibn Salah al-Din bin Taqi al-Din, Abu Amr al-Kurdi, al-Shahrazuri, al-Nasri, al-Sharkhani, the Shafi'i faqih known as Ibn al-Salah. He was born in 577 AH and died in 643 AH. Among his works: al-Ahadith al-Kulliyya (29 hadiths), Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti, Ta'liqa on Sharh al-Wasa'il by al-Ghazali, al-Rihla al-Sharqiyya, Silat al-Nasik fi Sifat al-Manasik, Fawa'id al-Rihla, a book on Usul al-Hadith, al-Fatawa, and Nukat 'ala Ulum al-Hadith. (Hadiyyat al-Arifin 1/654)
- Ibn al-Mundhir: He is Abu Bakr Muhammad bin Ibrahim bin al-Mundhir al-Naysaburi, resident of Mecca (may Allah honor it), one of the prominent imams. He did not follow anyone in the latter part of his life. Shaykh Abu Ishaq said: He died either in 309 or 310 AH. He has many works, including al-Ijma' wa al-Ashraf and al-Iqna'. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 2/374)
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index from Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Mufti, a classical Shafi'i manual on the etiquette of issuing fatwas. The commentator here provides concise yet rich biographies of leading scholars whose opinions or methodologies are cited in the main work. For each entry, the author traces scholarly lineage, includes notable statements from contemporaries, and gives death dates along with references. The inclusion of this index in the Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti suggests that the editor or commentator considered familiarity with these figures essential for understanding the development of fatwa methodology. Although the original work is Shafi'i, the biographies are of scholars who are widely respected across madhhabs, and their contributions to usul al-fiqh and fatwa procedures are relevant to Hanafi students as well. The entries follow a consistent pattern: full name, scholarly affiliation, educational background, key contributions, and death date. This allows the reader to quickly contextualize the authorities mentioned in the main text of the fatwa manual.

Key Terms
فهرس الأعلام (Fahras al-A'lam): Index of prominent figures; a list of biographical entries for scholars referenced in the main text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the index, which of the following scholars authored 'Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti'?
A) Ibn Abi Layla
B) Ibn Burhan
C) Ibn al-Sabbagh
D) Ibn al-Salah

Key Takeaway
A biographical index provides essential contextual data for evaluating the authority of cited scholars, a skill critical for muftis regardless of madhhab.

Life of the Author

Biographical Index in Adab al-Mufti: Knowing the Authorities
Biographical list of key scholars referenced in fatwa literature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholars referenced in fatwa literature and explain why their backgrounds matter for evaluating transmitted rulings.

Core Idea
A mufti must know the authorities he cites—their madhhab, reliability, and role in transmission.

This passage is a biographical index from Imam al-Nawawi's classic work on fatwa etiquette. It lists the lives of scholars such as Ibn al-Sabbagh, Ibn al-Salah, and Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi. Understanding who these scholars were helps a mufti assess the weight of their opinions and ensure correct attribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and epithet
Read the opening line that introduces each scholar with his full name and nickname (e.g., 'Ibn al-Sabbagh: Abu Nasr...').
The epithet often indicates a notable characteristic or lineage.
2
Note the madhhab and specialty
Determine from the text whether the scholar is Shafi'i, Hanafi, etc., and what field they specialized in (fiqh, hadith, usul).
This affects how their works are used in fatwa.
3
Extract key biographical data
Note birth/death years, teachers, students, and major works mentioned.
Dates help situate the scholar in the chain of transmission.
4
Assess relevance to fatwa methodology
Identify what contribution this scholar made to the science of fatwa (e.g., Ibn al-Salah wrote Adab al-Mufti).
Some scholars are more procedural, others substantive.
5
Connect to the mufti's practice
Consider why a mufti needs this information when citing a scholar in a fatwa.
Authority varies by madhhab and field.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى
فهرس الأعلام - ابن الصباغ : أبو نصر عبد السيد بن أبي ظاهر محمد بن عبد الواحد ابن محمد البغدادي المعروف بابن الصباغ. أخذ عن القاضي أبي الطيب وبرع حتى رجحوه في المذهب على الشيخ أبي إسحاق، وكان خيرا ، دينا ، درس بالنظامية أول ما فتحت، وذلك في سنة تسع وخمسين وأربع مائة ثم عزل بعد عشرين يوما بالشيخ أبي إسحاق، وذلك لأنها بنيت لأجل الشيخ فلم يجب إلى ذلك، وامتنع من الخروج من المسجد الذي يدرس فيه، وهو المسجد الذي بدرب الزعفرانى وكان الشافعي يدرس فيه . قال ابن خلكان ولد رحمه الله سنة أربع مائة وتوفى يوم الثلاثاء، الثالث عشر من جمادى الأولى سنة سبع وسبعين قال : وقيل : بل توفى يوم الخميس، منتصف شعبان ، من السنة المذكورة، ودفن يوم الأربعاء بداره ثم نقل إلى بناب حرب. (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوی : ۲/ ۱۳۰ ، ۱۳۱)
- ابن الصلاح : عثمان بن عبد الرحمن بن عثمان ابن صلاح الدين بن تقی الدين، أبو عمرو الكردي، الشهرزوری ،النصري الشرخانی، الفقيه الشافعي المعروف بابن الصلاح، ولد سنة ٥٧٧ وتوفى سنة ٦٤٣ ، من تصانيفه الأحاديث الكلية"، في ۲۹ حديثًا، "أدب المفتى والمستفتى"، "تعليقه على شرح الوسائل للغزالي الرحلة الشرقية" ، "صلة الناسك في صفة المناسك" ، "فوائد الرحلة"، "كتاب في أصول الحديث"، "الفتاوى" و "نكت على علوم الحديث " . (هدية العارفين : ٦٥٤/١)
- ابن المنذر : هو أبو بكر محمد بن إبراهيم بن المنذر النيسابوري، نزيل مكة شرفها الله تعالى- أحد الأئمة الأعلام، لم يقلد أحدا في آخر عمره، قال الشيخ أبو إسحاق: توفى إما سنة تسع أو عشر وثلاثمائة، وله تصانيف كثيرة، منها "الإجماع و الأشراف" و "الإقناع" . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٣٧٤/٢)
- ابن المنكدر : هو الإمام محمد بن عبد الله شيخ الإسلام، كـان مـعـدن الصدق، وكان ثقة حافظا، سيداً للقراء، كثير الخشية. سمع من السيدة عائشة وأبى هريرة وابن عباس، وجابر وغيرهم رضى الله عنهم - وتوفى رحمه الله سنة ثلاثين ومائة . (تذكرة الحفاظ : ۱۲۷/۱ ، وشذرات الذهب : ۲۲/۱-۱۷۷)
أبو جعفر الطحاوى : أحمد بن محمد بن سلامة أبو جعفر الطحاوي، الأزدى، إمام جليل القدر ، مشهور في الآفاق ذكره الجميل مملوء في بطون الأوراق . ولد سنة تسع وعشرين وقيل : سنة ثلاثين ومائتين، ومات سنة إحدى وعشرين وثلاثمائة وكان يقرأ على المزني الشافعي وهو خاله، وكان الطحاوى يكثر النظر في كتب أبى حنيفة ، فقال له المزنى : " والله لا يجيء منك شيء " . فغضب وانتقل من عنده . وتفقه في ، مذهب أبي حنيفة وصار إماما ، فكان إذا درس أو أجاب في شيء من المشكلات يقول : رحم الله خالي لو كان حيا لكفر عن يمينه " أخذ الطحاوى الفقه عن أبي جعفر أحمد ثم خرج إلى الشام فلقى بها " أبا خازم عبد الحميد" قاضی القضاة بالشام، فأخذ عنه عن عيسى بن أبان عن محمد . وكان إماما في الأحاديث والأخبار . وله تصانيف جليلة معتبرة فمنها : أحكام القرآن" و "کتاب معانی الآثار" و مشكل الآثار" و "المختصر" و "شرح الجامع الكبير " و "شرح الجامع الصغير" و كتاب الشروط الكبير والصغير والأوسط والمحاضر والسجلات والوصايا والفرائض " و "كتاب مناقب أبي حنيفة" و "تاريخ كبير " و "النوادر الفقهية". (الفوائد البهية : ٤١ - ٤٢)
- أبو جعفر النحاس: أبو جعفر النحاس أحمد بن محمد بن إسماعيل المرادى، المصرى النحوى، كان ينظر بابن الأنبارى ونفطويه . وله تصانيف كثيرة وكان مقتراً على نفسه في لباسه وطعامه . توفى مغروقاً بمصر في ذي الحجة سنة ٣٣٨هـ. قال السيوطي في حسن المحاضرة: "وقد أخذ عن الأخفش الصغير وغيره، وروى الحديث عن النسائي " . ومن مصنفاته: "تفسير القرآن" و "الناسخ والمنسوخ و شرح
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
Index of Notable Figures - Ibn al-Sabbagh: Abu Nasr Abd al-Sayyid ibn Abi Zahir Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi known as Ibn al-Sabbagh. He studied under Qadi Abu al-Tayyib and excelled until they preferred him in the school over Shaykh Abu Ishaq. He was good, religious. He taught at the Nizamiyya when it first opened, in the year 459 AH, then was removed after twenty days by Shaykh Abu Ishaq, because it was built for the shaykh and he did not respond to that, and he refused to leave the mosque where he taught, which is the mosque in Darb al-Za'farani where al-Shafi'i used to teach. Ibn Khallikan said: He was born in 400 AH and died on Tuesday, 13 Jumada al-Ula 477 AH. It is said he died on Thursday, mid-Sha'ban of the same year, and was buried on Wednesday in his house then transferred to Bab Harb. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnavi: 2/130-131)
- Ibn al-Salah: Uthman ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Uthman ibn Salah al-Din ibn Taqi al-Din, Abu Amr al-Kurdi, al-Shahrazuri, al-Nasri al-Sharkhani, the Shafi'i jurist known as Ibn al-Salah. Born 577 AH, died 643 AH. His works include: al-Ahadith al-Kulliyya (29 hadith), Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti, his commentary on Sharh al-Wasa'il by al-Ghazali, al-Rihla al-Sharqiyya, Silat al-Nasik fi Sifat al-Manasik, Fawa'id al-Rihla, a book on usul al-hadith, al-Fatawa, and Nukat 'ala Ulum al-Hadith. (Hadiyyat al-'Arifin: 1/654)
- Ibn al-Mundhir: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Mundhir al-Naysaburi, resident of Mecca (may Allah honor it), one of the distinguished imams. He did not blindly follow anyone in his later life. Shaykh Abu Ishaq said: He died either in 309 or 310 AH. He has many works, including al-Ijma' wa al-Ishraf and al-Iqna'. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnavi: 2/374)
- Ibn al-Munkadir: Imam Muhammad ibn Abd Allah, Shaykh al-Islam. He was a mine of truthfulness, trustworthy, a memorizer, a master of reciters, one of great fear of Allah. He heard from Aisha, Abu Huraira, Ibn Abbas, Jabir, and others (may Allah be pleased with them). He died in 130 AH. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz: 1/127, Shadharat al-Dhahab: 1/177-22)
- Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salama Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi al-Azdi, an imam of great standing, famous in all regions, full of beautiful mention in the pages of books. He was born in 229 AH (or 230 AH) and died in 321 AH. He used to study under al-Muzani al-Shafi'i, who was his maternal uncle. Al-Tahawi frequently studied the books of Abu Hanifa, so al-Muzani said to him: "By Allah, you will not amount to anything." He became angry and left him. He then studied the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and became an imam. When he taught or answered difficult questions, he would say: "May Allah have mercy on my uncle; if he were alive, he would have broken his oath." Al-Tahawi took fiqh from Abu Ja'far Ahmad, then went to Syria where he met Abu Khazim Abd al-Hamid, the chief qadi of Syria, and learned from him from Isa ibn Aban from Muhammad. He was an imam in hadith and reports. He has many esteemed works including: Ahkam al-Qur'an, Kitab Ma'ani al-Athar, Mushkil al-Athar, al-Mukhtasar, Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir, Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, Kitab al-Shurut (large, small, and medium), al-Muhadir wa al-Sijillat wa al-Wasaya wa al-Fara'id, Kitab Manaqib Abi Hanifa, Tarikh Kabir, and al-Nawadir al-Fiqhiyya. (al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya: 41-42)
- Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas: Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Muradi, the Egyptian grammarian. He used to compare with Ibn al-Anbari and Niftawayh. He has many works and was frugal in dress and food. He died drowned in Egypt in Dhu al-Hijjah 338 AH. Al-Suyuti said in Husn al-Muhadara: "He studied under al-Akhfash al-Saghir and others, and narrated hadith from al-Nasa'i." His works include: Tafsir al-Qur'an and al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh wa Sharh.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index (فهرس الأعلام) from Imam al-Nawawi's work on the etiquette of issuing fatwas (آداب الفتوى). It provides concise life accounts of key scholars whose names appear in the main text, giving students essential context. The first entry is Ibn al-Sabbagh, a prominent Shafi'i jurist who taught at the Nizamiyya school. The second is Ibn al-Salah, author of the famous 'Ulum al-Hadith and a work on mufti adab. Third is Ibn al-Mundhir, an independent mujtahid known for his works on consensus. Fourth is Ibn al-Munkadir, a trustworthy hadith transmitter among the Tabi'un. Fifth is Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, a key Hanafi imam who initially studied Shafi'i fiqh under his uncle al-Muzani but converted to the Hanafi school after studying Abu Hanifa's works; his story illustrates the depth of his commitment. Finally, Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas is a grammarian and Quranic exegete. For students of Hanafi fatwa methodology, al-Tahawi is particularly important as a transmitter of Hanafi doctrine through his works like Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Nawadir al-Fiqhiyya. The index helps the reader identify the authority and madhhab of each cited scholar.

Key Terms
ابن الصباغ (Ibn al-Sabbagh): Abu Nasr Abd al-Sayyid al-Baghdadi, a Shafi'i jurist who taught at the Nizamiyya school
ابن الصلاح (Ibn al-Salah): Uthman ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Shahrazuri, a Shafi'i hadith specialist and author of 'Ulum al-Hadith
أبو جعفر الطحاوى (Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi): Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Azdi, a leading Hanafi imam and hadith scholar
آداب الفتوى (Adab al-Fatwa): The etiquette and methodology of issuing fatwas, as compiled by Imam al-Nawawi

Key Takeaway
Knowing the biographical background of cited scholars is essential for proper attribution and for assessing the authority of their rulings in fatwa.

The Life and Works of Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi: A Hanafi Paradigm
Biography of Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details and scholarly contributions of Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi and explain why his works are authoritative in Hanafi iftaa.

Core Idea
Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi turned rejection by his Shafi'i uncle into mastery of Hanafi fiqh, authoring works still cited in fatwa today.

In this lesson, we examine the biography of Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, one of the greatest Hanafi scholars. His story illustrates how personal challenges can spur scholarly excellence. We will focus on how a mufti must know the authoritativeness of works like al-Tahawi's 'Mukhtasar' and his hadith compilations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and lineage
Note the name, tribal affiliation, and teachers. For al-Tahawi, his connection to al-Muzani (Shafi'i) and Abu Khazim (Hanafi) is critical.
Al-Tahawi's uncle al-Muzani was a leading Shafi'i, yet al-Tahawi became a Hanafi imam.
2
Analyze the turning point story
Read al-Muzani's harsh dismissal and al-Tahawi's response. This shows the role of motivation in scholarship.
Al-Tahawi later prayed that his uncle would have to expiate, indicating the gravity of his uncle's oath.
3
List al-Tahawi's major works
Identify works like 'Mushkil al-Athar', 'Ma'ani al-Athar', 'al-Mukhtasar', and commentaries on the Jami' works. Understand which are core to Hanafi fatwa.
His 'Mukhtasar' is a standard text in Hanafi curriculum.
4
Understand the scholarly chain (isnad)
Al-Tahawi's chain: from Abu Khazim from 'Isa ibn Aban from Muhammad (al-Shaybani). This chain links directly to Imam Muhammad.
This isnad gives his fatwa authority.

Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
Index of Notables: al-Sidq? He was trustworthy, a memorizer, a master of the reciters, abundant in reverence. He heard from Lady Aisha, Abu Huraira, Ibn Abbas, Jabir, and others, may Allah be pleased with them - and he died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year one hundred and thirty. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz: 1/127, and Shadharat al-Dhahab: 1/22-177)
Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salamah Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi al-Azdi, a great distinguished imam, famous in the regions, his beautiful mention fills the pages of books. He was born in the year twenty-nine, and it is said: in the year thirty and two hundred, and died in the year twenty-one and three hundred. He used to read to al-Muzani al-Shafi'i, who was his maternal uncle, and al-Tahawi would frequently study the books of Abu Hanifa. So al-Muzani said to him: "By Allah, nothing will come from you." So he became angry and left him. He then studied the fiqh of Abu Hanifa and became an imam. When he taught or answered something from the difficult issues, he would say: "May Allah have mercy on my uncle; if he were alive, he would have to expiate for his oath." Al-Tahawi took fiqh from Abu Ja'far Ahmad, then went to Syria where he met Abu Khazim 'Abd al-Hamid, the Chief Judge of Syria, and took from him from 'Isa ibn Aban from Muhammad. He was an imam in hadith and reports.
He has distinguished, esteemed works, including: 'Ahkam al-Qur'an', 'Kitab Ma'ani al-Athar', 'Mushkil al-Athar', 'al-Mukhtasar', 'Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir', 'Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir', 'Kitab al-Shurut al-Kabir wa al-Saghir wa al-Awsat wa al-Mahadir wa al-Sijillat wa al-Wasaya wa al-Fara'id', 'Kitab Manaqib Abi Hanifah', 'Tarikh Kabir', and 'al-Nawadir al-Fiqhiyyah'.
(Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah: 41-42)
- Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas: Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Muradi, al-Misri al-Nahwi. He was considered like Ibn al-Anbari and Niftawayh. He had many works, and he was frugal with himself in his clothing and food. He died drowned in Egypt in Dhu al-Hijjah of the year 338 AH. Al-Suyuti said in Husn al-Muhadara: "He learned from al-Akhfash al-Saghir and others, and narrated hadith from al-Nasa'i." Among his works: 'Tafsir al-Qur'an', 'al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh', and 'Sharh Abiyat Sibawayh' and 'Sharh al-Mu'allaqat'. He drowned under the measure and it was not known where he went.
(Shadharat al-Dhahab: 2/346)
-9 Abu Hatim al-Qazwini: He is Abu Hatim Mahmud ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ikrimah ibn Malik al-Ansari, al-Tabari, from the city of Amil Tabaristan, the Shafi'i jurist famous as al-Qazwini, died in Amil in the year 460 AH, sixty and four hundred, and it is said: the year forty-four. The author of 'Uqd al-Madhhab' said: He has many works in usul and khilaf, including: 'Tajrid al-Tajrid' and 'Kitab al-Hiyal'. (Hadiyyat al-Arifin: 6/402)
-10 Abu Hamid al-Marwazi: Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali Abu Hamid al-Faqih al-Marwazi. Al-Hakim and al-Khatib narrated that he was a jurist, knowledgeable in usul and furu'. He learned in Baghdad from Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and reports from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar from Nasir ibn Yahya from Muhammad ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf. He was a memorizer of hadith, insightful in tafsir. He wrote much and has a wonderful history. He came to Baghdad and studied, then returned to Khurasan and assumed the office of Chief Judge. Al-Jami' said: Ibn al-Athir recorded in al-Kamil his death in the year 376 AH, saying in its goodness: In it died Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali Abu Hamid al-Marwazi, known as Ibn al-Tabari, the Hanafi jurist; he studied in Baghdad with Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and served as Chief Judge in Khurasan, died in Safar, and was a devout worshiper, a muhaddith, trustworthy. (Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah: p. 24)
-11 Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya: 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari, titled 'Imad al-Din, known as al-Kiya al-Harrasi. A Shafi'i jurist, exegete, born in Tabaristan and settled in Baghdad, taught at the Nizamiyya, and preached. He memorized the ahadith of ahkam and debated on them. He is the one who said: "When the knights of hadith gallop in the fields of combat, the heads of analogies fly in the winds." He died in the year 504 AH. His works include: 'Ahkam al-Qur'an', 'Shifa' al-Mustarshidin', and 'Naqd Mufradat al-Imam Ahmad'. (Hadiyyat al-Arifin: 5/694, Shadharat al-Dhahab: 4/8,9)
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index from 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi. It lists the lives of key scholars whose works and teachings are relevant to the field of fatwa. The first entry, though unclear, describes an early pious figure who learned from major Companions. The second, Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, is a giant of the Hanafi school. His story with al-Muzani shows how conflict can lead to fruitful scholarship. Al-Tahawi’s many works, like 'Mushkil al-Athar' and 'Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir', are foundational. Next, Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas is a grammarian and exegete. Then Abu Hatim al-Qazwini, a Shafi'i usuli. Abu Hamid al-Marwazi represents the Hanafi chain through al-Karkhi and Abu Yusuf. Finally, Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya, a Shafi'i jurist known for his strong defense of hadith against blind analogy. These biographies underscore that a mufti must know the scholarly lineage to evaluate the reliability of transmitted rulings.

Key Terms
أبو جعفر الطحاوي (Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi): A great Hanafi jurist and hadith scholar, author of many key works like 'Mushkil al-Athar' and 'Mukhtasar', died 321 AH.

Scholarly Lineages in Adab al-Fatwa: From al-Nahhas to al-Kiya
Biographies of al-Nahhas, al-Qazwini, al-Marwazi, al-Kiya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the chains of transmission (isnad) of the Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars listed, and evaluate how knowledge of scholarly lineage strengthens fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Knowing a scholar's teachers and works helps a mufti assess the authority and scope of their rulings.

This lesson examines four more scholars from the biographical index: Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas (grammarian and exegete), Abu Hatim al-Qazwini (Shafi'i usuli), Abu Hamid al-Marwazi (Hanafi chief judge), and Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya (Shafi'i hadith advocate). By parsing their biographies, you learn how a mufti uses scholarly lineage to verify the transmission of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars and their madhhab
From the entries, note who is Hanafi (Abu Hamid al-Marwazi) and who is Shafi'i (the others).
Al-Nahhas is a grammarian but his works on tafsir are used across madhahib.
2
Trace the Hanafi chain of Abu Hamid al-Marwazi
Abu Hamid learned from Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, then from al-Saffar, from Nasir ibn Yahya, from Muhammad ibn Sama'ah, from Abu Yusuf. This chain connects to the founding imams.
This chain is similar to al-Tahawi's but through a different route.
3
Understand the Shafi'i emphasis of al-Kiya
Al-Kiya famously prioritized hadith over qiyas. His quote about 'knights of hadith' shows the Shafi'i methodological stance.
A mufti must recognize such positions to weigh evidence in inter-madhhab issues.
4
List the key works of each scholar
Identify works like al-Nahhas's 'al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh', al-Qazwini's 'Tajrid al-Tajrid', al-Marwazi's 'Tarikh', and al-Kiya's 'Ahkam al-Qur'an'.
These works are reference tools for fatwa.

-٩ أبو حاتم القزويني : هو أبو حاتم محمود بن الحسن بن محمد بن يوسف ابن الحسن بن محمد بن عكرمة بن مالك الأنصاري، الطبري، من مدينة آمل طبرستان الفقه الشافعي الشهير بالقزويني، المتوفى بآمل سنة ٤٦٠ هـ ستين وأربع مائة وقيل : سنة أربع وأربعين. قال صاحب عقد المذهب : له تصانيف كثيرة في الأصول والخلاف فمنها : تجريد التجريد وكتاب الحيل . (هدية العارفين: ٤٠٢/٦)
،
١٠ أبو حامد المروزى : أحمد بن الحسن بن على أبو حامد الفقيه المروزي . روى عن الحاكم والخطيب : أنه كان فقيها، عارفا بالأصول والفروع، أخذ ببغداد عن أبي الحسن الكرخي ويبلغ عن أبي القاسم الصفار عن نصير بن يحيى عن محمد ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف وكان حافظاً للحديث، بصيراً بالتفسير . صنف الكثير وله تاريخ بديع ورد بغداد وتفقه ثم عاد إلى خراسان فتولى قضاء القضاة . قال الجامع : أرّخ ابن الأثير في الكامل وفاته سنة ست وسبعين وثلاثمائة حيث قال في جوادتها : فيها توفى أحمد بن الحسن بن على أبو حامد المروزي ويعرف بـ ابن الطبرى"، "الفقيه الحنفى، تفقه ببغداد على أبي الحسن الكرخي وولى قضاء القضاة بخراسان ومات فى صفر وكان عابداً ، محدثًا ، ثقة (الفوائد البهية : ص ٢٤)
-١١ أبو الحسن الكيا : على بن محمد بن على أبو الحسن الطبري، الملقب
،
بعماد الدين المعروف بالكيا الهراسى. فقیه ،شافعی ،مفسر، ولد في طبرستان وسكن بغداد فدرس بالنظامية، ووعظ . كان يحفظ أحاديث الأحكام ويناظر فيها، وهو القائل: "إذا جالت فرسان الأحاديث في ميادين الكفاح، طارت رؤوس المقاييس في مهاب الرياح" : توفى سنة ٥٠٤هـ . من تصانيفه: أحكام القرآن" و "شفاء المسترشدين"
و نقد مفردات الإمام أحمد " . (هدية العارفين : ٦٩٤/٥ ، شذرات الذهب : ٨/٤، ٩)
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
Index of Notables: al-Sidq? He was trustworthy, a memorizer, a master of the reciters, abundant in reverence. He heard from Lady Aisha, Abu Huraira, Ibn Abbas, Jabir, and others, may Allah be pleased with them - and he died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year one hundred and thirty. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz: 1/127, and Shadharat al-Dhahab: 1/22-177)
Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salamah Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi al-Azdi, a great distinguished imam, famous in the regions, his beautiful mention fills the pages of books. He was born in the year twenty-nine, and it is said: in the year thirty and two hundred, and died in the year twenty-one and three hundred. He used to read to al-Muzani al-Shafi'i, who was his maternal uncle, and al-Tahawi would frequently study the books of Abu Hanifa. So al-Muzani said to him: "By Allah, nothing will come from you." So he became angry and left him. He then studied the fiqh of Abu Hanifa and became an imam. When he taught or answered something from the difficult issues, he would say: "May Allah have mercy on my uncle; if he were alive, he would have to expiate for his oath." Al-Tahawi took fiqh from Abu Ja'far Ahmad, then went to Syria where he met Abu Khazim 'Abd al-Hamid, the Chief Judge of Syria, and took from him from 'Isa ibn Aban from Muhammad. He was an imam in hadith and reports.
He has distinguished, esteemed works, including: 'Ahkam al-Qur'an', 'Kitab Ma'ani al-Athar', 'Mushkil al-Athar', 'al-Mukhtasar', 'Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir', 'Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir', 'Kitab al-Shurut al-Kabir wa al-Saghir wa al-Awsat wa al-Mahadir wa al-Sijillat wa al-Wasaya wa al-Fara'id', 'Kitab Manaqib Abi Hanifah', 'Tarikh Kabir', and 'al-Nawadir al-Fiqhiyyah'.
(Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah: 41-42)
- Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas: Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Muradi, al-Misri al-Nahwi. He was considered like Ibn al-Anbari and Niftawayh. He had many works, and he was frugal with himself in his clothing and food. He died drowned in Egypt in Dhu al-Hijjah of the year 338 AH. Al-Suyuti said in Husn al-Muhadara: "He learned from al-Akhfash al-Saghir and others, and narrated hadith from al-Nasa'i." Among his works: 'Tafsir al-Qur'an', 'al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh', and 'Sharh Abiyat Sibawayh' and 'Sharh al-Mu'allaqat'. He drowned under the measure and it was not known where he went.
(Shadharat al-Dhahab: 2/346)
-9 Abu Hatim al-Qazwini: He is Abu Hatim Mahmud ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ikrimah ibn Malik al-Ansari, al-Tabari, from the city of Amil Tabaristan, the Shafi'i jurist famous as al-Qazwini, died in Amil in the year 460 AH, sixty and four hundred, and it is said: the year forty-four. The author of 'Uqd al-Madhhab' said: He has many works in usul and khilaf, including: 'Tajrid al-Tajrid' and 'Kitab al-Hiyal'. (Hadiyyat al-Arifin: 6/402)
-10 Abu Hamid al-Marwazi: Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali Abu Hamid al-Faqih al-Marwazi. Al-Hakim and al-Khatib narrated that he was a jurist, knowledgeable in usul and furu'. He learned in Baghdad from Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and reports from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar from Nasir ibn Yahya from Muhammad ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf. He was a memorizer of hadith, insightful in tafsir. He wrote much and has a wonderful history. He came to Baghdad and studied, then returned to Khurasan and assumed the office of Chief Judge. Al-Jami' said: Ibn al-Athir recorded in al-Kamil his death in the year 376 AH, saying in its goodness: In it died Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali Abu Hamid al-Marwazi, known as Ibn al-Tabari, the Hanafi jurist; he studied in Baghdad with Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and served as Chief Judge in Khurasan, died in Safar, and was a devout worshiper, a muhaddith, trustworthy. (Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah: p. 24)
-11 Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya: 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari, titled 'Imad al-Din, known as al-Kiya al-Harrasi. A Shafi'i jurist, exegete, born in Tabaristan and settled in Baghdad, taught at the Nizamiyya, and preached. He memorized the ahadith of ahkam and debated on them. He is the one who said: "When the knights of hadith gallop in the fields of combat, the heads of analogies fly in the winds." He died in the year 504 AH. His works include: 'Ahkam al-Qur'an', 'Shifa' al-Mustarshidin', and 'Naqd Mufradat al-Imam Ahmad'. (Hadiyyat al-Arifin: 5/694, Shadharat al-Dhahab: 4/8,9)
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index from 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi. It lists the lives of key scholars whose works and teachings are relevant to the field of fatwa. The first entry, though unclear, describes an early pious figure who learned from major Companions. The second, Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, is a giant of the Hanafi school. His story with al-Muzani shows how conflict can lead to fruitful scholarship. Al-Tahawi’s many works, like 'Mushkil al-Athar' and 'Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir', are foundational. Next, Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas is a grammarian and exegete. Then Abu Hatim al-Qazwini, a Shafi'i usuli. Abu Hamid al-Marwazi represents the Hanafi chain through al-Karkhi and Abu Yusuf. Finally, Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya, a Shafi'i jurist known for his strong defense of hadith against blind analogy. These biographies underscore that a mufti must know the scholarly lineage to evaluate the reliability of transmitted rulings.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الكيا (Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya): A Shafi'i jurist and exegete, known as al-Kiya al-Harrasi, died 504 AH, famous for his emphasis on hadith over qiyas.
أبو حامد المروزي (Abu Hamid al-Marwazi): A Hanafi jurist and judge, student of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, author of a history and other works, died 376 AH.
أبو جعفر النحاس (Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas): An Egyptian grammarian and Quran exegete, known for works on naskh and tafsir, died 338 AH.
أبو حاتم القزويني (Abu Hatim al-Qazwini): A Shafi'i usuli jurist, author of works on legal theory and legal stratagems, died 460 AH.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which scholar's death is described as drowning?

C) Abu Ja'far al-Nahhas
D) Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya

Key Takeaway
A mufti's knowledge of scholarly lineages and madhhab affiliations ensures that rulings are correctly attributed and applied.

Life of the Author

Reading a Hanafi Biographical Index: Scholars 9–14
Biographical index of six scholars from a Hanafi usul al-iftaa work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key biographical details of Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars cited in usul al-iftaa texts and explain their relevance to fatwa methodology.

Core Idea
Biographical indexes anchor fatwa authority – knowing a scholar's madhhab, chain, and works is essential.

This lesson introduces you to the Fihris al-A'lam, an index of notable scholars found in classical Hanafi works on mufti methodology. The six entries here include both Hanafi and Shafi'i jurists, reflecting the cross-madhhab engagement central to usul al-iftaa. By learning to parse these entries, you will understand how biographical information establishes scholarly authority and informs the selection of relied-upon positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Note the full name, kunya, nisba, and madhhab (if mentioned). For example, Abu Hatim al-Qazwini is identified as Shafi'i.
The nisba often indicates origin, e.g., al-Marwazi from Marw.
2
Extract Key Life Dates
Look for birth and death years, teachers, and students. This helps place the scholar in a tabaqa (generation).
Death dates are given in AH; e.g., Abu Hanifa died 150 AH.
3
Note Scholarly Assessments
Quotes from other scholars (e.g., al-'Ijli, Ibn 'Uyayna) indicate reliability, piety, and expertise.
These assessments are crucial for evaluating the weight of the scholar's opinions.
4
List Major Works
Works in usul, ikhtilaf, tafsir, or hadith are often listed. For example, al-Kiya wrote Ahkam al-Qur'an.
Works relevant to fatwa methodology are especially important.
5
Determine Relevance to Usul al-Iftaa
Reflect on why the author included this scholar. Does the scholar represent a key authority, a transmitter, or a mujtahid?
The index supports cross-referencing in the main text.

فهرس الأعلام آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى ١٢ أبو الحصين : هو عثمان بن عاصم بن حصين أبو الحصين الأسدى الكوفى، قال العجلى : كان شيخًا عاليًا صاحب سنة، كوفيا، عثمانيا، ثقة، ثبتا في الحديث، وقال ابن عيينة : "كان ابن حصين إذا سئل عن مسألة قال : ليس لى بها علم والله أعلم . توفى رحمه الله سنة سبع وعشرين ومائة ، وقيل : غير ذلك .
(تهذيب التهذيب : ٤٩٠/٥)
١٣ أبو حنيفة : هو الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، صاحب المذهب الحنفى، وأحد الأئمة الأربعة المتبوعين، قال ابن حجر : قال بعض الأئمة : لم يظهر لأحد من أئمة الإسلام المشهورين مثل ما ظهر لأبي حنيفة من الأصحاب والتلاميذ، ولم ينتفع العلماء وجميع الناس بمثل ما انتفعوا به وبأصحابه " . قال أحمد بن حنبل في حقه : "إنه كان من العلم والورع والزهد وإيثار الآخرة بمحل لا يدركه أحد . قال عبد الله بن المبارك: "ليس أحد أحق من أن يقتدى به من أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه كان إماماً تقيا ،نقيّا، ورعًا، عالما، فقيها . قال الثورى لمن قال جئت من أبى حنيفة: "لقد جئت من عند أعبد أهل الأرض" . قال النووي: "كان رحمه الله إماما في ذلك (أى في الحديث) فإنه رضى الله عنه أخذ الحديث عن أربعة آلاف شيخ من أئمة التابعين وغيرهم". قال الشافعي: "الناس" فى الفقه عيال على أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى " . له في علم الكلام كتاب الفقه الأكبر" وفي الحديث "المسند" ولد سنة ٨٠هـ وتوفي رحمه الله رحمة واسعة سنة ١٥٠هـ . Index of Notable Figures. 106. Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. [Line about drowned under the scale?]. (Shadharat al-Dhahab 2:346). 9. Abu Hatim al-Qazwini: He is Abu Hatim Mahmud ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Ikrima ibn Malik al-Ansari, al-Tabari, from the city of Amul Tabaristan, the famous Shafi'i jurist known as al-Qazwini, died in Amul in the year 460 AH or 444 AH. The author of 'Uqd al-Madhhab said: He has many works in usul and ikhtilaf, including Tajrid al-Tajrid and Kitab al-Hiyal. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 6:402). 10. Abu Hamid al-Marwazi: Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali Abu Hamid al-Marwazi al-Faqih. Narrated from al-Hakim and al-Khatib that he was a jurist, knowledgeable in usul and furu', studied in Baghdad with Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and traced to Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar from Nasir ibn Yahya from Muhammad ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf. He was a memorizer of hadith, skilled in tafsir. He authored many works and had a remarkable history. He came to Baghdad, studied fiqh, then returned to Khurasan and became chief judge. Al-Jami' said: Ibn al-Athir recorded his death in al-Kamil in the year 376 AH. He died in Safar, was a worshiper, a muhaddith, trustworthy. (Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p.24). 11. Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya: 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari, titled 'Imad al-Din, known as al-Kiya al-Harrasi. A jurist, Shafi'i, mufassir, born in Tabaristan, resided in Baghdad, taught at the Nizamiyya, and preached. He memorized hadiths of rulings and debated, saying: 'When the steeds of hadith gallop in the fields of combat, the heads of analogies fly in the winds of winds.' Died 504 AH. Works: Ahkam al-Qur'an, Shifa' al-Mustarshidin, Naqd Mufradat al-Imam Ahmad. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 5:694, Shadharat al-Dhahab 4:8,9). 107. Index of Notable Figures. Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. 12. Abu al-Husayn: He is 'Uthman ibn 'Asim ibn Husayn Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi al-Kufi. Al-'Ijli said: He was an elder, high-ranking, adherent to sunna, Kufan, 'Uthmani, trustworthy, reliable in hadith. Ibn 'Uyayna said: 'When Ibn Husayn was asked about a matter, he would say: I have no knowledge of it, and Allah knows best.' He died in 127 AH or otherwise. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 5:490). 13. Abu Hanifa: He is the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, founder of the Hanafi school, one of the four followed imams. Ibn Hajar said: Some imams said: No one among the famous imams of Islam had as many companions and students as Abu Hanifa, and scholars and all people benefited from him and his companions as they did from none other. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said about him: 'He possessed knowledge, piety, asceticism, and preference for the Hereafter to a degree that no one else attained.' 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'No one is more deserving to be followed than Abu Hanifa; for he was an imam, pious, pure, scrupulous, knowledgeable, and a jurist.' Al-Thawri said to one who said 'I came from Abu Hanifa': 'You have come from the most worshipful person on earth.' Al-Nawawi said: 'He was an imam in that (i.e., hadith), for he took hadith from four thousand teachers among the leading tabi'un and others.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'People are dependent on Abu Hanifa in fiqh.' He wrote al-Fiqh al-Akbar in theology and al-Musnad in hadith. He was born in 80 AH and died in 150 AH. (Summarized from Radd al-Muhtar 1:55-56, Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 6:525). 14. Abu al-'Abbas ibn Surayj: The imam, eminent scholar, Shaykh al-Islam, judge Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn 'Umar ibn Surayj al-Baghdadi, the leader of the Shafi'is. He heard from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Za'farani, 'Ali ibn Ashkab, 'Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Duri, al-Ramadi, Abu Dawud al-Sijistani, and their peers. I saw for him a work in which he argued with hadith and approached it in a manner of one who understands this field.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index from a Hanafi usul al-iftaa work, listing scholars from the 9th to the 14th entry. It includes both Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars, providing essential details about their lives, teachers, works, and contributions. The entries serve as a reference for students of fatwa methodology to recognize the authorities cited in the text. The inclusion of scholars like Abu Hanifa underscores the centrality of the Hanafi school, while others like Abu al-Hasan al-Kiya and Abu al-'Abbas ibn Surayj represent Shafi'i scholarship, reflecting the inter-madhhab engagement in usul al-iftaa.

Key Terms
فهرس الأعلام (Fihris al-A'lam): Index of notable figures; a list of biographical entries for scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biography of Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi
Biographical entry of Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi and explain his significance in hadith transmission.

Core Idea
Reliability in hadith is essential for fatwa; Abu al-Husayn was a thiqah, an exemplar of caution in knowledge.

This lesson introduces you to Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi, a Kufan scholar known for his piety and caution in verdicts. Understanding his biography helps you appreciate the chain of transmission that underpins Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Read the name and lineage: Abu al-Husayn is 'Uthman ibn 'Asim ibn Husayn al-Asadi al-Kufi. This establishes his identity and origin.
The nisbah 'al-Asadi' indicates tribal affiliation.
2
Note character and reliability
Al-Ajli describes him as a high-ranking shaykh, a man of sunnah, thiqah (trustworthy), and thabit (reliable) in hadith. This makes his narrations acceptable.
Thiqah is a key term in hadith criticism.
3
Understand his cautious attitude
Ibn 'Uyaynah reports that when asked a question, Abu al-Husayn would say 'I have no knowledge of it'—a model of scholarly caution.
Adab al-fatwa requires a mufti to refrain from speaking without knowledge.
4
Record his death date
He died in 127 AH. This provides a chronological anchor.
Multiple dates may exist; the standard is 127 AH.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهرس الأعلام آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى ١٢ أبو الحصين : هو عثمان بن عاصم بن حصين أبو الحصين الأسدى الكوفى، قال العجلى : كان شيخًا عاليًا صاحب سنة، كوفيا، عثمانيا، ثقة، ثبتا في الحديث، وقال ابن عيينة : "كان ابن حصين إذا سئل عن مسألة قال : ليس لى بها علم والله أعلم . توفى رحمه الله سنة سبع وعشرين ومائة ، وقيل : غير ذلك . (تهذيب التهذيب : ٤٩٠/٥) ١٣ أبو حنيفة : هو الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، صاحب المذهب الحنفى، وأحد الأئمة الأربعة المتبوعين، قال ابن حجر : قال بعض الأئمة : لم يظهر لأحد من أئمة الإسلام المشهورين مثل ما ظهر لأبي حنيفة من الأصحاب والتلاميذ، ولم ينتفع العلماء وجميع الناس بمثل ما انتفعوا به وبأصحابه " . قال أحمد بن حنبل في حقه : "إنه كان من العلم والورع والزهد وإيثار الآخرة بمحل لا يدركه أحد . قال عبد الله بن المبارك: "ليس أحد أحق من أن يقتدى به من أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه كان إماماً تقيا ،نقيّا، ورعًا، عالما، فقيها . قال الثورى لمن قال جئت من أبى حنيفة: "لقد جئت من عند أعبد أهل الأرض" . قال النووي: "كان رحمه الله إماما في ذلك (أى في الحديث) فإنه رضى الله عنه أخذ الحديث عن أربعة آلاف شيخ من أئمة التابعين وغيرهم". قال الشافعي: "الناس" فى الفقه عيال على أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى " . له في علم الكلام كتاب الفقه الأكبر" وفي الحديث "المسند" ولد سنة ٨٠هـ وتوفي رحمه الله رحمة واسعة سنة ١٥٠هـ . (ملخصاً من رد المحتار: ٥٦،٥٥/١ ، وسير أعلام النبلاء : ٥٢٥/٦) ١٤ - أبو العباس بن سريج : الإمام العلامة شيخ الإسلام القاضي أبو العباس أحمد بن عمر بن سريج البغدادى قدوة الشافعية، سمع الحسن بن محمد الزعفراني، وعلى بن أشكاب، وعباس بن محمد الدورى والرمادي، وأبا داود السجستاني وطبقتهم . رأيت له فيه تصنيفا يحتج فيه بالأحاديث ويطرقها عمل من يفهم هذا الشأن ، وأما الفقه فهو حامل لواءه وعلم نظراءه، تصدر للاشتغال وتفقه به أئمة أعلام، وحدث عنه أبو القاسم الطبراني وأبو أحمد الغطريفى وأبو الوليد حسان بن محمد وآخرون . وقال أبو الوليد الفقيه يقول : سمعت ابن سريج يقول: ما رأيت من المتفقه من اشتغل بالكلام فأفلح ، يفوته الفقه ولا يصل إلى مــعــرفــة الكلام. وقد كان أبو العباس ابن سريج صاحب سنة واتباع، بلغني أنه سئل عن صفات الله تعالى فقال : حرام على العقول أن تمثل الله وعلى الأوهام أن تحده وعلى الألباب أن تصف إلا ما وصف به نفسه في كتابه أو على لسان رسوله . مات في جمادى الأولى سنة ست وثلاث مائة وله سبع و خمسون سنة ونصف . (تذکرة الحفاظ : ۸۱۱/۳، ۸۱۲) ١٥ - أبو عبد الله الحليمي : أبو عبد الله الحسين بن الحسن بن محمد ابن حليم المعروف بـ الحليمي " ، قال فيه الحاكم كان شيخ الشافعيين بما وراء النهر وأدبهم وأنظرهم بعد أستاذيه "القفال الشاشى" و "الأدنى"، وقال في النهاية : "كان الحليمي عظيم ،القدر، لا يحيط بكنه علمه إلا غواص". ولد ببخارى وقيل بجرجان سنة ثمان وثلاثين وثلاثمائة ومات سنة ثلاث وأربعمائة ، قيل : في جمادى وقيل : في ربيع الأول. ومن مصنفاته : "شعب الإيمان " : كتاب جليل جمع أحكاماً كثيرة ومعانى غريبة لم أظفر بكثير منها في غيره . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٤٠٤/١) ١٦ - أبو على السنجى : الشيخ أبو على الحسين بن شعيب المروزي السنجی، إمام زمانه في الفقه، تفقه على القفال وكان أجل أصحابه وأخذ أيضا عن الشيخ أبي حامد وشرح "المختصر شرحاً مطولا يُسمّيه إمام الحرمين بـ "المذهب الكبير " وشرحا أيضا " التلخيص " و "فروع ابن الحداد" وهما في غاية النفاسة والتحقيق، وهو أول من جمع في تصانيفه بين طريقة العراقيين والخراسانيين. توفى سنة سبع وعشرين وأربعمائة كذا قاله الرافعى في التدوين وقيل : سنة ثلاثين وقيل : نيف وثلاثين وجزم به ابن
Index of Notables: Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
12. Abu al-Husayn: He is Uthman ibn Asim ibn Husayn Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi al-Kufi. Al-Ijli said: He was a high-ranking shaykh, a man of sunnah, Kufan, Uthmani, trustworthy, reliable in hadith. Ibn Uyaynah said: 'When Ibn Husayn was asked about a matter, he said: I have no knowledge of it, and Allah knows best.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 127 AH, and it is also said otherwise. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 5:490)
13. Abu Hanifa: He is the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, founder of the Hanafi school, and one of the four followed imams. Ibn Hajar said: Some imams said: There has not appeared for any of the famous imams of Islam what has appeared for Abu Hanifa in terms of companions and students, and scholars and all people have not benefited as they have benefited from him and his companions. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said about him: 'He was in knowledge, piety, asceticism, and preferring the Hereafter at a level no one can reach.' Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'No one is more deserving of being followed than Abu Hanifa, because he was a pious, pure, devout, knowledgeable, and profound imam.' Al-Thawri said to someone who said 'I came from Abu Hanifa': 'You have come from the most worshipful person on earth.' Al-Nawawi said: 'He was an imam in that (meaning hadith), for he, may Allah be pleased with him, took hadith from four thousand shaykhs from the leading tabi'un and others.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'People in fiqh are dependent on Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' He authored in theology the book 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' and in hadith 'al-Musnad'. He was born in 80 AH and died, may Allah have mercy on him with abundant mercy, in 150 AH. (Summarized from Radd al-Muhtar 1:55-56, and Siyar A'lam al-Nubala 6:525)
14. Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj: The Imam, the scholar, Shaykh al-Islam, Judge Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Surayj al-Baghdadi, the role model of the Shafi'is. He heard from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Za'farani, Ali ibn Ashkab, Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Duri, al-Ramadi, Abu Dawud al-Sijistani and their class. I saw for him in it a composition in which he argued with hadith and analyzed them in the manner of one who understands this discipline. As for fiqh, he is its standard-bearer and the most learned of his peers. He assumed the position of teaching and leading imams studied under him. Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani, Abu Ahmad al-Ghitrifi, and Abu al-Walid Hassan ibn Muhammad and others narrated from him. Abu al-Walid al-Faqih said: I heard Ibn Surayj say: 'I have never seen a student of fiqh who engaged in theology and succeeded. He misses out on fiqh and does not attain knowledge of theology.' He was a man of sunnah and following. It reached me that he was asked about Allah's attributes, and he said: 'It is forbidden for intellects to depict Allah, for imaginations to limit Him, and for minds to describe Him except as He described Himself in His Book or on the tongue of His Messenger.' He died in Jumada al-Ula in the year 306 AH at the age of fifty-seven and a half. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 3:811-812)
15. Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi: Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Halim, known as al-Halimi. Al-Hakim said: He was the shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana, their most refined and the most insightful after his two teachers al-Qaffal al-Shashi and al-Adhani. In al-Nihayah, he said: 'Al-Halimi was of great stature; no one can encompass the depth of his knowledge except a diver.' He was born in Bukhara, and it is said in Jurjan, in 338 AH and died in 403 AH, it is said in Jumada or Rabi' al-Awwal. Among his works is 'Shu'ab al-Iman': a great book that collects many rulings and unique meanings, much of which I have not found in other works. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 1:404)
16. Abu Ali al-Sanji: Shaykh Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji, the imam of his time in fiqh. He studied fiqh under al-Qaffal and was the most prominent of his companions. He also studied under Shaykh Abu Hamid. He wrote a lengthy commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' which Imam al-Haramayn called 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir'. He also wrote commentaries on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad', both of which are extremely valuable and thorough. He was the first to combine in his works the method of the Iraqis and the Khurasanis. He died in 427 AH as stated by al-Rafi'i in al-Tadwin, and it is said 430 or around 431, and Ibn is certain of it.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is from the biographical index (fihris) of 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi, included in this work on Hanafi ifta' usul. It provides brief biographies of five key scholars who are referenced in the text. The first entry, Abu al-Husayn, is a trustworthy hadith transmitter. The second is the great Imam Abu Hanifa, whose virtues are extolled with quotes from Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Thawri, al-Nawawi, and al-Shafi'i. This establishes his authority in both fiqh and hadith. The third, Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj, was a leading Shafi'i scholar who warned against preoccupation with theology (kalam) at the expense of fiqh. The fourth, Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi, was a Shafi'i scholar in Transoxiana, author of 'Shu'ab al-Iman'. The fifth, Abu Ali al-Sanji, was the first to combine the Iraqi and Khurasani methods in his fiqh writings. These biographies serve to authenticate the sources and personalities cited in the fatwa methodology text.

Key Terms
ثقة (thiqah): A hadith transmitter who is reliable and trustworthy.
إمام (imam): A leading scholar in Islamic jurisprudence, followed by others.
قدوة (qudwah): A role model or exemplar to be followed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Abu al-Husayn do when asked a question he did not know?
A) He gave a speculative answer
B) He said 'I have no knowledge of it'
C) He remained silent
D) He referred to another scholar

Key Takeaway
A mufti must admit ignorance when lacking knowledge, following the caution of early scholars like Abu al-Husayn.

Life of the Author

The Stature of Imam Abu Hanifa
Biographical entry of Imam Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to summarise the key testimony from other imams about Abu Hanifa's knowledge, piety, and influence.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa is a matchless imam in fiqh and hadith; all later scholarship is indebted to him.

This lesson presents the glowing endorsements of Imam Abu Hanifa from major figures like Ahmad ibn Hanbal, al-Shafi'i, and al-Thawri. These testimonies establish his unparalleled authority as a mujtahid and exemplar for muftis.

Guided Path
1
Read the testimonies
The passage quotes five specific endorsements: Ibn Hajar's general praise, Ahmad's emphasis on his knowledge and piety, Ibn al-Mubarak's call to follow him, al-Thawri's comment on his worship, and al-Shafi'i's statement that all are dependent on him.
Each testimony highlights a different virtue.
2
Identify the common theme
All testimonies agree on Abu Hanifa's unmatched combination of profound knowledge (fiqh and hadith) and deep piety (zuhd, wara').
This dual excellence makes him a complete imam.
3
Note his contributions
Abu Hanifa authored 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' (theology) and 'al-Musnad' (hadith). He had thousands of teachers and students.
His works are foundational for Hanafi creed and law.
4
Record his lifespan
Born 80 AH, died 150 AH. This places him in the generation of the tabi'un and early tab' tabi'in.
He lived through the late Umayyad and early Abbasid periods.

(طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٤٠٤/١) ١٦ - أبو على السنجى : الشيخ أبو على الحسين بن شعيب المروزي السنجی، إمام زمانه في الفقه، تفقه على القفال وكان أجل أصحابه وأخذ أيضا عن الشيخ أبي حامد وشرح "المختصر شرحاً مطولا يُسمّيه إمام الحرمين بـ "المذهب الكبير " وشرحا أيضا " التلخيص " و "فروع ابن الحداد" وهما في غاية النفاسة والتحقيق، وهو أول من جمع في تصانيفه بين طريقة العراقيين والخراسانيين. توفى سنة سبع وعشرين وأربعمائة كذا قاله الرافعى في التدوين وقيل : سنة ثلاثين وقيل : نيف وثلاثين وجزم به ابن
Index of Notables: Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
12. Abu al-Husayn: He is Uthman ibn Asim ibn Husayn Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi al-Kufi. Al-Ijli said: He was a high-ranking shaykh, a man of sunnah, Kufan, Uthmani, trustworthy, reliable in hadith. Ibn Uyaynah said: 'When Ibn Husayn was asked about a matter, he said: I have no knowledge of it, and Allah knows best.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 127 AH, and it is also said otherwise. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 5:490)
13. Abu Hanifa: He is the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, founder of the Hanafi school, and one of the four followed imams. Ibn Hajar said: Some imams said: There has not appeared for any of the famous imams of Islam what has appeared for Abu Hanifa in terms of companions and students, and scholars and all people have not benefited as they have benefited from him and his companions. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said about him: 'He was in knowledge, piety, asceticism, and preferring the Hereafter at a level no one can reach.' Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'No one is more deserving of being followed than Abu Hanifa, because he was a pious, pure, devout, knowledgeable, and profound imam.' Al-Thawri said to someone who said 'I came from Abu Hanifa': 'You have come from the most worshipful person on earth.' Al-Nawawi said: 'He was an imam in that (meaning hadith), for he, may Allah be pleased with him, took hadith from four thousand shaykhs from the leading tabi'un and others.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'People in fiqh are dependent on Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' He authored in theology the book 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' and in hadith 'al-Musnad'. He was born in 80 AH and died, may Allah have mercy on him with abundant mercy, in 150 AH. (Summarized from Radd al-Muhtar 1:55-56, and Siyar A'lam al-Nubala 6:525)
14. Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj: The Imam, the scholar, Shaykh al-Islam, Judge Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Surayj al-Baghdadi, the role model of the Shafi'is. He heard from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Za'farani, Ali ibn Ashkab, Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Duri, al-Ramadi, Abu Dawud al-Sijistani and their class. I saw for him in it a composition in which he argued with hadith and analyzed them in the manner of one who understands this discipline. As for fiqh, he is its standard-bearer and the most learned of his peers. He assumed the position of teaching and leading imams studied under him. Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani, Abu Ahmad al-Ghitrifi, and Abu al-Walid Hassan ibn Muhammad and others narrated from him. Abu al-Walid al-Faqih said: I heard Ibn Surayj say: 'I have never seen a student of fiqh who engaged in theology and succeeded. He misses out on fiqh and does not attain knowledge of theology.' He was a man of sunnah and following. It reached me that he was asked about Allah's attributes, and he said: 'It is forbidden for intellects to depict Allah, for imaginations to limit Him, and for minds to describe Him except as He described Himself in His Book or on the tongue of His Messenger.' He died in Jumada al-Ula in the year 306 AH at the age of fifty-seven and a half. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 3:811-812)
15. Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi: Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Halim, known as al-Halimi. Al-Hakim said: He was the shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana, their most refined and the most insightful after his two teachers al-Qaffal al-Shashi and al-Adhani. In al-Nihayah, he said: 'Al-Halimi was of great stature; no one can encompass the depth of his knowledge except a diver.' He was born in Bukhara, and it is said in Jurjan, in 338 AH and died in 403 AH, it is said in Jumada or Rabi' al-Awwal. Among his works is 'Shu'ab al-Iman': a great book that collects many rulings and unique meanings, much of which I have not found in other works. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 1:404)
16. Abu Ali al-Sanji: Shaykh Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji, the imam of his time in fiqh. He studied fiqh under al-Qaffal and was the most prominent of his companions. He also studied under Shaykh Abu Hamid. He wrote a lengthy commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' which Imam al-Haramayn called 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir'. He also wrote commentaries on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad', both of which are extremely valuable and thorough. He was the first to combine in his works the method of the Iraqis and the Khurasanis. He died in 427 AH as stated by al-Rafi'i in al-Tadwin, and it is said 430 or around 431, and Ibn is certain of it.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is from the biographical index (fihris) of 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi, included in this work on Hanafi ifta' usul. It provides brief biographies of five key scholars who are referenced in the text. The first entry, Abu al-Husayn, is a trustworthy hadith transmitter. The second is the great Imam Abu Hanifa, whose virtues are extolled with quotes from Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Thawri, al-Nawawi, and al-Shafi'i. This establishes his authority in both fiqh and hadith. The third, Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj, was a leading Shafi'i scholar who warned against preoccupation with theology (kalam) at the expense of fiqh. The fourth, Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi, was a Shafi'i scholar in Transoxiana, author of 'Shu'ab al-Iman'. The fifth, Abu Ali al-Sanji, was the first to combine the Iraqi and Khurasani methods in his fiqh writings. These biographies serve to authenticate the sources and personalities cited in the fatwa methodology text.

Key Terms
إمام (imam): A leading scholar in Islamic jurisprudence, followed by others.
قدوة (qudwah): A role model or exemplar to be followed.
ورع (wara'): Scrupulous piety; abstaining from the doubtful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many shaykhs did Abu Hanifa study hadith from?
A) 400
B) 4,000
C) 14,000
D) 40,000

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa is the foundation of the Hanafi school, recognized by all for his unmatched knowledge and piety.

Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj: A Shafi'i Luminary
Biographical entry of Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contributions and warnings of Ibn Surayj, especially regarding the study of theology (kalam).

Core Idea
Ibn Surayj, a leading Shafi'i, warned that preoccupation with kalam harms fiqh—a lesson for muftis about prioritising sources.

This lesson focuses on Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj, a towering Shafi'i jurist. His biography includes a sharp warning against theology (kalam) for students of fiqh. This is relevant for Hanafi usul al-ifta, which prioritises textual evidence over speculative theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Ibn Surayj is Ahmad ibn Umar al-Baghdadi, a Shafi'i imam and qadi. He is known as 'Shaykh al-Islam' for his era.
He is a Shafi'i, not Hanafi, but still referenced in this Hanafi text.
2
Note his expertise
He was a master of hadith and fiqh, and his compositions in hadith are praised. He taught many leading scholars.
His hadith competency is highlighted.
3
Understand his warning
Ibn Surayj said: 'I never saw a student of fiqh who engaged in kalam and succeeded. He misses fiqh and does not attain kalam.' This is a critique of mixing theology into legal study.
This advice is often cited in usul al-ifta to caution against speculative reasoning.
4
Record his position on attributes
He upheld the traditional stance: affirm what Allah and the Prophet said about His attributes without tashbih or takyif.
This aligns with Hanafi creedal position.
5
Note his death
Died in 306 AH at age 57.5.
He lived during the height of the Abbasid era.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهرس الأعلام آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى ١٢ أبو الحصين : هو عثمان بن عاصم بن حصين أبو الحصين الأسدى الكوفى، قال العجلى : كان شيخًا عاليًا صاحب سنة، كوفيا، عثمانيا، ثقة، ثبتا في الحديث، وقال ابن عيينة : "كان ابن حصين إذا سئل عن مسألة قال : ليس لى بها علم والله أعلم . توفى رحمه الله سنة سبع وعشرين ومائة ، وقيل : غير ذلك . (تهذيب التهذيب : ٤٩٠/٥) ١٣ أبو حنيفة : هو الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، صاحب المذهب الحنفى، وأحد الأئمة الأربعة المتبوعين، قال ابن حجر : قال بعض الأئمة : لم يظهر لأحد من أئمة الإسلام المشهورين مثل ما ظهر لأبي حنيفة من الأصحاب والتلاميذ، ولم ينتفع العلماء وجميع الناس بمثل ما انتفعوا به وبأصحابه " . قال أحمد بن حنبل في حقه : "إنه كان من العلم والورع والزهد وإيثار الآخرة بمحل لا يدركه أحد . قال عبد الله بن المبارك: "ليس أحد أحق من أن يقتدى به من أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه كان إماماً تقيا ،نقيّا، ورعًا، عالما، فقيها . قال الثورى لمن قال جئت من أبى حنيفة: "لقد جئت من عند أعبد أهل الأرض" . قال النووي: "كان رحمه الله إماما في ذلك (أى في الحديث) فإنه رضى الله عنه أخذ الحديث عن أربعة آلاف شيخ من أئمة التابعين وغيرهم". قال الشافعي: "الناس" فى الفقه عيال على أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى " . له في علم الكلام كتاب الفقه الأكبر" وفي الحديث "المسند" ولد سنة ٨٠هـ وتوفي رحمه الله رحمة واسعة سنة ١٥٠هـ . (ملخصاً من رد المحتار: ٥٦،٥٥/١ ، وسير أعلام النبلاء : ٥٢٥/٦) ١٤ - أبو العباس بن سريج : الإمام العلامة شيخ الإسلام القاضي أبو العباس أحمد بن عمر بن سريج البغدادى قدوة الشافعية، سمع الحسن بن محمد الزعفراني، وعلى بن أشكاب، وعباس بن محمد الدورى والرمادي، وأبا داود السجستاني وطبقتهم . رأيت له فيه تصنيفا يحتج فيه بالأحاديث ويطرقها عمل من يفهم هذا الشأن ، وأما الفقه فهو حامل لواءه وعلم نظراءه، تصدر للاشتغال وتفقه به أئمة أعلام، وحدث عنه أبو القاسم الطبراني وأبو أحمد الغطريفى وأبو الوليد حسان بن محمد وآخرون . وقال أبو الوليد الفقيه يقول : سمعت ابن سريج يقول: ما رأيت من المتفقه من اشتغل بالكلام فأفلح ، يفوته الفقه ولا يصل إلى مــعــرفــة الكلام. وقد كان أبو العباس ابن سريج صاحب سنة واتباع، بلغني أنه سئل عن صفات الله تعالى فقال : حرام على العقول أن تمثل الله وعلى الأوهام أن تحده وعلى الألباب أن تصف إلا ما وصف به نفسه في كتابه أو على لسان رسوله . مات في جمادى الأولى سنة ست وثلاث مائة وله سبع و خمسون سنة ونصف . (تذکرة الحفاظ : ۸۱۱/۳، ۸۱۲) ١٥ - أبو عبد الله الحليمي : أبو عبد الله الحسين بن الحسن بن محمد ابن حليم المعروف بـ الحليمي " ، قال فيه الحاكم كان شيخ الشافعيين بما وراء النهر وأدبهم وأنظرهم بعد أستاذيه "القفال الشاشى" و "الأدنى"، وقال في النهاية : "كان الحليمي عظيم ،القدر، لا يحيط بكنه علمه إلا غواص". ولد ببخارى وقيل بجرجان سنة ثمان وثلاثين وثلاثمائة ومات سنة ثلاث وأربعمائة ، قيل : في جمادى وقيل : في ربيع الأول. ومن مصنفاته : "شعب الإيمان " : كتاب جليل جمع أحكاماً كثيرة ومعانى غريبة لم أظفر بكثير منها في غيره . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٤٠٤/١) ١٦ - أبو على السنجى : الشيخ أبو على الحسين بن شعيب المروزي السنجی، إمام زمانه في الفقه، تفقه على القفال وكان أجل أصحابه وأخذ أيضا عن الشيخ أبي حامد وشرح "المختصر شرحاً مطولا يُسمّيه إمام الحرمين بـ "المذهب الكبير " وشرحا أيضا " التلخيص " و "فروع ابن الحداد" وهما في غاية النفاسة والتحقيق، وهو أول من جمع في تصانيفه بين طريقة العراقيين والخراسانيين. توفى سنة سبع وعشرين وأربعمائة كذا قاله الرافعى في التدوين وقيل : سنة ثلاثين وقيل : نيف وثلاثين وجزم به ابن
Index of Notables: Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
12. Abu al-Husayn: He is Uthman ibn Asim ibn Husayn Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi al-Kufi. Al-Ijli said: He was a high-ranking shaykh, a man of sunnah, Kufan, Uthmani, trustworthy, reliable in hadith. Ibn Uyaynah said: 'When Ibn Husayn was asked about a matter, he said: I have no knowledge of it, and Allah knows best.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 127 AH, and it is also said otherwise. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 5:490)
13. Abu Hanifa: He is the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, founder of the Hanafi school, and one of the four followed imams. Ibn Hajar said: Some imams said: There has not appeared for any of the famous imams of Islam what has appeared for Abu Hanifa in terms of companions and students, and scholars and all people have not benefited as they have benefited from him and his companions. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said about him: 'He was in knowledge, piety, asceticism, and preferring the Hereafter at a level no one can reach.' Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'No one is more deserving of being followed than Abu Hanifa, because he was a pious, pure, devout, knowledgeable, and profound imam.' Al-Thawri said to someone who said 'I came from Abu Hanifa': 'You have come from the most worshipful person on earth.' Al-Nawawi said: 'He was an imam in that (meaning hadith), for he, may Allah be pleased with him, took hadith from four thousand shaykhs from the leading tabi'un and others.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'People in fiqh are dependent on Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' He authored in theology the book 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' and in hadith 'al-Musnad'. He was born in 80 AH and died, may Allah have mercy on him with abundant mercy, in 150 AH. (Summarized from Radd al-Muhtar 1:55-56, and Siyar A'lam al-Nubala 6:525)
14. Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj: The Imam, the scholar, Shaykh al-Islam, Judge Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Surayj al-Baghdadi, the role model of the Shafi'is. He heard from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Za'farani, Ali ibn Ashkab, Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Duri, al-Ramadi, Abu Dawud al-Sijistani and their class. I saw for him in it a composition in which he argued with hadith and analyzed them in the manner of one who understands this discipline. As for fiqh, he is its standard-bearer and the most learned of his peers. He assumed the position of teaching and leading imams studied under him. Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani, Abu Ahmad al-Ghitrifi, and Abu al-Walid Hassan ibn Muhammad and others narrated from him. Abu al-Walid al-Faqih said: I heard Ibn Surayj say: 'I have never seen a student of fiqh who engaged in theology and succeeded. He misses out on fiqh and does not attain knowledge of theology.' He was a man of sunnah and following. It reached me that he was asked about Allah's attributes, and he said: 'It is forbidden for intellects to depict Allah, for imaginations to limit Him, and for minds to describe Him except as He described Himself in His Book or on the tongue of His Messenger.' He died in Jumada al-Ula in the year 306 AH at the age of fifty-seven and a half. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 3:811-812)
15. Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi: Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Halim, known as al-Halimi. Al-Hakim said: He was the shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana, their most refined and the most insightful after his two teachers al-Qaffal al-Shashi and al-Adhani. In al-Nihayah, he said: 'Al-Halimi was of great stature; no one can encompass the depth of his knowledge except a diver.' He was born in Bukhara, and it is said in Jurjan, in 338 AH and died in 403 AH, it is said in Jumada or Rabi' al-Awwal. Among his works is 'Shu'ab al-Iman': a great book that collects many rulings and unique meanings, much of which I have not found in other works. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 1:404)
16. Abu Ali al-Sanji: Shaykh Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji, the imam of his time in fiqh. He studied fiqh under al-Qaffal and was the most prominent of his companions. He also studied under Shaykh Abu Hamid. He wrote a lengthy commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' which Imam al-Haramayn called 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir'. He also wrote commentaries on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad', both of which are extremely valuable and thorough. He was the first to combine in his works the method of the Iraqis and the Khurasanis. He died in 427 AH as stated by al-Rafi'i in al-Tadwin, and it is said 430 or around 431, and Ibn is certain of it.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is from the biographical index (fihris) of 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi, included in this work on Hanafi ifta' usul. It provides brief biographies of five key scholars who are referenced in the text. The first entry, Abu al-Husayn, is a trustworthy hadith transmitter. The second is the great Imam Abu Hanifa, whose virtues are extolled with quotes from Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Thawri, al-Nawawi, and al-Shafi'i. This establishes his authority in both fiqh and hadith. The third, Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj, was a leading Shafi'i scholar who warned against preoccupation with theology (kalam) at the expense of fiqh. The fourth, Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi, was a Shafi'i scholar in Transoxiana, author of 'Shu'ab al-Iman'. The fifth, Abu Ali al-Sanji, was the first to combine the Iraqi and Khurasani methods in his fiqh writings. These biographies serve to authenticate the sources and personalities cited in the fatwa methodology text.

Key Terms
كلام (kalam): Speculative theology involving dialectical reasoning about God and religion.
قدوة (qudwah): A role model or exemplar to be followed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Ibn Surayj say about students of fiqh who engage in kalam?
A) They become more successful
B) They fail in both fiqh and kalam
C) They become theologians
D) They are excused because it is difficult

Key Takeaway
Ibn Surayj's warning reminds muftis to prioritise textual evidence and not to let speculative theology distract from sound legal derivation.

Al-Halimi and the 'Shu'ab al-Iman'
Biographical entry of Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly contributions of al-Halimi, particularly his work 'Shu'ab al-Iman', and his role in Transoxiana.

Core Idea
Al-Halimi's 'Shu'ab al-Iman' is a comprehensive work that combines fiqh with unique insights, making him a key reference for later muftis.

This lesson covers Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi, a Shafi'i scholar from Transoxiana. His famous book 'Shu'ab al-Iman' collects many rulings and meanings not found elsewhere. This shows the importance of comprehensive reference works for muftis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Al-Halimi is al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan al-Halimi, a Shafi'i scholar in Transoxiana.
He is a Shafi'i, but his work is used by Hanafis too.
2
Note his teachers and status
He was the most insightful Shafi'i after his teachers al-Qaffal al-Shashi and al-Adhani.
This shows he was a top student of leading scholars.
3
Recognise his magnum opus
He authored 'Shu'ab al-Iman', a great book gathering many rulings and unique meanings not found in other works.
This book is a valuable resource for muftis.
4
Record his lifespan
Born 338 AH (or in Jurjan), died 403 AH.
He lived in the early 5th century AH.
