(تهذيب التهذيب : ٤٩٠/٥) ١٣ أبو حنيفة : هو الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، صاحب المذهب الحنفى، وأحد الأئمة الأربعة المتبوعين، قال ابن حجر : قال بعض الأئمة : لم يظهر لأحد من أئمة الإسلام المشهورين مثل ما ظهر لأبي حنيفة من الأصحاب والتلاميذ، ولم ينتفع العلماء وجميع الناس بمثل ما انتفعوا به وبأصحابه " . قال أحمد بن حنبل في حقه : "إنه كان من العلم والورع والزهد وإيثار الآخرة بمحل لا يدركه أحد . قال عبد الله بن المبارك: "ليس أحد أحق من أن يقتدى به من أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه كان إماماً تقيا ،نقيّا، ورعًا، عالما، فقيها . قال الثورى لمن قال جئت من أبى حنيفة: "لقد جئت من عند أعبد أهل الأرض" . قال النووي: "كان رحمه الله إماما في ذلك (أى في الحديث) فإنه رضى الله عنه أخذ الحديث عن أربعة آلاف شيخ من أئمة التابعين وغيرهم". قال الشافعي: "الناس" فى الفقه عيال على أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى " . له في علم الكلام كتاب الفقه الأكبر" وفي الحديث "المسند" ولد سنة ٨٠هـ وتوفي رحمه الله رحمة واسعة سنة ١٥٠هـ . (ملخصاً من رد المحتار: ٥٦،٥٥/١ ، وسير أعلام النبلاء : ٥٢٥/٦) ١٤ - أبو العباس بن سريج : الإمام العلامة شيخ الإسلام القاضي أبو العباس أحمد بن عمر بن سريج البغدادى قدوة الشافعية، سمع الحسن بن محمد الزعفراني، وعلى بن أشكاب، وعباس بن محمد الدورى والرمادي، وأبا داود السجستاني وطبقتهم . رأيت له فيه تصنيفا يحتج فيه بالأحاديث ويطرقها عمل من يفهم هذا الشأن ، وأما الفقه فهو حامل لواءه وعلم نظراءه، تصدر للاشتغال وتفقه به أئمة أعلام، وحدث عنه أبو القاسم الطبراني وأبو أحمد الغطريفى وأبو الوليد حسان بن محمد وآخرون . وقال أبو الوليد الفقيه يقول : سمعت ابن سريج يقول: ما رأيت من المتفقه من اشتغل بالكلام فأفلح ، يفوته الفقه ولا يصل إلى مــعــرفــة الكلام. وقد كان أبو العباس ابن سريج صاحب سنة واتباع، بلغني أنه سئل عن صفات الله تعالى فقال : حرام على العقول أن تمثل الله وعلى الأوهام أن تحده وعلى الألباب أن تصف إلا ما وصف به نفسه في كتابه أو على لسان رسوله . مات في جمادى الأولى سنة ست وثلاث مائة وله سبع و خمسون سنة ونصف . (تذکرة الحفاظ : ۸۱۱/۳، ۸۱۲) ١٥ - أبو عبد الله الحليمي : أبو عبد الله الحسين بن الحسن بن محمد ابن حليم المعروف بـ الحليمي " ، قال فيه الحاكم كان شيخ الشافعيين بما وراء النهر وأدبهم وأنظرهم بعد أستاذيه "القفال الشاشى" و "الأدنى"، وقال في النهاية : "كان الحليمي عظيم ،القدر، لا يحيط بكنه علمه إلا غواص". ولد ببخارى وقيل بجرجان سنة ثمان وثلاثين وثلاثمائة ومات سنة ثلاث وأربعمائة ، قيل : في جمادى وقيل : في ربيع الأول. ومن مصنفاته : "شعب الإيمان " : كتاب جليل جمع أحكاماً كثيرة ومعانى غريبة لم أظفر بكثير منها في غيره . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٤٠٤/١) ١٦ - أبو على السنجى : الشيخ أبو على الحسين بن شعيب المروزي السنجی، إمام زمانه في الفقه، تفقه على القفال وكان أجل أصحابه وأخذ أيضا عن الشيخ أبي حامد وشرح "المختصر شرحاً مطولا يُسمّيه إمام الحرمين بـ "المذهب الكبير " وشرحا أيضا " التلخيص " و "فروع ابن الحداد" وهما في غاية النفاسة والتحقيق، وهو أول من جمع في تصانيفه بين طريقة العراقيين والخراسانيين. توفى سنة سبع وعشرين وأربعمائة كذا قاله الرافعى في التدوين وقيل : سنة ثلاثين وقيل : نيف وثلاثين وجزم به ابن
Index of Notables: Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
12. Abu al-Husayn: He is Uthman ibn Asim ibn Husayn Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi al-Kufi. Al-Ijli said: He was a high-ranking shaykh, a man of sunnah, Kufan, Uthmani, trustworthy, reliable in hadith. Ibn Uyaynah said: 'When Ibn Husayn was asked about a matter, he said: I have no knowledge of it, and Allah knows best.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 127 AH, and it is also said otherwise. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 5:490)
13. Abu Hanifa: He is the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, founder of the Hanafi school, and one of the four followed imams. Ibn Hajar said: Some imams said: There has not appeared for any of the famous imams of Islam what has appeared for Abu Hanifa in terms of companions and students, and scholars and all people have not benefited as they have benefited from him and his companions. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said about him: 'He was in knowledge, piety, asceticism, and preferring the Hereafter at a level no one can reach.' Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'No one is more deserving of being followed than Abu Hanifa, because he was a pious, pure, devout, knowledgeable, and profound imam.' Al-Thawri said to someone who said 'I came from Abu Hanifa': 'You have come from the most worshipful person on earth.' Al-Nawawi said: 'He was an imam in that (meaning hadith), for he, may Allah be pleased with him, took hadith from four thousand shaykhs from the leading tabi'un and others.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'People in fiqh are dependent on Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' He authored in theology the book 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' and in hadith 'al-Musnad'. He was born in 80 AH and died, may Allah have mercy on him with abundant mercy, in 150 AH. (Summarized from Radd al-Muhtar 1:55-56, and Siyar A'lam al-Nubala 6:525)
14. Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj: The Imam, the scholar, Shaykh al-Islam, Judge Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Surayj al-Baghdadi, the role model of the Shafi'is. He heard from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Za'farani, Ali ibn Ashkab, Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Duri, al-Ramadi, Abu Dawud al-Sijistani and their class. I saw for him in it a composition in which he argued with hadith and analyzed them in the manner of one who understands this discipline. As for fiqh, he is its standard-bearer and the most learned of his peers. He assumed the position of teaching and leading imams studied under him. Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani, Abu Ahmad al-Ghitrifi, and Abu al-Walid Hassan ibn Muhammad and others narrated from him. Abu al-Walid al-Faqih said: I heard Ibn Surayj say: 'I have never seen a student of fiqh who engaged in theology and succeeded. He misses out on fiqh and does not attain knowledge of theology.' He was a man of sunnah and following. It reached me that he was asked about Allah's attributes, and he said: 'It is forbidden for intellects to depict Allah, for imaginations to limit Him, and for minds to describe Him except as He described Himself in His Book or on the tongue of His Messenger.' He died in Jumada al-Ula in the year 306 AH at the age of fifty-seven and a half. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 3:811-812)
15. Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi: Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Halim, known as al-Halimi. Al-Hakim said: He was the shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana, their most refined and the most insightful after his two teachers al-Qaffal al-Shashi and al-Adhani. In al-Nihayah, he said: 'Al-Halimi was of great stature; no one can encompass the depth of his knowledge except a diver.' He was born in Bukhara, and it is said in Jurjan, in 338 AH and died in 403 AH, it is said in Jumada or Rabi' al-Awwal. Among his works is 'Shu'ab al-Iman': a great book that collects many rulings and unique meanings, much of which I have not found in other works. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 1:404)
16. Abu Ali al-Sanji: Shaykh Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji, the imam of his time in fiqh. He studied fiqh under al-Qaffal and was the most prominent of his companions. He also studied under Shaykh Abu Hamid. He wrote a lengthy commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' which Imam al-Haramayn called 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir'. He also wrote commentaries on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad', both of which are extremely valuable and thorough. He was the first to combine in his works the method of the Iraqis and the Khurasanis. He died in 427 AH as stated by al-Rafi'i in al-Tadwin, and it is said 430 or around 431, and Ibn is certain of it.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is from the biographical index (fihris) of 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi, included in this work on Hanafi ifta' usul. It provides brief biographies of five key scholars who are referenced in the text. The first entry, Abu al-Husayn, is a trustworthy hadith transmitter. The second is the great Imam Abu Hanifa, whose virtues are extolled with quotes from Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Thawri, al-Nawawi, and al-Shafi'i. This establishes his authority in both fiqh and hadith. The third, Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj, was a leading Shafi'i scholar who warned against preoccupation with theology (kalam) at the expense of fiqh. The fourth, Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi, was a Shafi'i scholar in Transoxiana, author of 'Shu'ab al-Iman'. The fifth, Abu Ali al-Sanji, was the first to combine the Iraqi and Khurasani methods in his fiqh writings. These biographies serve to authenticate the sources and personalities cited in the fatwa methodology text.

Key Terms
شعب الإيمان (Shu'ab al-Iman): The Branches of Faith, a comprehensive work by al-Halimi covering various aspects of faith and fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who described al-Halimi as the shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana?
A) Al-Nawawi
B) Al-Hakim
C) Al-Qaffal
D) Al-Isnawi

Key Takeaway
Al-Halimi's 'Shu'ab al-Iman' is a valuable resource with unique rulings, useful for muftis beyond the Shafi'i school.

Abu Ali al-Sanji: Blending the Iraqi and Khurasani Methods
Biographical entry of Abu Ali al-Sanji

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe al-Sanji's role in combining the Iraqi and Khurasani jurisprudential methods and identify his major works.

Core Idea
Al-Sanji was the first to systematically merge the Iraqi and Khurasani approaches in fiqh, creating a synthetic, thorough methodology.

This lesson focuses on Abu Ali al-Sanji, a leading Shafi'i jurist who pioneered the integration of the Iraqi and Khurasani schools of legal thought. His work, like the large commentary on al-Mukhtasar, is known for its thoroughness and depth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Al-Sanji is al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji, an imam in fiqh.
He is from Marw in Khurasan.
2
Note his teachers
He studied under al-Qaffal and others.
Al-Qaffal is a major Shafi'i scholar.
3
Recognise his method
He was the first to combine the methods of the Iraqis and Khurasanians in his works.
This synthesis is significant for usul al-fiqh.
4
Identify his works
He wrote a lengthy commentary on al-Mukhtasar (called al-Madhhab al-Kabir by Imam al-Haramayn), commentaries on al-Talkhis and Furu' Ibn al-Haddad.
These works are highly regarded for their precision.
5
Record his death
Died in 427 AH (or 430/431).
He lived in the 5th century AH.

فهرس الأعلام آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى ١٢ أبو الحصين : هو عثمان بن عاصم بن حصين أبو الحصين الأسدى الكوفى، قال العجلى : كان شيخًا عاليًا صاحب سنة، كوفيا، عثمانيا، ثقة، ثبتا في الحديث، وقال ابن عيينة : "كان ابن حصين إذا سئل عن مسألة قال : ليس لى بها علم والله أعلم . توفى رحمه الله سنة سبع وعشرين ومائة ، وقيل : غير ذلك . (تهذيب التهذيب : ٤٩٠/٥) ١٣ أبو حنيفة : هو الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي، صاحب المذهب الحنفى، وأحد الأئمة الأربعة المتبوعين، قال ابن حجر : قال بعض الأئمة : لم يظهر لأحد من أئمة الإسلام المشهورين مثل ما ظهر لأبي حنيفة من الأصحاب والتلاميذ، ولم ينتفع العلماء وجميع الناس بمثل ما انتفعوا به وبأصحابه " . قال أحمد بن حنبل في حقه : "إنه كان من العلم والورع والزهد وإيثار الآخرة بمحل لا يدركه أحد . قال عبد الله بن المبارك: "ليس أحد أحق من أن يقتدى به من أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه كان إماماً تقيا ،نقيّا، ورعًا، عالما، فقيها . قال الثورى لمن قال جئت من أبى حنيفة: "لقد جئت من عند أعبد أهل الأرض" . قال النووي: "كان رحمه الله إماما في ذلك (أى في الحديث) فإنه رضى الله عنه أخذ الحديث عن أربعة آلاف شيخ من أئمة التابعين وغيرهم". قال الشافعي: "الناس" فى الفقه عيال على أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى " . له في علم الكلام كتاب الفقه الأكبر" وفي الحديث "المسند" ولد سنة ٨٠هـ وتوفي رحمه الله رحمة واسعة سنة ١٥٠هـ . (ملخصاً من رد المحتار: ٥٦،٥٥/١ ، وسير أعلام النبلاء : ٥٢٥/٦) ١٤ - أبو العباس بن سريج : الإمام العلامة شيخ الإسلام القاضي أبو العباس أحمد بن عمر بن سريج البغدادى قدوة الشافعية، سمع الحسن بن محمد الزعفراني، وعلى بن أشكاب، وعباس بن محمد الدورى والرمادي، وأبا داود السجستاني وطبقتهم . رأيت له فيه تصنيفا يحتج فيه بالأحاديث ويطرقها عمل من يفهم هذا الشأن ، وأما الفقه فهو حامل لواءه وعلم نظراءه، تصدر للاشتغال وتفقه به أئمة أعلام، وحدث عنه أبو القاسم الطبراني وأبو أحمد الغطريفى وأبو الوليد حسان بن محمد وآخرون . وقال أبو الوليد الفقيه يقول : سمعت ابن سريج يقول: ما رأيت من المتفقه من اشتغل بالكلام فأفلح ، يفوته الفقه ولا يصل إلى مــعــرفــة الكلام. وقد كان أبو العباس ابن سريج صاحب سنة واتباع، بلغني أنه سئل عن صفات الله تعالى فقال : حرام على العقول أن تمثل الله وعلى الأوهام أن تحده وعلى الألباب أن تصف إلا ما وصف به نفسه في كتابه أو على لسان رسوله . مات في جمادى الأولى سنة ست وثلاث مائة وله سبع و خمسون سنة ونصف . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٤٠٤/١) ١٦ - أبو على السنجى : الشيخ أبو على الحسين بن شعيب المروزي السنجی، إمام زمانه في الفقه، تفقه على القفال وكان أجل أصحابه وأخذ أيضا عن الشيخ أبي حامد وشرح "المختصر شرحاً مطولا يُسمّيه إمام الحرمين بـ "المذهب الكبير " وشرحا أيضا " التلخيص " و "فروع ابن الحداد" وهما في غاية النفاسة والتحقيق، وهو أول من جمع في تصانيفه بين طريقة العراقيين والخراسانيين. توفى سنة سبع وعشرين وأربعمائة كذا قاله الرافعى في التدوين وقيل : سنة ثلاثين وقيل : نيف وثلاثين وجزم به ابن
Index of Notables: Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
12. Abu al-Husayn: He is Uthman ibn Asim ibn Husayn Abu al-Husayn al-Asadi al-Kufi. Al-Ijli said: He was a high-ranking shaykh, a man of sunnah, Kufan, Uthmani, trustworthy, reliable in hadith. Ibn Uyaynah said: 'When Ibn Husayn was asked about a matter, he said: I have no knowledge of it, and Allah knows best.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 127 AH, and it is also said otherwise. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 5:490)
13. Abu Hanifa: He is the greatest Imam, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, founder of the Hanafi school, and one of the four followed imams. Ibn Hajar said: Some imams said: There has not appeared for any of the famous imams of Islam what has appeared for Abu Hanifa in terms of companions and students, and scholars and all people have not benefited as they have benefited from him and his companions. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said about him: 'He was in knowledge, piety, asceticism, and preferring the Hereafter at a level no one can reach.' Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'No one is more deserving of being followed than Abu Hanifa, because he was a pious, pure, devout, knowledgeable, and profound imam.' Al-Thawri said to someone who said 'I came from Abu Hanifa': 'You have come from the most worshipful person on earth.' Al-Nawawi said: 'He was an imam in that (meaning hadith), for he, may Allah be pleased with him, took hadith from four thousand shaykhs from the leading tabi'un and others.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'People in fiqh are dependent on Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' He authored in theology the book 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' and in hadith 'al-Musnad'. He was born in 80 AH and died, may Allah have mercy on him with abundant mercy, in 150 AH. (Summarized from Radd al-Muhtar 1:55-56, and Siyar A'lam al-Nubala 6:525)
14. Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj: The Imam, the scholar, Shaykh al-Islam, Judge Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Surayj al-Baghdadi, the role model of the Shafi'is. He heard from al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Za'farani, Ali ibn Ashkab, Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Duri, al-Ramadi, Abu Dawud al-Sijistani and their class. I saw for him in it a composition in which he argued with hadith and analyzed them in the manner of one who understands this discipline. As for fiqh, he is its standard-bearer and the most learned of his peers. He assumed the position of teaching and leading imams studied under him. Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani, Abu Ahmad al-Ghitrifi, and Abu al-Walid Hassan ibn Muhammad and others narrated from him. Abu al-Walid al-Faqih said: I heard Ibn Surayj say: 'I have never seen a student of fiqh who engaged in theology and succeeded. He misses out on fiqh and does not attain knowledge of theology.' He was a man of sunnah and following. It reached me that he was asked about Allah's attributes, and he said: 'It is forbidden for intellects to depict Allah, for imaginations to limit Him, and for minds to describe Him except as He described Himself in His Book or on the tongue of His Messenger.' He died in Jumada al-Ula in the year 306 AH at the age of fifty-seven and a half. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 3:811-812)
15. Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi: Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Halim, known as al-Halimi. Al-Hakim said: He was the shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana, their most refined and the most insightful after his two teachers al-Qaffal al-Shashi and al-Adhani. In al-Nihayah, he said: 'Al-Halimi was of great stature; no one can encompass the depth of his knowledge except a diver.' He was born in Bukhara, and it is said in Jurjan, in 338 AH and died in 403 AH, it is said in Jumada or Rabi' al-Awwal. Among his works is 'Shu'ab al-Iman': a great book that collects many rulings and unique meanings, much of which I have not found in other works. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi 1:404)
16. Abu Ali al-Sanji: Shaykh Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji, the imam of his time in fiqh. He studied fiqh under al-Qaffal and was the most prominent of his companions. He also studied under Shaykh Abu Hamid. He wrote a lengthy commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' which Imam al-Haramayn called 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir'. He also wrote commentaries on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad', both of which are extremely valuable and thorough. He was the first to combine in his works the method of the Iraqis and the Khurasanis. He died in 427 AH as stated by al-Rafi'i in al-Tadwin, and it is said 430 or around 431, and Ibn is certain of it.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is from the biographical index (fihris) of 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi, included in this work on Hanafi ifta' usul. It provides brief biographies of five key scholars who are referenced in the text. The first entry, Abu al-Husayn, is a trustworthy hadith transmitter. The second is the great Imam Abu Hanifa, whose virtues are extolled with quotes from Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Thawri, al-Nawawi, and al-Shafi'i. This establishes his authority in both fiqh and hadith. The third, Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj, was a leading Shafi'i scholar who warned against preoccupation with theology (kalam) at the expense of fiqh. The fourth, Abu Abd Allah al-Halimi, was a Shafi'i scholar in Transoxiana, author of 'Shu'ab al-Iman'. The fifth, Abu Ali al-Sanji, was the first to combine the Iraqi and Khurasani methods in his fiqh writings. These biographies serve to authenticate the sources and personalities cited in the fatwa methodology text.

Key Terms
طريقة العراقيين (tariqat al-'Iraqiyyin): The Iraqi method in fiqh, characterized by extensive use of qiyas and theoretical principles.
طريقة الخراسانيين (tariqat al-Khurasaniyyin): The Khurasani method, emphasizing transmitted texts (athar) and the literal meanings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Al-Madhhab al-Kabir

D) Furu' Ibn al-Haddad

Key Takeaway
Al-Sanji's synthesis of methods reminds muftis to use diverse approaches for thorough legal reasoning.

Who Was Abu Abdullah al-Halimi?
Biographical entry for a Shafi'i scholar from Adab al-Fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Abu Abdullah al-Halimi's madhhab, his scholarly rank, and his major work, and explain why his biography is relevant in usul al-iftaa.

Core Idea
A mufti must know the scholarly lineage and works of authoritative figures, even from other madhhabs.

This lesson introduces a Shafi'i scholar, Abu Abdullah al-Halimi, whose biography appears in al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa. Understanding his place in the Shafi'i school and his famous work 'Shu'ab al-Iman' helps a Hanafi mufti appreciate the breadth of Islamic scholarship and the need to reference works from other schools when necessary.

Guided Path
1
Locate the scholar's full name and nisbah
Identify the full Arabic name (Abu Abdullah al-Husayn ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Halim) and his nisbah (al-Halimi). This establishes his identity and lineage.
The nisbah often indicates place of origin or tribe; here it is derived from his grandfather's name.
2
Identify his madhhab and scholarly rank
From the text, note that al-Hakim called him 'shaykh of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana' and praised his knowledge. This confirms he is a Shafi'i jurist of high rank.
Knowing the madhhab prevents confusion: he is not Hanafi, but his works are used for reference.
3
Note his birth and death dates
He was born in 338 AH and died in 403 AH. These dates give historical context and show he lived during the 4th-5th centuries AH, a period of rich scholarly activity.
Dates help place him in the chain of scholars; he was contemporary with many Hanafi masters.
4
Recognize his major work and its significance
His work 'Shu'ab al-Iman' is described as a magnificent book collecting many rulings and rare meanings. This work is referenced across schools for its unique content.
Even though Hanafi muftis primarily rely on Hanafi texts, such works can be consulted for specific issues where Hanafi sources are silent.
5
Connect to usul al-iftaa
The biography appears in a work on the etiquette of fatwa. This reminds muftis to be aware of prominent scholars from other madhhabs and to use their works with proper attribution.
Al-Nawawi included this entry to show the breadth of sources a mufti might encounter.

Abu Ali al-Sanji: The Synthesizer of Shafi'i Schools
Biographical entry for a Shafi'i jurist and commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Abu Ali al-Sanji as a Shafi'i jurist and state his unique contribution to fiqh methodology.

Core Idea
Al-Sanji was the first to unite the Iraqi and Khurasani fiqh methods, bridging two major juristic traditions.

This lesson introduces a key figure in Shafi'i legal history: Abu Ali al-Sanji. Although not a Hanafi scholar, his synthesis of Iraqi and Khurasani approaches had a lasting impact on Sunni fiqh. Understanding his biography helps students appreciate the development of juristic methodology and the importance of scholarly chains in the transmission of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his full name
Record al-Sanji's full name: Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji. Note the nisbah 'al-Sanji' from the village Sanj near Marw.
His lineage traces to Marw in present-day Turkmenistan.
2
Trace his teachers and works
He studied under al-Qaffal (his most distinguished student) and Shaykh Abu Hamid. He wrote a lengthy commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' (called 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir' by Imam al-Haramayn), and commented on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad'.
These works are highly regarded in the Shafi'i tradition for their thoroughness.
3
Recognize his methodological innovation
He was the first to combine in his writings the methods of the Iraqi and Khurasani jurists. This synthesis made his works unique and influential.
Iraqi method tended to rely on qiyas and ra'y, while Khurasani method was more tradition-text based.
4
Memorize key dates and details
Death date: 427 AH (according to al-Rafi'i), also reported as 430 or 431 AH. He was buried next to his teacher al-Qaffal.
Variations in death dates are common in early biographies; the consensus is around 430 AH.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٦ - أبو علي السنجي : الشيخ أبو علي الحسين بن شعيب المروزي السنجي، إمام زمانه في الفقه، تفقه على القفال وكان أجل أصحابه وأخذ أيضا عن الشيخ أبي حامد وشرح "المختصر شرحاً مطولا يُسمّيه إمام الحرمين بـ "المذهب الكبير " وشرحا أيضا " التلخيص " و "فروع ابن الحداد" وهما في غاية النفاسة والتحقيق، وهو أول من جمع في تصانيفه بين طريقة العراقيين والخراسانيين. توفى سنة سبع وعشرين وأربعمائة كذا قاله الرافعي في التدوين وقيل : سنة ثلاثين وقيل : نيف وثلاثين وجزم به ابن خلكان، ودفن إلى جانب أستاذه القفال . و "سنج " قرية من قرى "مرو" وهي بكسر السين المهملة بعدها نون ساكنة ثم جيم. (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوي : ٢٨/٢)
16 - Abu Ali al-Sanji: Shaykh Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb al-Marwazi al-Sanji, the imam of his time in fiqh. He studied under al-Qaffal and was his most distinguished student, and also studied under Shaykh Abu Hamid. He wrote a lengthy commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' which Imam al-Haramayn called 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir', and also commented on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad', both of the highest quality and verification. He was the first to combine in his writings the method of the Iraqis and the Khurasanis. He died in the year 427 AH according to al-Rafi'i in al-Tadwin, and it is said 430 or 431 AH, which Ibn Khallikan affirmed, and was buried next to his teacher al-Qaffal. 'Sanj' is a village of Marw, with a kasrah on the sin, then a sukun on the noon, then a jim. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyah by al-Isnawi: 2/28)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage introduces Abu Ali al-Sanji, a prominent Shafi'i jurist and commentator. He was a student of al-Qaffal al-Shashi and later became a leading authority. His major contributions include a detailed commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' (known as 'al-Madhhab al-Kabir'), as well as commentaries on 'al-Talkhis' and 'Furu' Ibn al-Haddad'. He is noted for being the first to synthesize the Iraqi and Khurasani approaches in fiqh. The text also clarifies the etymology of 'Sanj' as a village near Marw. His death date is given with some variation, but he was buried beside his teacher al-Qaffal. This entry highlights the scholarly chain and the integration of different juristic traditions.

Key Terms
السنجي (al-Sanji): Nisbah referring to the village Sanj near Marw, used to identify Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Shu'ayb.
المذهب الكبير (al-Madhhab al-Kabir): The title given by Imam al-Haramayn to al-Sanji's lengthy commentary on al-Mukhtasar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Importance of Scholar Biographies for the Mufti: The Case of Ibn Abd al-Barr
Biographical entry for a Maliki hadith master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Ibn Abd al-Barr and explain why a Hanafi mufti must consider the madhhab and reliability of transmitters like him when evaluating hadith.

Core Idea
A mufti must know a narrator's madhhab and reliability; Ibn Abd al-Barr was Maliki, not Shafi'i.

This lesson presents a short biography of Abu Umar ibn Abd al-Barr, a towering Maliki hadith scholar from al-Andalus. While he did not belong to the Hanafi school, his works and narrations are widely used across madhhabs. Understanding his background helps a mufti correctly attribute rulings and assess the strength of hadith chains.

Guided Path
1
Extract core biographical data
Locate the scholar's full name, birth and death dates, and honorary titles such as 'Hafiz al-Maghrib'.
These details are the foundation for any biographical evaluation.
2
Identify his teachers and students
Note the names of those he narrated from and those who narrated from him. This reveals his scholarly network and chain of transmission.
A long list of reputable teachers and students indicates high standing.
3
Determine his madhhab and geographical context
From the region (al-Andalus) and his relationships (e.g., al-Baji), infer that he was Maliki. The passage does not explicitly state his madhhab, but context is key.
This is crucial for usul al-iftaa when a narrator's view is cited.
4
Assess his reliability (jarih and ta'dil)
Note the praise from scholars like al-Baji and al-Ghassani, confirming his mastery in hadith.
The title 'Hafiz al-Maghrib' and phrases like 'excelled over the people of his time' indicate high trustworthiness.
5
Apply the information to a Hanafi fatwa context
Consider how this biography would be used: if a hadith is transmitted through Ibn Abd al-Barr, a Hanafi mufti would verify his reliability and note his Maliki affiliation, which may affect the interpretation or tarjih.
Biographical knowledge prevents mistaken attribution of a Maliki view to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٧- أبو عمر بن عبد البر : الإمام، شيخ الإسلام، حافظ المغرب أبو عمر يوسف بن عبد الله بن محمد بن عبد البر بن عاصم النمري القرطبي . ولد سنة ثمان وستين وثلاث مائة في ربيع الآخر، وطلب الحديث قبل مولد الخطيب بأعوام، حدث عن خلف بن القاسم، وعبد الوارث بن سفيان وعبد الله بن محمد بن عبد المؤمن، ومحمد بن عبد الملك بن صيفون، وسعيد بن نصر وغيرهم. وأجاز له من مصر المسند أبو الفتح ابن سيبخت والحافظ عبد الغني ومن مكة أبو القاسم عبيد الله بن السقطي وساد أهل الزمان في الحفظ والإتقان. قال أبو الوليد الباجي : "لم يكن بالأندلس مثل أبي عمر في الحديث". وقال الغساني : سمعت ابن عبد البر يقول : لم يكن أحد ببلدنا مثل قاسم بن محمد وأحمد ابن خالد الجباب. قال الغساني : " ولم يكن ابن عبد البر بدونهما ولا متخلفا عنهما " . حدّث عنه أبو العباس الدلائي، وأبو محمد بن أبي قحافة، وأبو الحسن بن مفوز ، وأبو علي الغساني، وأبو عبد الله الحميدي وغيرهم. قال أبو داود المقرئ : مات أبو عمر ليلة الجمعة سلخ ربيع الآخر سنة ثلاث وستين وأربع مائة، واستكمل خمساً وتسعين سنة وخمسة أعوام . (تذكرة الحفاظ : ٣/ ١١٢٨)
17 - Abu Umar ibn Abd al-Barr: The Imam, Shaykh al-Islam, Hafiz of the Maghrib, Abu Umar Yusuf ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Barr ibn Asim al-Namari al-Qurtubi. He was born in the year 368 AH in Rabi' al-Akhir, and sought hadith years before the birth of al-Khatib. He narrated from Khalaf ibn al-Qasim, Abd al-Warith ibn Sufyan, Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Mu'min, Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Sayfun, Sa'id ibn Nasr, and others. He was granted ijazah from Egypt by al-Musnad Abu al-Fath ibn Sibakht and al-Hafiz Abd al-Ghani, and from Makkah by Abu al-Qasim Ubaydullah ibn al-Saqti, and he excelled over the people of his time in memorization and precision. Abu al-Walid al-Baji said: 'There was no one like Abu Umar in hadith in al-Andalus.' Al-Ghassani said: I heard Ibn Abd al-Barr say: 'There was no one in our land like Qasim ibn Muhammad and Ahmad ibn Khalid al-Jabab.' Al-Ghassani said: 'Ibn Abd al-Barr was not inferior to them nor lagging behind them.' Narrated from him by Abu al-Abbas al-Dala'i, Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Qahafa, Abu al-Hasan ibn Mafuz, Abu Ali al-Ghassani, Abu Abdullah al-Humaydi, and others. Abu Dawud al-Muqri' said: Abu Umar died on the night of Friday, the last day of Rabi' al-Akhir in the year 463 AH, having completed ninety-five years and five months. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz: 3/1128)
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This entry presents Abu Umar ibn Abd al-Barr, a towering figure in hadith and Maliki fiqh from al-Andalus. The biography emphasizes his exceptional memory and precision, making him a leading authority. It lists his teachers and students, including notable scholars like al-Baji and al-Ghassani. His death date is given precisely. Ibn Abd al-Barr is known for his works such as 'al-Istidhkar' and 'al-Tamhid'. This entry serves to document the scholarly chain of hadith masters, which is relevant for muftis in evaluating the reliability of narrations.

Key Terms
ابن عبد البر (Ibn Abd al-Barr): The famous Maliki hadith scholar and historian from Cordoba, known for his works in hadith and fiqh.
حافظ المغرب (Hafiz al-Maghrib): Title meaning 'the memorizer of the Maghrib,' indicating his supreme status in hadith memorization in the western Islamic world.

This lesson introduces you to a Shafi'i jurist whose work 'al-Bahr fi al-Madhhab' is occasionally referenced in later Hanafi fatwa collections. Using the Biographical Index (Fihris al-A'lam) in Hanafi Usul al-Iftaa
Biographical index listing scholars cited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of a biographical index in a Hanafi usul al-iftaa text and extract key biographical details for cited scholars.

Core Idea
A biographical index establishes the authority and transmission chains of scholars quoted in a text.

The following passage is a biographical index (Fihris al-A'lam) from the end of a work on usul al-iftaa. It provides concise biographies of scholars cited in the main discussion, including their full names, birth/death dates, teachers, students, and notable works. This index serves as a reference to assess the credibility and madhhab affiliation of each scholar, which is crucial for understanding the weight of their opinions in Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the index's purpose
Understand that this index is an appendix providing biographical data, not a ruling or argument. It is used to verify the credentials of scholars mentioned in the main text.
This is a standard feature of classical Islamic works.
2
Identify key biographical details
For each scholar, note the full name, madhhab, birth/death dates, teachers, students, and major works. For example, Ibn Abd al-Barr is a Maliki hadith scholar from Andalusia.
Details such as 'Hanafi then Shafi'i' for al-Sam'ani are important for understanding cited opinions.
3
Note cross-madhhab inclusion
The index includes scholars from other madhhabs (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) because their works or opinions are referenced. Recognize that this does not imply endorsement of their madhhab, but acknowledges their authority in specific fields.
For instance, al-Athram is a Hanbali student of Imam Ahmad.
4
Use the index to assess authority
When encountering a scholar cited in the main text, refer to the index to determine their level of knowledge, chain of transmission, and any relevant biographical notes that affect the weight of their opinion in Hanafi fatwa.
For example, al-Ruyani's claim to memorize all of Shafi'i's works would enhance his authority on Shafi'i positions.

۱۷- أبو عمر بن عبد البر : الإمام، شيخ الإسلام، حافظ المغرب أبو عمر يوسف بن عبد الله بن محمد بن عبد البر بن عاصم النمرى القرطبي . ولد سنة ثمان وستين وثلاث مائة في ربيع الآخر، وطلب الحديث قبل مولد الخطيب بأعوام، حدث عن خلف بن القاسم، وعبد الوارث بن سفيان وعبد الله بن محمد بن عبد المؤمن، ومحمد بن عبد الملك بن صيفون، وسعيد بن نصر وغيرهم. وأجاز له من مصر المسند
أبو الفتح ابن سيبخت والحافظ عبد الغنى ومن مكة أبو القاسم عبيد الله بن السقطي وساد أهل الزمان في الحفظ والإتقان. قال أبو الوليد الباجي : "لم يكن بالأندلس مثل أبي عمر في الحديث". وقال الغساني : سمعت ابن عبد البر يقول : لم يكن أحد ببلدنا مثل قاسم بن محمد وأحمد ابن خالد الجباب. قال الغساني : " ولم يكن ابن عبد البر بدونهما ولا متخلفا عنهما " . حدّث عنه أبو العباس الدلائي، وأبو محمد بن أبي قحافة، وأبو الحسن بن مفوز ، وأبو على الغساني، وأبو عبد الله الحميدي وغيرهم. قال أبو داود المقرئ : مات أبو عمر ليلة الجمعة سلخ ربيع الآخر سنة ثلاث وستين وأربع مائة، واستكمل خمساً وتسعين سنة وخمسة أعوام . (تذكرة الحفاظ : ۳/ ۱۱۲۸)
-۱۸ - أبو المحاسن الروياني : أبو المحاسن عبد الواحد بن إسماعيل بن أحمد ابن محمد الرویانی ،الطبری ،الشافعی، مولده آخر سنة خمس عشرة وأربعمائة، وتفقه ببخارى مدة، وارتحل في طلب الحديث والفقه جميعا، وبرع في الفقه ومَهَرَ وناظر وصنّف التصانيف الباهرة .
حدث عنه زاهر الشحامي، وإسماعيل بن محمد التيمي، وأبو طاهر السلفي وأبو رشيد إسماعيل بن غانم ،وغيرهم، وكان يقول : "لو احترقت كتب الشافعي لأمليت من حفظي " . وله كتاب البحر في المذهب " ، طويل جداً غزير الفوائد، وكتاب
مناصيص الشافعي"، وكتاب "حلية المؤمن"، وكتاب "الكافي
وكان ذا جاه عريض وحشمة وافرة، وقبول تام وباع طويل في الفقه وكان العماد محمد بن أبي سعد صدر الرى فى عصره يقول : " أبو المحاسن القاضي شافعي عصره".
قال معمر بن الفاخر : " قتل بجامع آمل يوم جمعة حادي عشر المحرم، قتله الملاحدة يعنى الإسماعيلية" . قلت : قتل سنة إحدى وخمسمائة، ورويان : بلدة من أعمال طبرستان، وأما الرى فمدينة كبيرة والنسبة إليها رازى .

17- Abu Umar ibn Abd al-Barr: The Imam, Shaykh al-Islam, Hafiz of the Maghreb, Abu Umar Yusuf ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Barr ibn Asim al-Numari al-Qurtubi. Born in the year 368 AH in Rabi' al-Akhir, and sought hadith years before the birth of al-Khatib. He narrated from Khalaf ibn al-Qasim, Abdul Warith ibn Sufyan, Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Mu'min, Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Sayfun, Sa'id ibn Nasr, and others. He was granted ijazah from Egypt by al-Musnad Abu al-Fath ibn Sibakht and al-Hafiz Abd al-Ghani, and from Mecca by Abu al-Qasim Ubaydullah ibn al-Siqti. He surpassed the people of his time in memorization and precision. Abu al-Walid al-Baji said: 'There was no one in Andalusia like Abu Umar in hadith.' Al-Ghassani said: I heard Ibn Abd al-Barr say: 'There was no one in our country like Qasim ibn Muhammad and Ahmad ibn Khalid al-Jabbab.' Al-Ghassani said: 'And Ibn Abd al-Barr was not inferior to them nor lagging behind them.' Narrated from him by Abu al-Abbas al-Dala'i, Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Qahafa, Abu al-Hasan ibn Mufawwiz, Abu Ali al-Ghassani, Abu Abdullah al-Humaydi, and others. Abu Dawud al-Muqri' said: Abu Umar died on the night of Friday at the end of Rabi' al-Akhir in the year 463 AH, and he had completed ninety-five years and five months. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz: 3/1128)
-18 - Abu al-Mahasin al-Ruyani: Abu al-Mahasin Abd al-Wahid ibn Ismail ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Ruyani, al-Tabari, al-Shafi'i. His birth was at the end of the year 415 AH. He studied fiqh in Bukhara for a period, and traveled seeking both hadith and fiqh. He excelled in fiqh, mastered it, debated, and authored brilliant works.
Narrated from him by Zahir al-Shahami, Ismail ibn Muhammad al-Taymi, Abu Tahir al-Silafi, Abu Rashid Ismail ibn Ghanim, and others. He used to say: 'If the books of al-Shafi'i were burned, I would dictate from my memory.' He authored the book 'al-Bahr fi al-Madhhab', very long and abundant in benefits, and the book
'Manasib al-Shafi'i', and the book 'Hilyat al-Mu'min', and the book 'al-Kafi'.
He had great prestige, ample dignity, complete acceptance, and a long stance in fiqh. Al-Imad Muhammad ibn Abi Sa'd, the chief of Rayy in his time, said: 'Abu al-Mahasin al-Qadi is the Shafi'i of his era.'
Mu'ammar ibn al-Fakhir said: 'He was killed in the Jami' of Amul on a Friday, the 11th of Muharram, killed by the heretics, meaning the Ismailis.' I said: He was killed in the year 501 AH. Ruyan is a town of the districts of Tabaristan, and as for Rayy, it is a large city and the nisba to it is Razi.
19 - Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni: See Imam al-Haramayn.
(Siyar A'lam al-Nubala: 14/280)
-20 - Abu al-Muzaffar al-Sam'ani: Abu al-Muzaffar Mansur ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Jabbar ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far ibn Ahmad al-Tamimi al-Marwazi, the jurist, Hanafi then Shafi'i, famous and known like his forefathers as 'al-Sam'ani'. He traveled the lands and returned to his homeland and died there. He was born in 642 AH and died in 489 AH (nine and eighty and four hundred). He authored the books: 'al-Istilam fi al-Radd ala Abi Zayd al-Dabusi', 'Alf Hadith an Alf Shaykh', 'al-Intisar fi al-Radd ala al-Qadiriyya al-Ashraf', 'al-Awsat fi al-Khilaf', 'al-Burhan' containing a thousand controversial issues, 'Tafsir al-Qur'an', 'al-Qawati' fi al-Usul', 'Mu'jam al-Shuyukh', 'Minhaj Ahl al-Sunna fi al-Hadith'. (Hadiyyat al-Arifin: 6/473)
-21 - al-Athram: He is the Imam, the allama, Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hani, al-Isyafi, al-Athram al-Tai, one of the prominent figures, author of 'al-Sunan', and student of Imam Ahmad. He was born in the era of al-Rashid. Abu Bakr al-Khallal said: 'Al-Athram was great in rank, a hafiz. And when Asim ibn Ali came to Baghdad, he sought a man to produce benefits for him to dictate, and he found at that time no one other than Abu Bakr.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index (Fihris al-A'lam) from the end of the book. It provides brief biographies of scholars cited in the main text. The entries include birth, death, teachers, students, and notable works. The first entry is for Abu Umar ibn Abd al-Barr, a renowned Maliki hadith scholar from Andalusia. The second is Abu al-Mahasin al-Ruyani, a Shafi'i jurist who was killed by Ismailis. The third is a cross-reference to Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni. The fourth is Abu al-Muzaffar al-Sam'ani, a Hanafi-turned-Shafi'i scholar with many works. The fifth is al-Athram, a student of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. This index serves as a reference for the scholars mentioned earlier in the work on usul al-ifta. It is typical for classical texts to include such biographical dictionaries to establish the credibility and chains of transmission of the scholars quoted.

Key Terms
ابن عبد البر (Ibn Abd al-Barr): Abu Umar Yusuf ibn Abd al-Barr al-Qurtubi, a prominent Maliki hadith scholar and historian from Andalusia (d. 463 AH).
الروياني (al-Ruyani): Abu al-Mahasin Abd al-Wahid al-Ruyani, a Shafi'i jurist known for his work 'al-Bahr' in the Shafi'i madhhab (d. 501 AH).
السمعاني (al-Sam'ani): Abu al-Muzaffar Mansur al-Sam'ani, initially Hanafi later Shafi'i, a scholar from Marw known for his works in usul and kalam (d. 489 AH).
الأثرم (al-Athram): Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Hani al-Athram, a student of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal and author of 'al-Sunan' (d. 3rd century AH).

A biographical index provides essential credentials of cited scholars, enabling the mufti to assess the authority and relevance of their opinions in Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Life of the Author
intermediate
6 min
Parsing Biographical Entries in Fatwa Works
Biographical sketches of Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the madhhab affiliation, teacher-student links, and key works from a scholar's biography and explain their relevance to the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
A scholar's madhhab and teacher chain determine the authority of their transmitted opinions in fatwa.

Biographical entries in classical fatwa manuals are not mere historical notes. They provide crucial data for evaluating the reliability of transmitted opinions. In the Hanafi tradition, knowing a scholar's madhhab, whether they were a mujtahid, and their chain of transmission helps the mufti assign appropriate weight to their rulings. This lesson guides you through parsing such entries from the work on the etiquette of fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Extract the full name and nisbah
Identify the scholar's complete name, including lineage and geographical nisbah (e.g., al-Marwazi, al-Baghdadi). This helps place the scholar in time and region.
Nisbah often indicates the school or region of influence.
2
Determine madhhab affiliation
Look for explicit statements like 'al-Hanafi' or 'al-Shafi'i'. Note any changes (e.g., 'first Hanafi then Shafi'i'). This is critical for assigning the scholar's opinions to the correct madhhab hierarchy.
A scholar may have studied under multiple schools; the final affiliation matters most for fatwa.
3
Identify teachers and students
List the names of teachers (e.g., 'talmidh al-Imam Ahmad') and notable students. This establishes the transmission chain (sanad) for rulings.
Direct transmission from a major imam enhances the authority of a transmitted opinion.
4
List key works
Take note of the book titles mentioned. They indicate the scholar's specialization (e.g., 'al-Sunan' for hadith, 'al-Burhan' for khilaf).
Works may be used as sources for fatwa; their presence signals the scholar's contribution.
5
Assess the scholar's status and relevance to Hanafi fatwa
Ask: Is the opinion of this scholar part of the Hanafi corpus? Is he cited in later Hanafi works? Scholars like al-Athram (Hanbali) are not Hanafi authorities, whereas al-Sam'ani (who turned Shafi'i) may still be cited for khilaf. Ahmad ibn Hanbal is the founder of the Hanbali school.
Biographical parsing helps avoid mixing madhabs in fatwa compilation.

٢٢- أحمد بن حنبل : هو أبو عبد الله ، أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل الذهلي، الشيباني، المروزى ثم البغدادي، أحد الأئمة الأعلام. قال ابن ذريح العكبرى : طلبت أحمد بن حنبل فسلمت عليه، وكان شيخا مخضوبا طوالا أسمر شديد السمرة" . وعن محمد بن عباس النحوى ، قال : رأيت أحمد بن حنبل حسن الوجه، ربعة يخضب بالحناء خضابا ليس بالقاني، في لحيته شعرات سود، ورأيت ثيابه غلاظا بيضا، ورأيته معتماً وعليه إزار . وحفظه قوى جدا . قال ابن أبي حاتم : قال سعيد ابن عمرو : يا أبا زرعة أأنت أحفظ، أم أحمد ؟ قال : بل أحمد . قلت : كيف علمت؟ قال : وجدت كتبه ليس في أوائل الأجزاء أسماء الذين حدثوه. فكان يحفظ كل جزء ممن سمعه، وأن لا أقدر على هذا . قال إبراهيم الحربي: "رأيت أبا عبد الله ، كأن الله جمع له علم الأولين والآخرين". فعدة شيوخه الذين روى عنهم في "المسند" مائتان وثمانون ونيف. قال أبو داود : سمعت يعقوب الدورقى يقول : سمعت أحمد يقول : ولدت في شهر ربيع الأول سنة أربع وستين ومائة" . توفي رحمه الله سنة ٢٤١هـ . (Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 6/473) 21. al-Athram: The Imam, the scholar, Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hani, al-Iskaafi, al-Athram al-Ta'i, one of the prominent figures, author of 'al-Sunan', and student of Imam Ahmad. He was born in the era of al-Rashid. Abu Bakr al-Khallal said: 'Al-Athram was of great status, a memorizer. When Asim ibn Ali came to Baghdad, he sought a man to bring out benefits for him to dictate, but he did not find at that time anyone other than Abu Bakr al-Athram. It was as if when he saw him, he was not impressed due to his young age.' Abu Bakr said: 'Bring out your books,' and he began saying to him: 'This hadith is wrong, this is an error, this is such.' He said: Asim ibn Ali was pleased with him and dictated nearly fifty sessions. He knew hadith and memorized. When he accompanied Ahmad ibn Hanbal, he left that and turned to the madhhab of Ahmad. He died in 260 AH. (al-Kashif 1/27, Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 2/570, 570, Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 10/420) 22. Ahmad ibn Hanbal: He is Abu Abd Allah, Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal al-Dhuhli, al-Shaybani, al-Marwazi then al-Baghdadi, one of the eminent imams. Ibn Dhurayh al-'Ukbari said: 'I sought Ahmad ibn Hanbal and greeted him. He was an old man with dyed hair, tall, dark-skinned, very dark.' And from Muhammad ibn Abbas al-Nahwi, he said: 'I saw Ahmad ibn Hanbal with a handsome face, of medium stature, dyeing with henna, not deep red, with some black hairs in his beard. I saw his clothes coarse and white, and I saw him wearing a turban and a loincloth.' His memory was very strong. Ibn Abi Hatim said: Said ibn Amr said: 'O Abu Zur'a, are you more memorizing or Ahmad?' He said: 'Rather Ahmad.' I said: 'How did you know?' He said: 'I found his books without the names of those who narrated to him at the beginnings of the parts. So he would memorize every part from whom he heard it, and I cannot do that.' Ibrahim al-Harbi said: 'I saw Abu Abd Allah, as if Allah had gathered for him the knowledge of the first and the last.' The number of his shaykhs he narrated from in 'al-Musnad' is two hundred and eighty and more. Abu Dawud said: I heard Ya'qub al-Dawraqi say: I heard Ahmad say: 'I was born in Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 164 AH.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in 241 AH. (Summarized from Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 9/434) 23. al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq: He is Abu Ishaq Rukn al-Din Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Isfarayini. He swam in the seas of sciences, challenging its waves, and journeyed through the nights of understandings, enduring its night journeys. He possessed shar'i, rational, and linguistic sciences, and was in the habit of ijtihad and piety... He stayed in Iraq for a time, then chose his homeland, so he returned to Isfarayin, and the people of Nishapur visited him.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index (fihris al-a'lam) from a work on the etiquette of fatwa. It provides concise biographies of key scholars, highlighting their madhhab affiliation, teachers, works, and historical context. For a student of ifta', knowing the scholarly lineage and reliability of narrators is essential for evaluating the strength of transmitted rulings. The entries include both Hanafi and Shafi'i figures, emphasizing the interconnectedness of the madhahib.

Key Terms
فهرس الأعلام (Fihris al-A'lam): Index of notable personalities, specifically scholars mentioned in the book
السمعاني (al-Sam'ani): A scholar first Hanafi then Shafi'i, known for works on usul and khilaf
الأثرم (al-Athram): A Hanbali scholar, student of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, author of 'al-Sunan'
أحمد بن حنبل (Ahmad ibn Hanbal): Founder of the Hanbali madhhab, renowned hadith memorizer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biographical details are not decorative; they directly impact the authority and classification of transmitted rulings in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal: A Biographical Sketch from a Hanafi Fatwa Manual
Biographical entry of the Hanbali imam from a Hanafi fatwa etiquette manual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical data from a classical entry and explain why a Hanafi fatwa manual includes a non-Hanafi imam.

Core Idea
Imam Ahmad's scholarly stature is acknowledged across madhhabs, highlighting the Hanafi tradition's respect for authenticated knowledge.

This passage introduces Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal (d. 241/855), the eponym of the Hanbali school, from a Hanafi work on the 'Adab al-Fatwa' (etiquette of issuing fatwas). Though not a Hanafi, his authority in hadith and his rigorous methodology are recognized even in Hanafi contexts. Understanding his credentials helps a mufti appreciate the source of hadith transmissions that may cross madhhab lines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and his full lineage
Read the opening lines to find Imam Ahmad's complete name and tribal affiliations. Note the toponymic links: al-Marwazi then al-Baghdadi.
His nisbah 'al-Shaybani' is Arab tribal affiliation.
2
Extract physical description and character
Find details about his appearance, dress, and demeanor. This helps assess his reliability in transmitting knowledge through sight and character.
The description includes his height, dye use, and coarse white clothes.
3
Analyze the evidence for his strong memory
Study the anecdote about his books lacking narrator names, which indicates he memorized each part directly from the teacher. This is a key indicator of his 'dabt' (accuracy) in hadith.
This attribute is crucial for evaluating the authenticity of his narrated hadith.
4
Note the scope of his teachers and his magnum opus
Identify the number of shaykhs he narrated from in 'al-Musnad' and the total number of hadith it contains. This shows his prodigious output.
280+ teachers indicates broad exposure to hadith across the Islamic world.
5
Record his birth and death years
Memorize the dates given: born in 164 AH, died in 241 AH. This places him as a contemporary of the earlier Hanafi masters (e.g., Abu Yusuf d. 182).
The year 241 corresponds to 855 CE.

٢٢- أحمد بن حنبل : هو أبو عبد الله ، أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل الذهلي، الشيباني، المروزى ثم البغدادي، أحد الأئمة الأعلام. قال ابن ذريح العكبرى : طلبت أحمد بن حنبل فسلمت عليه، وكان شيخا مخضوبا طوالا أسمر شديد السمرة" . وعن محمد بن عباس النحوى ، قال : رأيت أحمد بن حنبل حسن الوجه، ربعة يخضب بالحناء خضابا ليس بالقاني، في لحيته شعرات سود، ورأيت ثيابه غلاظا بيضا، ورأيته معتماً وعليه إزار . وحفظه قوى جدا . قال ابن أبي حاتم : قال سعيد ابن عمرو : يا أبا زرعة أأنت أحفظ، أم أحمد ؟ قال : بل أحمد . قلت : كيف علمت؟ قال : وجدت كتبه ليس في أوائل الأجزاء أسماء الذين حدثوه. فكان يحفظ كل جزء ممن سمعه، وأن لا أقدر على هذا . قال إبراهيم الحربي: "رأيت أبا عبد الله ، كأن الله جمع له علم الأولين والآخرين". فعدة شيوخه الذين روى عنهم في "المسند" مائتان وثمانون ونيف. قال أبو داود : سمعت يعقوب الدورقى يقول : سمعت أحمد يقول : ولدت في شهر ربيع الأول سنة أربع وستين ومائة" . توفي رحمه الله سنة ٢٤١هـ . 22- Ahmad bin Hanbal: He is Abu Abdullah, Ahmad bin Muhammad bin Hanbal al-Dhuhli, al-Shaybani, al-Marwazi then al-Baghdadi, one of the great imams. Ibn Dhurayh al-‘Ukbari said: I sought Ahmad bin Hanbal and greeted him, and he was an old man with dyed beard, tall, dark with deep darkness. And from Muhammad bin ‘Abbas al-Nahwi, he said: I saw Ahmad bin Hanbal with a handsome face, of medium height, he dyes with henna a dye not bright red, in his beard there are black hairs, and I saw his clothes coarse white, and I saw him wearing a turban and an izār. And his memory was very strong. Ibn Abi Hatim said: Sa‘id bin ‘Amr said: O Abu Zur‘a, are you more retentive, or Ahmad? He said: Rather Ahmad. I said: How did you know? He said: I found his books, there are not at the beginnings of the parts the names of those who narrated to him. So he used to memorize every part from whom he heard it, and I cannot do that. Ibrahim al-Harbi said: I saw Abu Abdullah, as if Allah had gathered for him the knowledge of the first and the last. The number of his shaykhs from whom he narrated in the Musnad is two hundred and eighty and some. Abu Dawud said: I heard Ya‘qub al-Dawraqi say: I heard Ahmad say: I was born in Rabi‘ al-Awwal in the year one hundred and sixty-four. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 241 AH. (Summarized from Siyar A‘lam al-Nubala’ 9/434).
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the founder of the Hanbali school. The passage describes his physical appearance, his exceptional memory, and the number of his teachers. It emphasizes that his books did not list the names of his narrators at the beginnings of parts, indicating he remembered directly from whom he heard each hadith. His birth year is given as 164 AH and death as 241 AH. This biography is sourced from Siyar A‘lam al-Nubala’.

Key Terms
المسند (al-Musnad): The collection of hadith compiled by Imam Ahmad, containing approximately 30,000 hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Biography of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini
Biographical entry of a Shafi'i scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly contributions and timeline of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, and explain his relevance to the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A Shafi'i polymath whose life exemplifies the rich scholarly exchange between madhhabs in the 5th century AH.

This biographical entry introduces Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, a towering Shafi'i scholar whose breadth across legal, theological, and linguistic sciences earned him the title 'al-Ustadh'. His life illustrates the vibrant academic culture of the early Islamic centuries and his interactions with Hanafi circles highlight the respectful coexistence of madhhabs. Understanding such figures enriches a mufti's appreciation of the broader scholarly landscape.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and titles
The text gives his full name: Abu Ishaq Rukn al-Din Ibrahim bin Muhammad al-Isfarayini. Note the honorific 'al-Ustadh' (the master) and 'Rukn al-Din' (pillar of the religion).
Full names often include place-based nisbahs; here 'al-Isfarayini' indicates his origin from Isfarayin.
2
Note his areas of expertise
The biography states he was a 'possession of the legal, intellectual and linguistic sciences' and also practiced ijtihad in habit and piety. This indicates mastery in fiqh, kalam, and Arabic language.
His expertise in both aqli (rational) and naqli (transmitted) sciences was rare.
3
Trace his geographical movements
He initially stayed in Iraq, then returned to his homeland Isfarayin, and later accepted an invitation to Nishapur where a school was built for him.
These movements show the mobility of scholars and the patronage of learning.
4
Recognize the significance of the school
The school built for him in Nishapur was described as unparalleled in size or magnificence. This indicates his high status and the importance of educational institutions.
Such schools were early examples of organized madrasas that later became common.
5
Note his death date and burial
He died on Ashura (10th of Muharram) in the year 418 AH. His body was carried from Nishapur to his hometown Isfarayin for burial.
Death dates help in establishing a scholar's period and possible interactions with other scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٣ - الأستاذ أبو إسحاق : هو أبو إسحاق ركن الدين إبراهيم بن محمد الأسفراييني، سبح في بحار العلوم معاندا ،أمواجها ، وسرى في ليالي الفهوم مكابداً إدلاجها صاحب للعلوم الشرعية والعقلية واللغوية، والاجتهاد في العادة والورع .. أقام بالعراق مدة ثم اختار وطنه، فرجع إلى أسفرايين فدخل عليه أهل نيسابور في الانتقال إليهم، فأجابهم، وبنوا له مدرسة عظيمة ، لم يبن قبلها بنيسابور مثلها، فلزمها إلى أن توفى يوم عاشوراء سنة ثمان عشرة وأربعمائة . وحمل منها إلى بلده، فدفن بها . طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٥٩/١)
23- Al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq: He is Abu Ishaq Rukn al-Din Ibrahim bin Muhammad al-Isfarayini. He swam in the seas of sciences, resisting its waves, and traveled in the nights of understandings, striving in its journeys; possessor of the legal, intellectual and linguistic sciences, and ijtihad in habit and piety. He stayed in Iraq for a time, then chose his homeland, so he returned to Isfarayin. The people of Naysabur came to him to move to them, so he answered them, and they built for him a great school, the likes of which had not been built before in Naysabur. He adhered to it until he died on the day of Ashura in the year 418 AH. He was carried from there to his town and buried there. (Tabaqat al-Shafi‘iyya by al-Isnawi 1/59).
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This entry introduces Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, a Shafi'i scholar of the 5th century AH. He was proficient in many fields: Islamic law, theology, and language. He initially stayed in Iraq and then returned to his hometown, after which the people of Naysabur requested him to teach there. They built a school for him, which was unparalleled. He lived there until his death in 418 AH.

Key Terms
الأستاذ (al-Ustadh): A title meaning 'the master', given to Abu Ishaq indicating his high scholarly rank.
ركن الدين (Rukn al-Din): A title meaning 'Pillar of the Religion', indicating his role in supporting Islamic scholarship.
أسفرايين (Isfarayin): A town in northeastern Iran, his birthplace and burial place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 418 AH
B) 419 AH
C) 408 AH
D) 428 AH

Key Takeaway
Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini was a Shafi'i polymath whose life and works are a testament to the depth of classical Islamic scholarship, valuable for any mufti to appreciate the breadth of the tradition.

Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni: The Leading Shafi'i Scholar and His Legacy
Biographical entry of the leading Shafi'i theologian and jurist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to summarize the key events of Imam al-Haramayn's life and identify his major works and their significance in Hanafi iftaa context.

Core Idea
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was a Shafi'i giant whose scholarly rigor and works influenced later Hanafi usul and iftaa.

Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni is a towering figure in Shafi'i fiqh and usul, but his works, especially al-Nihaya, are often cited in Hanafi scholarly discourse. Understanding his biography helps contextualize the inter-madhhab debates and the transmission of knowledge. This lesson covers his life, travels, and major contributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify his full name and birth details
Note his name: Diya' al-Din Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Malik al-Juwayni, born on 18 Muharram 419 AH.
The title 'Imam al-Haramayn' (Imam of the Two Sanctuaries) is a famous honorific.
2
Trace his educational journey
He studied fiqh with his father, usul with Abu al-Qasim al-Isfahani. After his father's death, he was seated in his place for teaching.
This shows his early scholarly recognition.
3
Follow his travels
He left Naysabur due to fitna between Mu'tazila and Ash'aris, traveled to Baghdad, Isfahan, then to Hijaz (Mecca) where he stayed four years, compiling al-Nihaya.
His travels were partly forced by political-religious conflicts.
4
Note his return and institutional role
Back in Naysabur, the Nizamiyya madrasa was built for him; he taught, gave khutba, and oversaw endowments.
His return marks the stabilization of his reputation.
5
List his major works
Al-Nihaya (usul/fiqh), a large tafsir, al-Furuq, al-Silsila, al-Tabsira, Mukhtasar al-Mukhtasar, and a work on imam and ma'mum.
These works are references in Shafi'i and Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤ - إمام الحرمين : ضياء الدين أبو المعالي عبد الملك إمام الحرمين ابن الشيخ أبي محمد الجويني، إمام الأئمة في زمانه، وأعجوبة دهره وأوانه، وفى أئمة خراسان بمنزلة أنسان العين من الإنسان، إن عرضت الشبهات أذهب جوهر ذهنه ما عرض، أو تعارضت المشكلات فوض إليها سهم فكره فأصاب ،الغرض، ولد في ثامن عشر المحرم سنة تسع عشرة وأربع مائة ، وقرأ الفقه على والده، والأصول على أبي القاسم الإسكاف تلميذ الأسفراييني، وتوفى والده وله نحو عشرين سنة، فأقعده الأئمة في مكانه. للتدريس، وخرج من نيسابور لما وقعت الفتن بين المعتزلة والأشاعرة، فظهرت المعتزلة فأقام ببغداد تارة وبأصبهان تارة وغيرهما من الأماكن ، ثم خرج إلى الحجاز فجاور بمكة أربع سنين ، يدرس ويفتى ويجمع "النهاية هناك، ثم عاد إلى نيسابور عند استقامة الأمور، فبنيت له نظاميتها وفوض إليه التدريس بها، والخطابة بالجامع المعروف به المنيعي" ، ومجلس الوعظ وأمور الأوقاف، وعظم شأنه عند الملوك واجتمع المستفيدون عليه . وكان إماماً في التفسير والفقه والأدب، مجتهداً في العبادة، ورعاً مهيبا، صاحب جد ووقار . قال شيخ الإسلام أبو عثمان الصابوني : لو كان الشيخ أبو محمد في بني إسرائيل لنقلت إلينا أوصافه وافتخروا به " ونقل النووى في الطبقات عن الشيخ أبي سعد عبد الواحد بن القشيري صاحب الرسالة : إن المحققين من أصحابنا يعتقدون فيه من الكمال أنه لو جاز أن يبعث الله تعالى نبيا فى عصره لما كان إلا هو " . صنف رحمه الله تفسيراً كبيراً يشتمل على عشرة أنواع من العلوم في كل آية، وتعليقا في الفقه متوسطا، وعندى من تصانيفه : "الفروق" و"السلسلة" و "التبصرة" و " مختصر المختصر" وتصنيفه في "موقف الإمام والمأموم" .
24- Imam al-Haramayn: Diya' al-Din Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Malik Imam al-Haramayn Ibn al-Shaykh Abi Muhammad al-Juwayni, the imam of imams in his time, the marvel of his age and time. Among the imams of Khurasan, he was like the pupil of the eye. If doubts arose, the essence of his mind would remove them; if difficulties conflicted, he would shoot the arrow of his thought and hit the target. He was born on the 18th of Muharram in the year 419 AH. He studied fiqh with his father and usul with Abu al-Qasim al-Isfahani, a student of al-Isfarayini. His father died when he was about twenty years old, so the imams seated him in his place for teaching. He left Naysabur when a fitna occurred between the Mu'tazila and the Ash'aris; the Mu'tazila prevailed, so he stayed in Baghdad sometimes and Isfahan sometimes and other places. Then he went to the Hijaz and stayed in Mecca for four years, teaching, giving fatwa, and compiling al-Nihaya there. Then he returned to Naysabur when conditions stabilized, and the Nizamiyya was built for him and he was entrusted with teaching in it, and the khutba in the famous al-Manī‘ī mosque, and the council of admonition and affairs of endowments. His status became great with the kings, and students gathered around him. He was an imam in tafsir, fiqh, and adab, diligent in worship, pious, awe-inspiring, possessed of seriousness and dignity. Shaykh al-Islam Abu 'Uthman al-Sabuni said: 'If Shaykh Abu Muhammad had been among the Children of Israel, his descriptions would have been transmitted to us and they would have boasted of him.' And al-Nawawi transmitted in al-Tabaqat from Shaykh Abu Sa'd 'Abd al-Wahid bin al-Qushayri, author of al-Risala: 'The verifying scholars among our companions believe of him such perfection that if it were permissible for Allah to send a prophet in his time, it would be none other than him.' He authored, may Allah have mercy on him, a great tafsir containing ten types of sciences in every verse, and a medium commentary on fiqh, and among his works I have: al-Furuq, al-Silsila, al-Tabsira, Mukhtasar al-Mukhtasar, and his work on 'The Position of the Imam and the Ma'mum'.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This biography covers the life of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, a towering figure in the Shafi'i school. Born in 419 AH, he studied under his father and then under Abu al-Qasim al-Isfahani. He faced persecution from the Mu'tazila and traveled to Baghdad, Isfahan, and the Hijaz. The Nizamiyya madrasa was built for him in Naysabur. His students included many scholars, and he was praised highly. He authored many works, including a large tafsir and the book al-Nihaya. His students considered him of such rank that he would have been a prophet if prophethood were possible after the Prophet Muhammad.

Key Terms
النهاية (al-Nihaya): A major work of Shafi'i fiqh and usul by Imam al-Haramayn.
إمام الحرمين (Imam al-Haramayn): Title meaning 'Imam of the Two Sanctuaries' (Mecca and Medina).
الجويني (al-Juwayni): Nisba referring to the town of Juwayn in Khurasan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where did Imam al-Haramayn compile his work al-Nihaya?
A) Baghdad
B) Naysabur
C) Mecca
D) Isfahan

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was a master of multiple Islamic sciences, and his works, especially al-Nihaya, remain influential in usul discourse across madhahib.

Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni: A Biographical Anchor for Rasm al-Mufti
Biographical entry of a Shafi'i usul scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recall the key life events of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and explain why his biography is studied in the Hanafi rasm al-mufti tradition.

Core Idea
Biographies of major usul scholars like al-Juwayni provide context for the authority and methodology of fatwa works.

Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni was a towering Shafi'i jurist and usuli scholar whose works, though from another madhhab, are integral to the Hanafi fatwa tradition because of their methodological rigor. This lesson presents his life story as recorded in classical biographical sources, highlighting aspects that shaped his contributions to usul al-fiqh and fatwa issuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of the biography
Read the passage and note the key phases of al-Juwayni's life: birth, education, travels, return to Nishapur, teaching, and death. These phases are relevant to understanding his scholarly formation.
Focus on why a Shafi'i scholar is studied in Hanafi rasm al-mufti texts.
2
Extract his major teachers and students
List the scholars he learned from (his father, Abu al-Qasim al-Iskaaf) and note that he taught at the Nizamiyya. This shows his transmission chain.
Indirectly relates to the Hanafi concept of sanad.
3
Analyze his scholarly output
Identify the works mentioned: al-Nihaya, a large tafsir, and other titles. Consider their relevance to usul and fatwa.
Al-Nihaya is a major Shafi'i fiqh reference; knowing its author aids cross-madhhab understanding.
4
Reflect on personal qualities and trials
Note his piety, humility, and the Mu'tazila-Ash'ari conflict. These circumstances influenced his intellectual development and authority.
Traits like piety and humility are valued in muftis; his trials show resilience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤ - إمام الحرمين : ضياء الدين أبو المعالي عبد الملك إمام الحرمين ابن الشيخ أبي محمد الجويني، إمام الأئمة في زمانه، وأعجوبة دهره وأوانه، وفى أئمة خراسان بمنزلة أنسان العين من الإنسان، إن عرضت الشبهات أذهب جوهر ذهنه ما عرض، أو تعارضت المشكلات فوض إليها سهم فكره فأصاب الغرض، ولد في ثامن عشر المحرم سنة تسع عشرة وأربع مائة ، وقرأ الفقه على والده، والأصول على أبي القاسم الإسكاف تلميذ الأسفراييني، وتوفى والده وله نحو عشرين سنة، فأقعده الأئمة في مكانه. للتدريس، وخرج من نيسابور لما وقعت الفتن بين المعتزلة والأشاعرة، فظهرت المعتزلة فأقام ببغداد تارة وبأصبهان تارة وغيرهما من الأماكن ، ثم خرج إلى الحجاز فجاور بمكة أربع سنين ، يدرس ويفتى ويجمع "النهاية هناك، ثم عاد إلى نيسابور عند استقامة الأمور، فبنيت له نظاميتها وفوض إليه التدريس بها، والخطابة بالجامع المعروف به المنيعي" ، ومجلس الوعظ وأمور الأوقاف، وعظم شأنه عند الملوك واجتمع المستفيدون عليه . وكان إماماً في التفسير والفقه والأدب، مجتهداً في العبادة، ورعاً مهيبا، صاحب جد ووقار . قال شيخ الإسلام أبو عثمان الصابوني : لو كان الشيخ أبو محمد في بني إسرائيل لنقلت إلينا أوصافه وافتخروا به " ونقل النووى في الطبقات عن الشيخ أبي سعد عبد الواحد بن القشيري صاحب الرسالة : إن المحققين من أصحابنا يعتقدون فيه من الكمال أنه لو جاز أن يبعث الله تعالى نبيا فى عصره لما كان إلا هو " . صنف رحمه الله تفسيراً كبيراً يشتمل على عشرة أنواع من العلوم في كل آية، وتعليقا في الفقه متوسطا، وعندى من تصانيفه : "الفروق" و"السلسلة" و "التبصرة" و " مختصر المختصر" وتصنيفه في "موقف الإمام والمأموم" . وكان رحمه الله متواضعاً جداً بحيث يتخيل جليسه أنه يستهزئ به، رقيق القلب بحيث يبكي إذا سمع بيتا أو تفكر فى نفسه، أو خاض في علوم الصوفية وأرباب الأحوال، وبقى على ما ذكرناه قريباً من ثلاثين سنة إلى أن مرض باليرقان، وبقى به أياماً وبرئ منه، وعاد إلى الدرس والمجلس، وحصل السرور للخواص والعوام، فلم يكن إلا يسيراً حتى عاوده المرض وغلبت عليه الحرارة، فحمل فى محقة إلى قرية من قرى نيسابور، لاعتدال هوائها وخفة مائها، فتوفى بها ليلة الأربعاء بعد صلاة العشاء، الخامس والعشرين من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة ثمان وسبعين وأربع مائة عن تسع وخمسين سنة . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٤٠٩/١-٤١٢)
24 – Imam al-Haramayn: Diya' al-Din Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Malik, Imam al-Haramayn, son of Shaykh Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni. He was the imam of imams in his time, the wonder of his age and era. Among the imams of Khurasan he was like the pupil of the eye to a person. If doubts arose, the essence of his mind would remove what appeared; if problems conflicted, the arrow of his thought would be entrusted to them and hit the target. He was born on the 18th of Muharram 419 AH. He studied fiqh under his father and usul under Abu al-Qasim al-Iskaaf, a student of al-Isfarayini. His father died when he was about twenty years old, so the imams seated him in his place for teaching. He left Nishapur when conflict occurred between the Mu'tazila and Ash'ariyya; the Mu'tazila prevailed, so he stayed sometimes in Baghdad, sometimes in Isfahan, and other places. Then he went to the Hijaz and resided in Mecca for four years, teaching, giving fatwas, and compiling 'al-Nihaya' there. Then he returned to Nishapur when matters settled. The Nizamiyya was built for him, and he was entrusted with teaching there, delivering sermons at the mosque known as al-Mani'i, the preaching council, and the affairs of endowments. His status became great with kings, and seekers of knowledge gathered around him. He was an imam in tafsir, fiqh, and literature, diligent in worship, pious, awe-inspiring, serious and dignified. Shaykh al-Islam Abu 'Uthman al-Sabuni said: 'If Shaykh Abu Muhammad had been among the Children of Israel, his qualities would have been transmitted to us and they would have boasted of him.' Al-Nawawi narrated in al-Tabaqat from Shaykh Abu Sa'd 'Abd al-Wahid ibn al-Qushayri, author of al-Risala: 'The verifying scholars among our companions believe about his perfection that if it were permissible for Allah to send a prophet in his era, no one else would be suitable.' He authored, may Allah have mercy on him, a great tafsir containing ten types of sciences in each verse, a medium-length commentary on fiqh, and among his works I have: 'al-Furuq', 'al-Silsila', 'al-Tabsira', 'Mukhtasar al-Mukhtasar', and his work on 'Mawqif al-Imam wa al-Ma'mum'. He was, may Allah have mercy on him, extremely humble to the point that his companion would imagine he was mocking him, tender-hearted so that he would weep if he heard a verse or reflected on himself, or when he delved into the sciences of the Sufis and people of spiritual states. He remained as described for nearly thirty years until he fell ill with jaundice, suffered for days, then recovered and returned to teaching and the council, bringing joy to elites and commoners. But not long after, his illness returned and fever overcame him, so he was carried in a litter to a village of Nishapur for its moderate climate and light water, and he died there on Wednesday night after Isha prayer, the 25th of Rabi' al-Akhir 478 AH, at the age of fifty-nine. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi: 1/409-412)
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This is a biographical entry from al-Nawawi's 'Adab al-Fatwa', a work on the ethics and methodology of issuing fatwas. Although al-Nawawi and al-Juwayni are Shafi'i scholars, their works are studied in Hanafi circles for their contributions to usul al-fiqh and fatwa methodology. This passage provides a comprehensive life account of Imam al-Haramayn, emphasizing his scholarly lineage, his trials during the Mu'tazila-Ash'ari conflict, his teaching at the Nizamiyya, his voluminous authorship, and his personal piety and humility. The text highlights his mastery in tafsir, fiqh, and literature, and quotes two eminent scholars praising him. For a student of rasm al-mufti, such biographical details contextualize the authority of the scholars whose works form part of the tradition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When he was about 10

C) When he was about 30
D) When he was about 40

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni's biography exemplifies the ideal mufti: scholarly mastery, piety, resilience, and humility, making his works authoritative references even in Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Core Idea

Biography of Hasan al-Basri: A Key Tabi'i Scholar
Concise biographical entry from al-Kashif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Hasan al-Basri and explain his significance in the early Islamic scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Hasan al-Basri was a preeminent tabi'i scholar whose life bridged the Companions and the formation of madhhabs.

Hasan al-Basri is one of the most important figures in early Islamic history, revered for his knowledge and piety. This biographical entry from al-Dhahabi's al-Kashif gives us the essential facts about his life, which are foundational for understanding the transmission of knowledge from the Companions to later generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the name and lineage
State the full name 'al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Basri' and note his patronymic titles such as 'Imam Abu Sa'id'. Recognize the different accounts of his status as a freed slave.
His father's name was Yasar, a captive from Maysan.
2
Note the time of birth and early life
Record that he was born during the caliphate of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him), which places him in the early generation of the tabi'un.
This timing means he likely met many senior Companions.
3
List his teachers and students
Identify the Companions he narrated from: 'Imran ibn Husayn, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Ibn 'Abbas, and Jundab. Also note his students: Ibn 'Awn, Yunus, and others.
These chains link him directly to the Prophet's Companions.
4
Determine his scholarly stature
Observe the description: 'He was of great stature, high renown, a leader in knowledge and action.' This indicates his authority and influence.
His reputation as a scholar-activist is widely acknowledged.
5
Memorize the year of death
The text states he died in Rajab of the year 110 AH. This is a standard date in biographical works.
Knowing death dates helps in evaluating hadith chains and scholarly connections.

٢٥- الحسن البصري : هو الحسن بن أبي الحسن البصري، الإمام أبو سعيد مولى زید بن ثابت وقيل : مولى جميل بن قطبة . وقيل : غير ذلك، وأبوه يسار من سبى ميسان، أعتقه الربيع بنت النضر ، ولد الحسن زمن عمر، وروى عن عمران بن حصين وأبي موسى وابن عباس وجندب، وعنه ابن عون، ويونس وأم، كان كبير الشأن، رفيع الذكر، رأسا في العلم والعمل، مات في رجب سنة عشر ومائة . ( الكاشف : ١ / ٢٢٠)
25- Hasan al-Basri: He is al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Basri, the Imam Abu Sa'id, freed slave of Zayd ibn Thabit, and it is said: freed slave of Jamil ibn Qutba, and it is said: other than that. His father Yasar was from the captives of Maysan, freed by al-Rabi' bint al-Nadr. Hasan was born in the time of 'Umar. He narrated from 'Imran ibn Husayn, Abu Musa, Ibn 'Abbas, and Jundab. Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Hasan al-Basri, a famous tabi'i and early Islamic scholar. The text provides his lineage, his status as a freed slave of Zayd ibn Thabit or others, his birth during the caliphate of 'Umar, his teachers and students, and his death in 110 AH. His reputation as a leader in both knowledge and practice underscores his importance in the early Islamic scholarly tradition. This biography is taken from al-Kashif, a work by al-Dhahabi.

Key Terms
الحسن البصري (al-Hasan al-Basri): A renowned tabi'i and early Islamic scholar from Basra, known for his asceticism and oratory.
التابعي (al-tabi'i): A Muslim who met the Companions of the Prophet Muhammad but did not meet the Prophet himself.

Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi: A Biographical Sketch
Biographical entry on al-Khatib al-Baghdadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholarly contributions of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and explain their relevance to the Hanafi tradition of iftaa.

Core Idea
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's works are essential references for Hanafi muftis despite his Shafi'i affiliation.

Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi is a towering figure in hadith and history. Although he was a Shafi'i jurist, his works—especially 'Tarikh Baghdad' and 'al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih'—are frequently cited in Hanafi fatwa literature. This lesson introduces his biography and explains why his contributions matter for usul al-iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and key attributes
Locate the name, epithets (al-Khatib, al-Hafiz), birth year, and his madhhab affiliation from the text.
Note the Shafi'i madhhab: this affects how later Hanafis evaluate his narrations.
2

From the text, list 'Tarikh Baghdad' and 'Kitab al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih'. Consider why each is important for iftaa.
'Al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih' is a foundational work in usul al-fiqh and adab al-mufti.
3
Understand his scholarly authority
Note the praise: 'thiqah, hujjah, khatama bihi al-huffaz'. This indicates his reliability in hadith, relevant for Hanafi acceptance of his transmissions.
Hanafi scholars often rely on his hadith criticism in works like al-Hidayah.
4
Connect his charitable acts to scholarly integrity
His endowment of books and charity reinforce his trustworthiness, a key criterion for accepting narrations in Hanafi usul.
The text explicitly mentions he stopped his books for Muslims.

Although Shafi'i, his works are used by Hanafi muftis. Reflect on inter-madhhab borrowing in iftaa.
This exemplifies the principle of taking sound knowledge from any reliable source.

٢٦- الخطيب : هو أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت البغدادي الخطيب الحافظ، أحد أئمة الأعلام وصاحب التأليفات الكثيرة، ولد عام ٣٩٢هـ، تفقه على مذهب الشافعي، وكان مهيباً، وفوراً، ثقة، حجة ، حسن الخط، كثير الضبط، فصيحاً، ختم به الحفاظ، وكان حسن القراءة والصوت ومن مؤلفاته: "تاريخ بغداد" الذي لم يصنف مثله ، و "كتاب الفقيه والمتفقه " . وكان قد تصدق بجميع ماله على العلماء والفقراء، وأوصى أن يتصدق بثيابه ووقف كتبه على المسلمين ولم يكن له عقب . (شذرات الذهب : ۳۱۱/۳-۳۱۲ ، والأعلام للزركلي : ١٦٦/١)
26- Al-Khatib: He is Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Baghdadi al-Khatib al-Hafiz, one of the leading imams and author of many works. He was born in 392 AH. He studied fiqh according to the Shafi'i school. He was majestic, learned, trustworthy, authoritative, had beautiful handwriting, was very precise, eloquent. The hadith memorizers ended with him. He had a beautiful recitation and voice. Among his works are 'Tarikh Baghdad', which has no peer, and 'Kitab al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih'. He gave away all his wealth to scholars and the poor, and willed that his clothes be given in charity and his books be endowed for Muslims. He had no offspring. (Shadharat al-Dhahab: 3/311-312, and al-A'lam by al-Zirikli: 1/166)

He is described as the last of the great hadith memorizers. His charitable acts and endowment of books reflect his piety. The sources are given as Shadharat al-Dhahab and al-A'lam.

Key Terms
الخطيب البغدادي (al-Khatib al-Baghdadi): A renowned Shafi'i hadith scholar and historian, known for his book Tarikh Baghdad.
كتاب الفقيه والمتفقه (Kitab al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih): A work on the methodology of fiqh and the ethics of the faqih and the student, useful for iftaa training.
