Dawud ibn Rashid: A Trusted Hanafi Narrator
Biographical entry with trustworthiness assessment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Dawud ibn Rashid as a Hanafi narrator and state the significance of his work 'al-Nawadir' in Hanafi fiqh transmission.

Core Idea
Dawud ibn Rashid's 'al-Nawadir' preserves rare Hanafi narrations, and his trustworthiness is affirmed by major hadith scholars.

As a mufti, your ability to evaluate transmitted rulings depends on knowing the transmitters. This lesson introduces you to Dawud ibn Rashid, a Hanafi scholar whose collection 'al-Nawadir' is a source of uncommon narrations. You will learn his place in the Hanafi transmission chain and why his reliability matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's profile
Note his full name, origin (Khawarizmi), and teachers: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (al-Shaybani) and Hafs ibn Ghiyath. This connects him to the Hanafi core.
2
Recognize his work 'al-Nawadir'
He authored 'al-Nawadir' (rare narrations). In Hanafi terms, nawadir are transmissions outside the mashhur zahir al-riwaya. Understanding this helps you classify his contributions.
3
Assess his hadith credentials
Major hadith collectors (Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i) narrated from him. Al-Bukhari used him via an intermediary. This establishes his general reliability.
4
Resolve the dispute about his reliability
Ibn Hazm claimed he was weak, but Ibn Hajar counters that this was a confusion. The consensus of scholars like Ibn Ma'in and the compilers above supports his trustworthiness.
5
Memorize his death year and source
He died in 230 AH. The entry is from al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya. This anchors his timeline in Hanafi history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٧- داود بن رشيد : الخوارزمى من أصحاب محمد بن الحسن، وحفص ابن غياث ، سكن بغداد وروى عنه مسلم وأبو داود وابن ماجة والنسائي، وله النوادر، مات سنة ثلاثين ومائتين ذكره فى الجواهر المضيئة . قال الجامع : ذكره الحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني في "الهدى السارى مقدمة فتح البارى"، ووصفه بأحد الثقات وقال : "وثقه ابن معين وغیره، روى عنه مسلم وأبو داود وابن ماجه وروى له البخاري حديثًا بواسطة، وكذا النسائي، وغفل ابن حزم وقال : إنه ضعيف فكأنه اشتبه عليه انتهى" . (الفوائد البهية : ٩٥)
27- Dawud ibn Rashid: al-Khawarizmi, one of the companions of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and Hafs ibn Ghiyath. He lived in Baghdad, and narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Nasa'i. He has 'al-Nawadir'. He died in 230 AH. Mentioned in al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a. The compiler says: al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani mentioned him in 'al-Huda al-Sari, Introduction to Fath al-Bari', and described him as one of the trustworthy. He said: 'Ibn Ma'in and others declared him trustworthy. Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Nasa'i narrated from him. Al-Bukhari narrated a hadith through him with an intermediary. Ibn Hazm was mistaken and said he was weak, as if he confused him.' End quote. (al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya: 95)
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This biography of Dawud ibn Rashid emphasizes his role as a transmitter of hadith and his association with the Hanafi school (as a companion of Muhammad al-Shaybani and Hafs ibn Ghiyath). He is noted for his work 'al-Nawadir', likely a collection of rare hadith or fatwas. The text then cites Ibn Hajar's assessment of his reliability, countering Ibn Hazm's criticism. The source is al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya, a biographical work on Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-nawadir): A collection of rare or uncommon narrations or rulings, possibly referring to Dawud ibn Rashid's work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Biography of Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna
Biographical entry on Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna in the transmission of tafsir and hadith knowledge, and identify his role as a teacher of al-Shafi'i and a source of Hijazi scholarship.

Core Idea
Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna preserved the knowledge of the Hijaz; his tafsir expertise was unmatched.

This biography introduces Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna, a key figure in the early Islamic scholarly community. His praise by al-Shafi'i and Ibn Wahb highlights his authority in both hadith and Quranic exegesis. For a mufti, understanding the credibility of such transmitters is essential for evaluating the strength of narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Read the full name and region: Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna al-Hilali, shaykh of the Hijaz, resident of Mecca. Note his title 'Imam' and 'hafiz'.
He belonged to the Banu Hilal tribe.
2
Recognize the Testimonies
Al-Shafi'i said: 'Were it not for Malik and Ibn 'Uyayna, the knowledge of the Hijaz would have disappeared.' Ibn Wahb said: 'I do not know anyone more knowledgeable in tafsir than Ibn 'Uyayna.'
These statements establish his dual expertise in hadith and tafsir.
3
Understand the Mufti's Relevance
A mufti relies on authentic chains of transmission. Ibn 'Uyayna is a key link in Hijazi narrations, especially those reaching al-Shafi'i. Knowing his stature helps assess the reliability of reports.
His students included al-Shafi'i, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and others.

Biographical Notices and Their Role in Fatwa
Index of prominent scholars with brief biographies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details that establish a scholar's authority in the transmission of fatwa and evaluate their relevance to Hanafi legal methodology.

Core Idea
Biography verifies the chain of knowledge; fatwa relies on trustworthy transmitters.

This passage from Imam al-Nawawi's "Adab al-Fatwa" presents a concise index of scholars whose lives and works underpin the science of fatwa. Understanding their teachers, students, and the assessments of later critics allows a mufti to gauge the reliability of legal transmissions and the weight of different opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify Each Scholar
Read the entry for each scholar and note their full name, nisba, and death date. This establishes their identity and time period.
Scholars are listed in alphabetical order by first name.
2
Extract Teachers and Students
List the teachers and students mentioned. This shows the chain of knowledge transmission and the scholar's place in the network.
For example, Dawud ibn Rashid studied under Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and narrated to major hadith collectors.
3
Assess Reliability
Note any endorsements or criticisms from recognized critics. For instance, Ibn Hajar confirms Dawud's trustworthiness, while Ibn Hazm's weakness claim is dismissed as confusion.
Reliability affects whether a scholar's narrations can be used as evidence.
4
Recognize Works
Identify the works attributed to each scholar, such as al-Nawadir or al-Mudawwanah. Their works indicate their contributions to legal literature.
In Hanafi usul, al-Nawadir are transmissions outside Zahir al-Riwayah and have a different authority level.
5
Connect to Fatwa Practice
Consider how each scholar's life and works influence fatwa. For example, a mufti must know the reliability of Dawud's al-Nawadir before relying on a ruling therein.
This step bridges biography to practical iftaa.

28 - Sahnun: He is the Shaykh Abu al-Sa'id Abd al-Salam ibn Sa'id ibn Habib al-Tanukhi, originally from Hims, then Maghribi Maliki, the author of al-Mudawwanah, mufti of Qayrawan and its judge. He studied under Abu al-Qasim, Ibn Wahb, and Ashhab. He had many students. He died in the year 240 AH and lived 80 years. (al-Shadharat: 2/94)

Al-Shafi'i said: 'Were it not for Malik and Ibn 'Uyaynah, the knowledge of the Hijaz would have disappeared.' Ibn Wahb said: 'I know no one more knowledgeable in tafsir than Ibn 'Uyaynah.'
115 - Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi - Index of Notable Figures - and Ahmad al-'Ijli said: 'His hadiths numbered about seven thousand, and he had no books.' He was born in Kufa in the middle of Sha'ban in the year 107 AH. He died at the beginning of Rajab in the year 198 AH. (Shadharat al-Dhahab: 1/354)
30 - al-Shafi'i: He is Imam Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Idris ibn al-Abbas ibn Uthman ibn al-Shafi' ibn al-Sa'ib ibn 'Ubayd ibn Abd Yazid ibn Hashim ibn al-Muttalib ibn Abd Manaf, the grandfather of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace. Al-Shafi' ibn al-Sa'ib is the one to whom al-Shafi'i is attributed. He met the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, when he was a youth, and his father al-Sa'ib accepted Islam on the day of Badr. Al-Shafi'i was born in Ghazza in Syria, because his father and other Qurayshis used to trade there, in the year 150 AH. It is also said otherwise. Then he was taken to Mecca at the age of two, grew up there, memorized the Qur'an at seven, and 'al-Muwatta'' at ten. He studied jurisprudence under Muslim ibn Khalid, the mufti of Mecca, known as al-Zanji, and this Muslim authorized him to give fatwa at age fifteen. Then he traveled to Malik in Medina and stayed with him for a while. Then he came to Baghdad in 195 AH, stayed there for about two years, and the scholars gathered around him and took from him, and he wrote his old book there. Then he went out to Mecca, then returned to Baghdad in 198 AH, stayed there for a month, then left for Egypt, where he wrote his new books, including al-Risalah, al-Umm, al-Musnad, al-Sunan, and others. He remained there spreading knowledge, continuously occupied in its ancient mosque, until he was struck a severe blow, fell ill for days as it is said, then passed to the mercy of God Almighty on Friday, the end of Rajab 204 AH, and was buried in al-Qarafah after the afternoon prayer of that day. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyah by al-Isnawi: 1/11)

It is also said: Shuraih ibn Shurahbil, one of those who lived in both pre-Islamic and Islamic times. He was appointed as judge by Umar over Kufa, then by those after him. He narrated from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with them. And from him...

Commentary
This passage is an index of notable figures (فهرس الأعلام) from the work 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi. It provides concise biographical entries for scholars that are relevant to the science of issuing fatwa, covering their lineage, teachers, students, works, and death dates. 
- Dawud ibn Rashid: A Khwarazmian scholar, student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani and Hafs ibn Ghiyath. He is noted for his collection 'al-Nawadir' and is considered trustworthy by major hadith critics, though Ibn Hazm mistakenly considered him weak. 
- Sahnun: A prominent Maliki jurist, author of al-Mudawwanah, and mufti of Qayrawan. 
- Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah: A major hadith memorizer and mufassir, praised by al-Shafi'i and Ibn Wahb for his knowledge. 
- al-Shafi'i: The founder of the Shafi'i school, born in Ghazza, raised in Mecca, studied under Muslim ibn Khalid and Malik, wrote both 'old' and 'new' works, and taught in Baghdad and Egypt. 
- Shuraih: A famous early judge appointed by Umar ibn al-Khattab over Kufa, known for his legal acumen.
These biographies serve to establish the authority and reliability of these scholars, which is essential for understanding the transmission of legal knowledge and the chain of fatwa.

Key Terms
فهرس الأعلام (fihris al-a‘lām): An index of notable figures, listing brief biographical entries.
النوادر (al-nawādir): A collection of rare or uncommon narrations and legal rulings, here attributed to Dawud ibn Rashid.
المدونة (al-mudawwanah): A foundational Maliki legal work compiled by Sahnun.

Key Takeaway
Biographical knowledge of early scholars is indispensable for assessing the authority of legal transmissions and for weighing conflicting opinions in fatwa.

Imam al-Shafi'i: A Biographical Anchor for the Mufti
Biographical entry of Imam al-Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key milestones in Imam al-Shafi'i's life that shaped his legal methodology and his two madhhabs (qadim and jadid).

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i gave fatwa at 15 and authored two madhhabs—his travels evolved his usul.

This biographical entry from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa presents the life of Imam al-Shafi'i, a founding figure of usul al-fiqh. For a mufti, understanding al-Shafi'i's scholarly journey illuminates the development of his legal principles and the distinction between his old and new madhhabs. This anchor passage provides the chronological framework for his contributions.

Guided Path
1
Trace his lineage and birth location
Note his Quraysh descent and birth in Ghazzah (Gaza) to understand his tribal connection to the Prophet.
2
Follow his early education
He memorized the Quran at 7 and the Muwatta' at 10, then studied fiqh under Muslim ibn Khalid. This shows his precociousness.
3
Mark the granting of fatwa permission at 15
His teacher authorized him to give fatwa at age 15, a remarkable milestone indicating exceptional knowledge.
4
Map his scholarly travels
From Mecca to Medina (study under Malik), then to Baghdad (old madhhab), and finally to Egypt (new madhhab). Each location influenced his methodology.
5
Identify his major works and death
He authored al-Risalah, al-Umm, al-Musnad, al-Sunan, etc. Died in 204 AH. Connect to the mufti's need to know the authoritative texts.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۰ الشافعي : هو الإمام أبو عبد الله محمد بن إدريس بن العباس بن عثمان ابن الشافع بن السائب بن عبيد بن عبد يزيد بن هاشم بن المطلب بن عبد مناف، جد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وشافع بن السائب هو الذي ينسب إليه الشافعي، لقى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهو مترعرع ، وأسلم أبوه السائب يوم بدر، كانت ولادة الشافعي بغزة من الشام ؛ لأن أباه وغيره من قريش، كانوا يتعاهدون، وذلك في سنة خمسين ومائة . وقيل غير ذلك، ثم حمل إلى مكة وهو ابن سنتين، ونشأ بها، وحفظ القرآن وهو ابن سبع سنين ، و "الموطأ" وهو ابن عشرة، وتفقه على مسلم بن خالد مفتى مكة، ويعرف بالزنجى، وأذن مسلم المذكور له في الإفتاء، وعمره خمس عشر سنة، ثم رحل إلى مالك بالمدينة، ولازمه مدة، ثم قدم بغداد سنة خمس وتسعين ومائة ، فأقام بها حولين، فاجتمع عليه علماؤها، وأخذوا عنه، وصنف بها كتابه القديم، ثم خرج إلى مكة ثم عاد إلى بغداد سنة ثمان وتسعين فأقام بها شهراً ثم خرج إلى مصر، وصنف فيها كتبه الجديدة، منها الرسالة والأم، والمسند والسنن وغيرها، ولم يزل بها ناشراً للعلم ملازماً للاشتغال بجامعها العتيق، إلى أن أصابته ضربة شديدة، فمرض بسببها أياماً على ما قيل ، ثم انتقل إلى رحمة الله تعالى يوم الجمعة، سلخ رجب سنة أربع ومائتين، ودفن بالقرافة بعد العصر من يومه . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ١١/١)
30. Al-Shafi'i: He is the Imam Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Idris ibn al-Abbas ibn Uthman ibn al-Shafi' ibn al-Sa'ib ibn Ubayd ibn Abd Yazid ibn Hashim ibn al-Muttalib ibn Abd Manaf, the grandfather of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. Al-Shafi' ibn al-Sa'ib is the one to whom al-Shafi'i is attributed. He met the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was a boy, and his father al-Sa'ib became Muslim on the day of Badr. The birth of al-Shafi'i was in Ghazzah of Syria because his father and other Quraysh used to trade there, and that was in the year 150 AH. It is also said otherwise. Then he was taken to Mecca at the age of two, grew up there, memorized the Quran at seven, and the Muwatta' at ten. He studied fiqh under Muslim ibn Khalid, the mufti of Mecca, known as al-Zanji. The aforementioned Muslim granted him permission to give fatwa at the age of fifteen. Then he traveled to Malik in Medina and stayed with him for a while. Then he came to Baghdad in 195 AH, stayed two years, the scholars gathered around him, took from him, and he authored his old book there. Then he went to Mecca, returned to Baghdad in 198 AH, stayed a month, then went to Egypt, authored his new books there, including al-Risalah, al-Umm, al-Musnad, al-Sunan, and others. He remained there spreading knowledge, constantly occupied in its ancient mosque, until a severe blow struck him, causing him illness for days as is said. Then he passed away to the mercy of Allah on Friday, the end of Rajab, 204 AH, and was buried in al-Qarafah after Asr on the same day. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyah by al-Isnavi: 1/11)
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry of Imam al-Shafi'i from al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa. It details his lineage, birth in Ghazzah in 150 AH, move to Mecca, early memorization of Quran and Muwatta', study under Muslim ibn Khalid, receipt of permission to give fatwa at fifteen, his journey to Medina to study under Imam Malik, his stay in Baghdad where he authored his old madhhab, and his final settlement in Egypt where he wrote his new books. The entry ends with his death in 204 AH and burial in al-Qarafah. This biography highlights the scholarly pedigree and travels that shaped al-Shafi'i's jurisprudence.

Key Terms
الشافعي (al-Shafi'i): Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Idris, founder of the Shafi'i school of law, descendant of the Prophet's clan.

C) Fifteen years old
D) Twenty years old

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Shafi'i's life exemplifies the ideal scholarly journey for a mufti: early grounding, travel, and methodological evolution.

Shuraih al-Qadi: A Model Judge in Hanafi Usul al-Iftaa
Biographical entry of the judge Shuraih ibn al-Harith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Shuraih al-Qadi and explain why his judicial practice is cited in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Core Idea
Shuraih, the judge of Kufa appointed by Umar, is a foundational reference for Hanafi istidlal bi qada al-sahabah.

This biographical entry introduces Shuraih ibn al-Harith, one of the earliest and most influential judges of Kufa. His rulings and methods are frequently invoked by later Hanafi muftis as part of the school's reliance on qada al-sahabah (judicial decisions of the Companions). Understanding his stature and reliability helps contextualize why his practice carries weight in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography and note key facts
Go through the Arabic text and literal translation. Identify the full name, lineage, kunya, and tribal affiliation. Also note the significant events: appointment by Umar, narration from major Companions, students, length of judgeship, and date of death.
The text mentions he lived 120 years and died around 78-80 AH.
2
Recognize the chain of transmission
Identify whom Shuraih narrated from (Umar, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud) and who narrated from him (Sha'bi, Nakha'i, Ibn Sirin). This chain shows his direct link to the Prophet through prominent Companions, enhancing the reliability of his transmitted rulings.
He is said to be from the Mukhadramun – those who lived in both Jahiliyyah and Islam.
3
Assess his credibility as a judge
Note that Yahya ibn Ma'in declared him trustworthy (thiqah). Also observe his character: he was a jurist, a poet, and had a sense of humor. His long tenure and resignation a year before death indicate stability and independence.
His wit and poetry do not detract from his judicial reliability.
4
Connect to Hanafi usul al-ifta
Reflect on why the compiler includes this biography in a work on Rasm al-Mufti. Shuraih represents the Kufan school of qada, which is a major source for Hanafi fiqh. His practices and decisions are often cited as evidence in Hanafi fatwas, especially in matters of qada and adab al-qadi.
Hanafi muftis consider qada al-sahabah as a source of law when no clear text or ijma exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-۳۱ شريح : هو شريح بن الحارث بن قيس القاضي أبو أمية، الكندى، الكوفي، الفقيه ويقال : شريح بن شرحبيل بن المخضرمين استقضاه عمر على الكوفة ، ثم على فمن بعده ، وحدّث عن عمر، وعلى وابن مسعود رضي الله عنهم. وعنه الشعبي والنخعي، وعبد العزيز بن رفيع ومحمد ابن سيرين، وطائفة . استعفى من القضاء قبل موته بسنة من الحجاج، وعاش مائة وعشرين سنة، وثقه يحيى بن معين، وكان فقيهاً شاعراً ،فائقا فيه دعابة، مات سنة ثمان وسبعين وقيل : في سنة ثمانين . ( تذكرة الحفاظ : ٥٩/١)
31. Shuraih: He is Shuraih ibn al-Harith ibn Qays, the judge, Abu Umayyah al-Kindi al-Kufi, the jurist. It is also said: Shuraih ibn Shurahbil, from the Mukhadramun. Umar appointed him as judge over Kufa, then those after him followed. He narrated from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with them. Al-Sha'bi, al-Nakha'i, Abd al-Aziz ibn Rufay', Muhammad ibn Sirin, and a group narrated from him. He resigned from the judiciary a year before his death from al-Hajjaj. He lived 120 years. Yahya ibn Ma'in declared him trustworthy. He was a jurist, poet, and excelled in wit. He died in 78 AH, and it was said in 80 AH. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz: 1/59)
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry of Shuraih ibn al-Harith, a prominent early judge of Kufa. It details his appointment by Umar, his narration from major Companions, and the many students who narrated from him, including Sha'bi and Nakha'i. The text notes his long life of 120 years, his resignation from judgeship a year before death, and his character as a jurist and poet with a sense of humor. His death is placed in 78 or 80 AH. This biography illustrates the type of early authorities whose practices informed later usul al-ifta.

Key Terms
شريح (Shuraih): Shuraih ibn al-Harith, a noted judge of Kufa appointed by Caliph Umar.

C) To criticize his rulings.

Key Takeaway
Shuraih al-Qadi's biography confirms his reliability and his connection to the Companions, making his judicial practice a valued precedent in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Biography of al-Sha'bi (الشعبي) – A Pillar of Early Knowledge
Biographical entry of the great tabi'i Amir ibn Sharahil al-Sha'bi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Sha'bi's full name, his generation (tabi'i), his intellectual abilities, and his significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Sha'bi met 500 Companions and memorized every hadith he ever heard — he never wrote a single word.

Al-Sha'bi is one of the most important figures of the tabi'un generation. His biography reminds us that the earliest scholars preserved knowledge through prodigious memory. For students of Hanafi fiqh and usul al-iftaa, identifying the transmission layer (tabi'i vs. Companion) is critical for evaluating the authority of a narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and lineage
Read the full name and nisba: Amir ibn Sharahil ibn Abd al-Sha'bi al-Himyari, Abu Amr al-Kufi. Note his tribal affiliation (Sha'b Hamdan) and his kunya.
2
Determine his generation
The text explicitly calls him 'from the great tabi'un.' This means he belonged to the generation after the Companions, not a Companion himself, even though he met many.
3
Note his intellectual capacity
Al-Sha'bi's statement about never writing and memorizing every hadith demonstrates extraordinary memory, a hallmark of early oral tradition.
This also informs us that reliance on memory was the norm, not writing.
4
Locate his time period
He was born six years into Umar's caliphate (approx. 640 CE) and died around 103 AH (721 CE). The text acknowledges some variation in the death year.
5
Recognize his significance
Having met 500 Companions, al-Sha'bi is a major link in the chain of transmission. His opinions carry weight in early fiqh, and he is frequently cited in Hanafi works.
This makes him a reliable authority for legal rulings (aqwal).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۲- الشعبي : هو الإمام عامر بن شراحيل بن عبد الشعبي، الحميري، أبو عمر الكوفى من شعب همدان من كبار التابعين كان كثير العلم، عظيم الحلم قديم السلم . قال منصور الغذائي عن الشعبي : أدركت خمسمائة من الصحابة". قال ابن شبرمه سمعت الشعبي يقول : ما كتبت سوداء في بيضاء، ولا حدثني رجل بحديث إلا حفظته، ولا حدثنى رجل بحديث فأحببت أن يعيد على . والمشهور أن مولده كان لست سنين خلت من خلافة عمر ، قيل : مات سنة ١٠٣ هـ وقيل : غير ذلك . (تهذيب التهذيب : ٤ / ١٥٨)
32. Al-Sha'bi: He is the Imam Amir ibn Sharahil ibn Abd al-Sha'bi al-Himyari, Abu Amr al-Kufi from Sha'b Hamdan, one of the great Successors. He had extensive knowledge, great forbearance, and early peace. Mansur al-Ghudani said about al-Sha'bi: 'I encountered five hundred Companions.' Ibn Shubrumah said: I heard al-Sha'bi say: 'I never wrote black on white, nor did any man narrate a hadith to me except that I memorized it, nor did any man narrate a hadith to me that I wished he would repeat.' It is well-known that his birth was six years into the caliphate of Umar. It is said he died in 103 AH, and other dates are also mentioned. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib: 4/158)
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry of al-Sha'bi (Amir ibn Sharahil), a prominent tabi'i from Kufa. It highlights his vast knowledge and remarkable memory, as he claimed never to write down hadiths and never needed repetition. His encounter with 500 Companions shows his early stature. The text notes his birth date as six years into Umar's caliphate and his death around 103 AH. Al-Sha'bi is an important figure in hadith transmission and early fiqh.

Key Terms
الشعبي (al-Sha'bi): Amir ibn Sharahil, a major tabi'i and scholar from Kufa.
تابعي (tabi'i): A person who met a Companion of the Prophet ﷺ but did not meet the Prophet himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He wrote hadiths extensively
B) He memorized hadiths without writing
C) He relied on written notes
D) He never learned hadith

Key Takeaway
Al-Sha'bi's prodigious memory and direct contact with 500 Companions make him a pivotal transmitter in the Hanafi chain of knowledge.

The Ideal Scholar: Biography of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi
Biographical entry of a Shafi'i jurist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three key qualities of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and explain why his biography is relevant to the character of a mufti.

Core Idea
A true scholar combines great influence with personal poverty and humility.

This passage introduces us to a towering Shafi'i jurist whose life exemplifies the ideal of a scholar detached from worldly wealth despite immense influence. As students of iftaa, we can learn from his character and the respect he commanded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and his school
Read the first line to know who is being introduced: his name, lineage, and affiliation with the Shafi'i school.
He is a Shafi'i jurist, but his biography is included in a Hanafi text for comparative fiqh and as an example of scholarship.
2
Note his scholarly reach
Find the sentence about students traveling from east and west and fatwas being brought to him. Appreciate the geographical extent of his influence.
This illustrates how a scholar's reputation can spread without modern technology.
3
Understand his poverty and humility
Read his personal statement about finding students everywhere and his lack of worldly possessions. Contrast his poverty with his high status.
His poverty prevented him from performing Hajj, showing his asceticism.
4
Appreciate his personal character
Look for descriptions of his cheerfulness, openness, and memorization of stories and poems. This shows the ideal of a balanced personality.
A mufti should be approachable and pleasant.
5
Reflect on the relevance to iftaa
Consider why a Hanafi text includes a Shafi'i biography. Think about the qualities a mufti should embody: humility, independence from worldly power, and dedication to learning.
This example teaches that a mufti's authority comes from knowledge, not wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٣- الشيخ أبو إسحاق الشيرازي : الشيخ أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن على ابن يوسف الشيرازي، شيخ الإسلام علما وعملا وورعاً وزهدا وتصنيفا وإملاء وتلاميذا واشتغالا ، كانت الطلبة ترحل من الشرق والغرب إليه، والفتاوى تحمل من البر والبحر إلى بين يديه . قال رحمه الله : لما خرجت في رسالة الخليفة إلى خراسان لم أدخل بلداً ولا قرية إلا وجدتُ قاضيها وخطيبها أو مفتيها من تلاميذي، ومع هذا فكان لا يملك شيئًا من الدنيا، بلغ من الفقر حتى كان لا يجد في بعض الأوقات قوتاً ولا لباسًا، ولم يحج بسبب ذلك، هذا والأمراء والوزراء بين يديه، ولو أراد الحج لحملوه على الأعناق . وكان طلق الوجه دائم البشر كثير البسط، حسن المجالسة، يحفظ كثيراً من الحكايات الحسنة والأشعار ولد رحمه الله بفيروز آباد وهي قرية من قرى شيراز في سنة ثلاث وتسعين وثلاثمائة، وقيل: في سنة خمس وقيل ست. توفي رحمه الله يوم
33. Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi: Sheikh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Shirazi, the Sheikh of Islam in knowledge, action, piety, asceticism, authorship, dictation, students, and occupation. Students would travel from east and west to him, and fatwas were brought from land and sea to his presence. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'When I went on the caliph's mission to Khurasan, I did not enter any city or village except that I found its judge, preacher or mufti from among my students.' Yet he owned nothing of this world, so much so that sometimes he could not find food or clothing, and because of that he did not perform Hajj, even though princes and ministers were at his service, and if he wanted to go for Hajj they would carry him on their shoulders. He was cheerful, always smiling, very open, good company, and memorized many good tales and poems. He was born, may Allah have mercy on him, in Firuzabad, a village of Shiraz, in the year 393 AH, and it is said 395 or 396. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, on the day of...
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (d. 476 AH), the renowned Shafi'i jurist and author of al-Tanbih and al-Muhadhdhab. It emphasizes his humility and poverty despite his great influence. His statement about finding his students in every Khurasani town illustrates his wide reach. The entry highlights his cheerful disposition and memorization of stories and poems. His birth is given as 393 AH in Firuzabad, and the text begins his death date but cuts off. This biography shows the ideal of a scholar who combined deep learning with asceticism.

Key Terms
الشيخ أبو إسحاق الشيرازي (Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi): Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf, a leading Shafi'i jurist and teacher, author of al-Tanbih and al-Muhadhdhab.

C) He was too poor to afford it
D) He was busy with students

Key Takeaway
Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi embodies the ideal scholar: great influence combined with deep personal humility and asceticism.

Understanding the Role of a Biographical Index in Usul al-Iftaa
Biographical entries of prominent scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of a biographical index in usul al-iftaa and extract key scholarly virtues from the entries of al-Sha'bi, Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, and Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini.

Core Idea
A biographical index documents chains of knowledge transmission and exemplars of scholarly adab for the mufti.

Imam al-Nawawi's 'Adaab al-Fatwa' includes a biographical index of prominent scholars. This index serves as a reminder that the science of iftaa is built upon the shoulders of previous generations. By studying these biographies, the student of usul al-iftaa learns the virtues expected of a mufti: immense knowledge, memory, asceticism, and dedication to teaching. This lesson guides you through parsing these entries to uncover the adab embedded in each scholar's life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage type
Recognize that this is a biographical index (Fihris al-A'lam) from a classical work on fatwa etiquette. The passage lists scholars with brief life accounts.
It is not a ruling or a dispute; it is a reference list for students of ifta.
2
Extract key details for each scholar
For each entry, note the full name, birth/death years, notable teachers/students, and key characteristics (e.g., memory, poverty, influence).
Focus on the virtues and adab highlighted.
3
Identify common themes across entries
Look for recurring themes: reliance on memory (al-Sha'bi), far-reaching teaching (al-Shirazi), extreme asceticism (al-Shirazi, al-Isfarayini), and authoring major works (al-Mawardi).
These themes are part of the adab al-mufti.
4
Reflect on the purpose of this index
Understand that the index helps the student of iftaa to contextualize the sources and authorities. Knowing the biographies builds respect for the chain of transmission and the values behind the fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى
فهرس الأعلام الشعبي والنخعي، وعبد العزيز بن رفيع ومحمد ابن سيرين، وطائفة . استعفى من القضاء قبل موته بسنة من الحجاج، وعاش مائة وعشرين سنة، وثقه يحيى بن معين، وكان فقيهاً شاعراً ،فائقا فيه دعابة، مات سنة ثمان وسبعين وقيل : في سنة ثمانين . ( تذكرة الحفاظ : ٥٩/١)
۳۲- الشعبي : هو الإمام عامر بن شراحيل بن عبد الشعبي، الحميري، أبو عمر الكوفى من شعب ،همدان من كبار التابعين كان كثير العلم، عظيم الحلم قديم السلم . قال منصور الغذائي عن الشعبي : أدركت خمسمائة من الصحابة". قال ابن شبرمه سمعت الشعبي يقول : ما كتبت سوداء في بيضاء، ولا حدثني رجل بحديث إلا حفظته، ولا حدثنى رجل بحديث فأحببت أن يعيد على . والمشهور أن مولده كان لست سنين خلت من خلافة عمر ، قيل : مات سنة ١٠٣ هـ وقيل : غير ذلك . تهذيب التهذيب : ٤ / ١٥٨)
٣٣- الشيخ أبو إسحاق الشيرازي : الشيخ أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن على ابن يوسف الشيرازي، شيخ الإسلام علما وعملا وورعاً وزهدا وتصنيفا وإملاء وتلاميذا واشتغالا ، كانت الطلبة ترحل من الشرق والغرب إليه، والفتاوى تحمل من البر والبحر إلى بين يديه .
قال رحمه الله : لما خرجت في رسالة الخليفة إلى خراسان لم أدخل بلداً ولا قرية إلا وجدتُ قاضيها وخطيبها أو مفتيها من تلاميذي، ومع هذا فكان لا يملك شيئًا من الدنيا، بلغ من الفقر حتى كان لا يجد في بعض الأوقات قوتاً ولا لباسًا، ولم يحج بسبب ذلك، هذا والأمراء والوزراء بين يديه، ولو أراد الحج لحملوه على الأعناق . وكان طلق الوجه دائم البشر كثير البسط، حسن المجالسة، يحفظ كثيراً من الحكايات الحسنة والأشعار ولد رحمه الله بفيروز آباد وهي قرية من قرى شيراز في سنة ثلاث وتسعين وثلاثمائة، وقيل: في سنة خمس وقيل ست. توفي رحمه الله يوم الأحد، وقيل: ليلة الأحد، حادي عشر جمادى الآخرة ، وقيل : الأولى سنة ست وسبعين وأربع مائة ودفن من الغد بمقبرة باب أبرز . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٢/ ٨٣-٨٤)
·
٣٤- الشيخ أبو حامد : هو الشيخ أبو حامد أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد الأسفراييني شيخ الدهر بلا نزاع، ووجه العصر بغير دفاع، ذو الأصحاب الذين طبقوا، الأرض، وملأ تصانيفهم وتلامذهم الطول والعرض، ولد سنة أربع وأربعين وثلاثمائة، وقدم بغداد سنة أربع وستين. فدرس علي ابن المرزبان، فلما مات لزم الداركي، ثم درس سنة سبعين، وأقام ببغداد مشغولا بالعلم، حتى صار فريد زمانه ،وأنظرهم، ومن وقف على تعليقته علم ذلك. توفي رحمه الله ليلة السبت، إحدى عشرة ليلة بقيت من شوال سنة ست وأربع مائة، ودفن في داره ، وكان يوما مشهوداً من كثرة الناس، وشدة الحزن والبكاء ثم نقل سنة عشر إلى باب حرب .
طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٥٧/١-٥٨)
٣٥- صاحب الحاوى : على بن محمد بن حبيب الماوردي، الإمام أبو الحسن البصرى الفقيه المفسر الشافعي، ولد سنة ٣٧٠هـ . وتوفى سنة ٤٥٠هـ خمسين وأربع مائة . له من الكتب : الأحكام السلطانية" في مجلد مطبوع بمصر، أدب الدنيا والدين" في مجلد مطبوع فى الجوائب، أعلام النبوة"، "الإقناع في الفروع ، أمثال القرآن"، "تسهيل النصر وتعجيل الظفر"، "الحاوى الكبير في الفروع " ، سياسة الملك" ، "قانون الوزارة" ، "النكت والعيون في التفسير وغير ذلك .
(هدية العارفين : ٦٨٩/١)
٣٦- صاحب الشامل : عبد السيد بن محمد بن عبد الواحد بن أحمد
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi - Index of prominent figures: al-Sha'bi, al-Nakha'i, Abd al-Aziz ibn Rafi', Muhammad ibn Sirin, and a group. He [al-Sha'bi] resigned from the judiciary one year before his death from al-Hajjaj, lived one hundred and twenty years, authenticated by Yahya ibn Ma'in, and was a jurist, poet, excellent in joking, died in seventy-eight or eighty. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 1/59) 32- al-Sha'bi: He is Imam Amir ibn Sharahil ibn Abd al-Sha'bi, al-Himyari, Abu Umar al-Kufi from Sha'b Hamdan, one of the great tabi'un, had much knowledge, great forbearance, early peace. Mansur al-Ghidhani said about al-Sha'bi: 'I met five hundred Companions.' Ibn Shubruma said: I heard al-Sha'bi say: 'I never wrote black on white, nor did any man narrate a hadith to me except I memorized it, nor did any man narrate a hadith to me that I wished he would repeat for me.' It is well-known that his birth was six years after the caliphate of Umar, died 103 AH or otherwise. (Tahdhib al-Tahdhib 4/158) 33- Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi: Sheikh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Shirazi, Sheikh of Islam in knowledge, deed, piety, asceticism, authorship, dictation, students, and occupation. Students would travel from east and west to him, and fatwas would be carried from land and sea to his presence. He said: 'When I went out in the caliph's mission to Khurasan, I did not enter a city or village except I found its judge, preacher, or mufti from my students.' Despite this, he owned nothing of the world; he was so poor that sometimes he had no food or clothing, and did not perform Hajj because of that, while princes and ministers were before him. If he wanted to perform Hajj, they would carry him on shoulders. He was cheerful, always smiling, jovial, good company, memorized many good stories and poems. He was born in Firuzabad, a village of Shiraz, in 393 AH (or 395/6). Died on Sunday (or Saturday night), 11 Jumada al-Akhirah (or al-Ula?) in 476 AH, buried the next day at Bab Abraz cemetery. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnaawi 2/83-84) 34- Sheikh Abu Hamid: He is Sheikh Abu Hamid Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Isfarayini, the unquestioned sheikh of the age, the face of the era without denial, possessing companions who filled the earth, and his books and students filled length and width. Born 344 AH, came to Baghdad 364 AH. Studied under Ibn al-Marzuban, after his death he followed al-Daraki, then began teaching in 370. He stayed in Baghdad occupied with knowledge until he became unique of his time and the most insightful. Whoever sees his commentary knows that. Died Saturday night, 11 days remaining of Shawwal 406 AH, buried in his home, a day witnessed by many people, intense grief and weeping, then transferred in 410 to Bab Harb cemetery. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnaawi 1/57-58) 35- Author of al-Hawi: Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Habib al-Mawardi, Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Basri al-Faqih al-Mufassir al-Shafi'i, born 370 AH, died 450 AH. His books include: al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya (printed in Egypt), Adab al-Dunya wa al-Din (printed in al-Jawa'ib), A'lam al-Nubuwwa, al-Iqna' fi al-Furu', Amthal al-Qur'an, Tashil al-Nasr wa Ta'jil al-Zafar, al-Hawi al-Kabir fi al-Furu', Siyasat al-Mulk, Qanun al-Wizara, al-Nukat wa al-'Uyun fi al-Tafsir and others. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin 1/689) 36- Author of al-Shamil: Abd al-Sayyid ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Ahmad...
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index from Imam al-Nawawi's 'Adaab al-Fatwa', listing prominent scholars whose lives and works are relevant to the discipline of ifta. The passage begins with a general mention of al-Sha'bi and others, then provides detailed entries for each scholar.

The first entry (32) is about al-Sha'bi (Amir ibn Sharahil), a famous tabi'i known for his vast knowledge and memory. He is noted for resigning from the judiciary and his statement 'I never wrote black on white', emphasizing reliance on memory. This illustrates the adab of a scholar who preserves knowledge without notes, though later scholarship relied more on writing.

Entry 33 covers Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, a Shafi'i jurist and teacher. His biography highlights his widespread influence: students and fatwa-seekers came from afar, and he trained many judges and muftis. Despite his status, he lived in poverty, exemplifying zuhd (asceticism) in scholars. His inability to perform Hajj due to poverty shows that even great scholars may face hardship, and it is not a fault.

Entry 34 is Sheikh Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini, another Shafi'i authority. His description as 'sheikh of the age without dispute' underscores his preeminence. He taught many students and produced works that became standard.

Entry 35 is about al-Mawardi, author of al-Hawi al-Kabir and other important works. His bibliography includes titles on politics, ethics, and tafsir, showing the breadth of his scholarship relevant to ifta.

The last entry (36) is incomplete, mentioning the author of al-Shamil. Overall, this index serves as a reference for students of ifta to recognize the authorities whose books and methods form the backbone of fatwa literature.

Key Terms
فهرس الأعلام (Fihris al-A'lam): An index of prominent scholars, as compiled in Imam al-Nawawi's work on the etiquette of fatwa.
الشعبي (al-Sha'bi): Amir ibn Sharahil al-Sha'bi, a tabi'i known for his knowledge, memory, and avoidance of writing hadith.
الشيخ أبو إسحاق الشيرازي (Sheikh Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi): Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Shirazi, a Shafi'i jurist and teacher, known for training many judges and muftis.
الشيخ أبو حامد الأسفراييني (Sheikh Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini): Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Isfarayini, a leading Shafi'i scholar of his time, known for his teaching and commentary.
صاحب الحاوي (Sahib al-Hawi): Title referring to Imam al-Mawardi, author of al-Hawi al-Kabir, a comprehensive Shafi'i fiqh work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Sha'bi say about writing and memorizing hadith according to the passage?
A) I wrote every hadith I heard on black and white.
B) I never wrote black on white, and I memorized every hadith I heard.
C) I wrote hadith on white paper only.
D) I preferred books over memory.

Key Takeaway
Biographical indexes in usul al-iftaa preserve the adab of scholars and emphasize the virtues of memory, teaching, asceticism, and authorship that a mufti should embody.

Reading a Classical Scholar’s Biography: Sheikh Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini
biographical entry of a leading Shafi'i scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details from a classical tabaqat entry and explain how such entries inform the authority of a mufti in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A mufti’s lineage of teachers and students establishes his ijazah chain and credibility.

Biographical entries (tabaqat) are common in classical works on iftaa. They document the scholarly lineage and achievements of jurists. While this entry is about a Shafi'i scholar, the method of analyzing such entries is the same across madhhabs. For a Hanafi mufti, understanding another school's major figures can help in cross-madhhab fatwa comparisons and in respecting the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and honorific
Extract the scholar's complete name (ism, nasab, nisba) and any honorifics like 'Shaykh al-Dahr'.
Honorifics indicate the scholar's standing in the community.
2
Note the birth and death dates
Record the hijri years of birth and death. This helps situate the scholar in time and possible cross-madhhab interactions.
Here: born 344 AH, died 406 AH.
3
Identify key teachers and students
List the scholars he studied under and his own students. This shows his scholarly lineage (sanad).
Teachers: Ibn al-Marzban, al-Daraki. Students: many who 'covered the earth'.
4
Recognize scholarly output
Note any works or commentaries (ta'liqa) mentioned. They demonstrate his expertise and contribution to fiqh/usul.
His ta'liqa is cited as evidence of his depth.
5
Relate to mufti credentials
Consider how these details (teachers, students, works) establish his authority to issue fatwas. In Hanafi iftaa, a mufti's chain of learning is critical.
This entry shows al-Isfarayini was a 'shaykh of the age' – a recognized authority.

٣٤- الشيخ أبو حامد : هو الشيخ أبو حامد أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد الأسفراييني شيخ الدهر بلا نزاع، ووجه العصر بغير دفاع، ذو الأصحاب الذين طبقوا، الأرض، وملأ تصانيفهم وتلامذهم الطول والعرض، ولد سنة أربع وأربعين وثلاثمائة، وقدم بغداد سنة أربع وستين. فدرس علي ابن المرزبان، فلما مات لزم الداركي، ثم درس سنة سبعين، وأقام ببغداد مشغولا بالعلم، حتى صار فريد زمانه ،وأنظرهم، ومن وقف على تعليقته علم ذلك. توفي رحمه الله ليلة السبت، إحدى عشرة ليلة بقيت من شوال سنة ست وأربع مائة، ودفن في داره ، وكان يوما مشهوداً من كثرة الناس، وشدة الحزن والبكاء ثم نقل سنة عشر إلى باب حرب .
طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٥٧/١-٥٨)
34 - Sheikh Abu Hamid: He is Sheikh Abu Hamid Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Isfarayini, the undisputed (shaykh) of the age, the face of the era without dispute, possessor of companions who covered the earth, and his books and students filled length and breadth. He was born in the year 344 AH, and arrived in Baghdad in the year 364. He studied under Ibn al-Marzban, and when he died, he stayed with al-Daraki, then taught (as a professor) in the year 370. He remained in Baghdad occupied with knowledge until he became the unique one of his time and the most insightful. Whoever examines his commentary will know that. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, on the night of Saturday, with eleven nights remaining of Shawwal in the year 406 AH, and was buried in his house, and it was a witnessed day due to the multitude of people and intensity of grief and weeping. Then he was transferred in the year 410 to Bab Harb. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi: 1/57-58)
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry from the index of Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa. It introduces Sheikh Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini, a leading Shafi'i scholar of the 4th/10th century. The text highlights his status as the foremost scholar of his time, his prolific teaching, and his many students and works. It provides his birth (344 AH), arrival in Baghdad, teachers, and death (406 AH). For students of Hanafi fiqh, this entry is useful as it shows the structure of scholarly biographies in classical works on iftaa, and emphasizes the importance of scholarly credentials in issuing fatwas.

Key Terms
شيخ الدهر (Shaykh al-Dahr): The scholar of the age, indicating preeminence
تعليقة (Ta'liqa): A scholar's commentary or gloss

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 344 AH
B) 364 AH

Key Takeaway
Biographical entries (tabaqat) are essential for establishing the credibility and chain of transmission of a mufti’s knowledge.

Biography of al-Mawardi: The Author of al-Hawi
Biographical entry of a Shafi'i jurist and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key works of Imam al-Mawardi and explain their relevance to a Hanafi mufti.

Core Idea
Al-Mawardi's al-Hawi is a treasure trove of comparative fiqh essential for a mufti navigating ikhtilaf.

This lesson introduces you to a towering Shafi'i scholar whose works are frequently cited in Hanafi fatwa literature. Understanding who al-Mawardi is and what he wrote helps you navigate inter-madhhab debates as a mufti. His 'al-Hawi al-Kabir' is particularly important for its comprehensive treatment of furu' and its engagement with Hanafi positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and lineage
Read the Arabic passage and extract the full name: Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Habib al-Mawardi. Note his title: Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Basri al-Shafi'i.
The name 'al-Mawardi' likely derives from his place of origin, Maward.
2
Note his birth and death years
Born 370 AH, died 450 AH. These dates place him in the 4th-5th centuries AH, a period of rich juristic development.
Knowing his era helps contextualize his works relative to other classical scholars.
3
List his major works
From the text, list the books mentioned: al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya, Adab al-Dunya wa al-Din, A'lam al-Nubuwwa, al-Iqna' fi al-Furu', Amthal al-Qur'an, Tashil al-Nasr, al-Hawi al-Kabir, Siyasat al-Mulk, Qanun al-Wizara, al-Nukat wa al-'Uyun.
Focus on al-Hawi al-Kabir and al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya as his most influential works.
4
Identify the work most relevant to comparative fiqh
Al-Hawi al-Kabir fi al-Furu' is a comprehensive legal encyclopedia that engages with multiple madhhabs, making it invaluable for a Hanafi mufti for cross-madhhab comparison.
Al-Hawi is often cited in later Hanafi works, especially for Shafi'i positions.
5
Reflect on why a Hanafi mufti should know this scholar
A mufti must be aware of prominent scholars from other madhhabs to correctly attribute positions and weigh evidence. Al-Mawardi's works provide authoritative statements of the Shafi'i school and are frequently referenced in fatwa literature.
Knowing the author's madhhab prevents misattribution during tarjih.

35 - Author of al-Hawi: Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Habib al-Mawardi, the Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Basri, the Shafi'i jurist and exegete. He was born in the year 370 AH and died in the year 450 AH (fifty and four hundred). Among his books are: 'al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya' in a volume printed in Egypt, 'Adab al-Dunya wa al-Din' in a volume printed in al-Jawa'ib, 'A'lam al-Nubuwwa', 'al-Iqna' fi al-Furu', 'Amthal al-Qur'an', 'Tashil al-Nasr wa Ta'jil al-Zafar', 'al-Hawi al-Kabir fi al-Furu', 'Siyasat al-Mulk', 'Qanun al-Wizara', 'al-Nukat wa al-'Uyun fi al-Tafsir' and others. (Hadiyat al-'Arifin: 1/689)
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This entry describes al-Mawardi, a towering Shafi'i scholar best known for his legal works, especially 'al-Hawi al-Kabir' and 'al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya'. His birth (370 AH) and death (450 AH) are given. For Hanafi students, al-Mawardi is important because he often engages with Hanafi positions in his works, and his 'al-Hawi' contains extensive comparative fiqh. His presence in a work on iftaa underscores the need for a mufti to be aware of different madhhabs.

Key Terms
صاحب الحاوى (Sahib al-Hawi): The author of the book 'al-Hawi'
فقيه مفسر (Faqih Mufassir): A jurist and Quran exegete
الماوردي (al-Mawardi): Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Habib al-Mawardi, the Shafi'i scholar

Introducing Ibn al-Sabbagh and His Works on Ikhtilaf
Biographical entry of a Shafi'i scholar with works on ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key works of Ibn al-Sabbagh and explain their relevance to the Hanafi tradition, especially for understanding inter-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Even a Shafi'i scholar's works on ikhtilaf serve as a valuable resource for Hanafi jurists.

This lesson examines the biographical entry of Ibn al-Sabbagh, a Shafi'i judge and professor at the Nizamiyya. Although not a Hanafi scholar, his works—particularly 'al-Kamil fi al-Khilaf'—systematically document points of difference between the Shafi'i and Hanafi schools. For the student of Hanafi fiqh and iftaa, such works are indispensable for understanding the broader landscape of legitimate disagreement and for preparing robust fatwas that engage with counterarguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar's Madhhab and Position
The entry explicitly states 'al-Shafi'i' after his name, and he is a judge and teacher at the Nizamiyya, a major Shafi'i institution. Recognize that this is a scholar from outside the Hanafi school.
Do not discount the value of non-Hanafi sources; they often provide the other side of an ikhtilaf.
2
List His Major Works
Scan the list of compiled works: 'al-Shamil fi al-Furu', 'al-Tariq al-Salim', 'al-Kamil fi al-Khilaf', etc. Note which works are discipline-specific (furu', usul, hadith, etc.).
Pay special attention to 'al-Kamil fi al-Khilaf bayn al-Shafi'iyya wa al-Hanafiyya'.
3
Identify the Work Directly Relevant to Hanafi-Shafi'i Differences
The work 'al-Kamil fi al-Khilaf' is explicitly about the comparative jurisprudence between the Shafi'i and Hanafi schools. This is a primary source for understanding the points of disagreement and the arguments of both sides.
Such works are often cited by later Hanafi jurists to present the opposing view and then rebut it.
4
Reflect on How This Resource Serves the Hanafi Tradition
Even though the author is Shafi'i, his systematic compilation of khilaf helps a Hanafi mufti anticipate objections, understand the strengths of the opposing view, and issue well-reasoned fatwas that address the evidence from both sides.
Knowledge of ikhtilaf is a key component of ijtihad and iftaa.

36 - Author of al-Shamil: Abd al-Sayyid ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far al-Shafi'i, the judge Abu Nasr ibn al-Sabbagh, teacher at the Nizamiyya. Commentary
This entry introduces Ibn al-Sabbagh, a Shafi'i judge and professor at the Nizamiyya madrasa in Baghdad. He authored several works, notably 'al-Shamil fi al-Furu' (a comprehensive work on Shafi'i furu') and a book on the points of difference between Shafi'is and Hanafis ('al-Kamil fi al-Khilaf'). This latter work is particularly relevant for Hanafi students as it systematically presents points of ikhtilaf. His biographical details (birth 400 AH, death 477 AH) place him in the 5th/11th century.

Al-Saymari and the Genre of Adab al-Mufti
Biographical entry of a Shafi'i judge and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the contributions of al-Saymari to the genre of adab al-mufti wa al-mustafti and explain the relevance of his works to a Hanafi student of iftaa.

Core Idea
Al-Saymari's Kitab fi Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti is a foundational work on the etiquette of fatwa-giving.

In this lesson, we examine a brief biographical entry on al-Saymari, a Shafi'i jurist from Basra. While his madhhab differs from the Hanafi school, his works—especially on the etiquette of muftis and seekers of fatwa—are valuable resources for any student of iftaa. By parsing this entry, you will learn to identify key scholarly attributes and understand the cross-madhhab significance of his writings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and his madhhab
Locate the name, kunya, and residential city. Note his madhhab affiliation: Shafi'i.
Al-Saymari is explicitly described as one of the most eminent Shafi'i jurists.
2
Note his scholarly authority
Look for phrases like 'hafiz li al-madhhab' and 'hujja' (authority). These indicate his mastery.
The text says he is a 'hafiz' (memorizer) of the madhhab and an authority well-versed in its subtleties.
3
Catalog his works
List the works mentioned, separating usul and furu. Pay special attention to the work on adab al-mufti.
His works include 'Kitab al-Qiyas wa al-'Ilal' (usul), and on furu: 'al-Idah', 'al-Kifaya', 'Kitab fi al-Shurut', and the key work 'Kitab fi Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti'.
4
Focus on the iftaa-specific work
Identify 'Kitab fi Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti' as directly relevant to the discipline of iftaa.
This work covers the etiquette (adab) for both the mufti and the one seeking a fatwa.
5
Reflect on cross-madhhab relevance
Consider why a Hanafi would study a Shafi'i work on adab. Recognize that adab principles often transcend madhhab boundaries.
While the ruling details may differ, the ethical framework for giving fatwa is shared across schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۷- الصميري : هو عبد الواحد بن الحسين بن محمد القاضي الصيمري المكنى بأبي القاسم، وكان يسكن البصرة، وكان من أجل فقهاء الشافعية، حافظ للمذهب، حجة فيه محيط بدقائقه وله تصانيف كثيرة، منها في الأصول : كتاب القياس والعلل" ، وفى الفروع : كتاب الإيضاح وهو في سبع مجلدات و كتاب الكفاية " ، و "كتاب فى الشروط" ، و"كتاب في أدب المفتى والمستفتى".

37 - al-Saymari: He is Abd al-Wahid ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Qadi al-Saymari, known by the kunya Abu al-Qasim. He lived in Basra and was among the most eminent Shafi'i jurists, a memorizer (hafiz) of the madhhab, an authority in it, well-versed in its subtleties. He has many works, including on usul: 'Kitab al-Qiyas wa al-'Ilal', and on furu': 'Kitab al-Idah' in seven volumes, 'Kitab al-Kifaya', 'Kitab fi al-Shurut', and 'Kitab fi Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti'.
See: (al-Fath al-Mubin: 1:21)
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This entry describes al-Saymari, a Shafi'i judge from Basra, emphasizing his mastery of the Shafi'i madhhab and his numerous works. Notably, he wrote a book on the etiquette of the mufti and the one seeking fatwa ('Kitab fi Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti'), which is directly relevant to the discipline of iftaa. His works on usul (like 'Kitab al-Qiyas wa al-'Ilal') and furu (like 'al-Idah' and 'al-Kifaya') show his breadth. For Hanafi students, his work on adab al-mufti is an important reference.

Key Terms
حافظ للمذهب (Hafiz li al-Madhhab): One who has memorized the rulings of the madhhab
أدب المفتى والمستفتى (Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti): The etiquette of the mufti and the seeker of fatwa

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Kitab al-Idah
C) Kitab fi Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti
D) Kitab al-Kifaya

Key Takeaway
Al-Saymari's 'Kitab fi Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti' is a seminal reference for the ethics of fatwa-giving, relevant to all madhahib.

Biography of 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib: Relevance for Iftaa
Biographical entry of a Kufan tabi'i and hadith narrator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details of 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib and explain why narrator reliability is essential for fatwa derivation.

Core Idea
A narrator's biography determines the weight of his hadith in fatwa.

This lesson presents the biographical entry of 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib, a renowned tabi'i and hadith scholar of Kufa. While he was not a Hanafi jurist himself, his inclusion in a work on iftaa underscores the importance of hadith narrators in the fatwa process. A mufti must assess the reliability of narrators whose hadith are cited. The evaluations quoted here—praise from Ahmad ibn Hanbal but a warning of memory decline—illustrate the nuanced nature of jarh wa ta'dil (criticism and validation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the person's full name and affiliation
Note his kunya, nasab, and nisba: Abu al-Sa'ib 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib al-Thaqafi al-Kufi.
The nisba 'al-Kufi' signals his connection to Kufa, a major center of Hanafi thought.
2
Determine his status and role
He is described as a tabi'i, 'one of the notable figures,' and 'muhaddith of Kufa.' This tells us he is a hadith authority, not a jurist.
His role as a hadith transmitter is crucial for iftaa.
3
Map his teachers and students
He narrated from his father, Ibn Abi Awfa, and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami. His students include Shu'ba, the two Hammad, the two Sufyan, and Ali ibn 'Asim.
The list shows he is a major link in transmission chains.
4
Analyze the scholarly evaluations (jarh wa ta'dil)
Ahmad ibn Hanbal calls him 'thiqah thiqah' (very trustworthy) but notes his memory deteriorated later. Abu Hatim specifies that Hammad ibn Zayd heard from him before that change.
This distinction is vital: hadith from his later period are considered weaker.
5
Note the year of death and source references
He died in 136 AH. The entry cites 'al-Kashif' and 'Siyar A'lam al-Nubala'.'
Dating helps in understanding which generation he belonged to.

Source Text

۳۸ - عطاء بن السائب : هو أبو السائب عطاء بن السائب الثقفي، الكوفي، أحد الأعلام ، تابعی مشهور، حسن الحديث، محدّث الكوفة، روى عن أبيه، وابن أبي أوفى، وأبى عبد الرحمن السلمي، وعنه شعبة والحمادان والسفيانان، وعلى ابن عاصم وأمم . قال أحمد : "ثقة ثقة، رجل صالح يختم القرآن كل ليلة، ساء حفظه بآخره " . قال أبو حاتم : "سمع منه حماد بن زيد قبل أن يتغير " . مات سنة ١٣٦هـ. 38 - 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib: He is Abu al-Sa'ib 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib al-Thaqafi, al-Kufi, one of the notable figures, a famous tabi'i, good in hadith, the muhaddith of Kufa. He narrated from his father, Ibn Abi Awfa, and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami. From him narrated Shu'ba, the two Hammad, the two Sufyan, Ali ibn 'Asim, and many others. Ahmad said: 'Thiqah thiqah, a righteous man who would complete the Quran every night, but his memory deteriorated towards the end.' Abu Hatim said: 'Hammad ibn Zayd heard from him before he changed.' He died in the year 136 AH. (al-Kashif: 2/265, Siyar A'lam al-Nubala': 6/336)

Commentary
This entry is about 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib, a tabi'i and hadith narrator from Kufa. Though not a jurist himself, he is included because of his importance as a hadith authority, which is essential for iftaa (since fatwas rely on hadith). The text gives his date of death (136 AH) and citations from Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Abu Hatim regarding his reliability. For Hanafi students, this shows that the index includes early narrators whose hadith are used in fiqh.

Key Terms
تابعي (Tabi'i): A successor, one who met a Companion
محدث الكوفة (Muhaddith al-Kufa): The hadith scholar of Kufa

Ibn al-Sabbagh: A Shafi'i Scholar Relevant to Hanafi Ifta'
Biographical entry for a Shafi'i jurist and teacher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of Ibn al-Sabbagh's work on khilaf for Hanafi ifta' practice.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Sabbagh's comparative fiqh work aids Hanafi muftis in understanding Shafi'i arguments.

This lesson introduces al-Qadi Abu Nasr ibn al-Sabbagh, a Shafi'i jurist who taught at the Nizamiyya madrasa in Baghdad. Though not a Hanafi, his authorship of a work on the differences between the Shafi'i and Hanafi schools makes him a valuable reference for Hanafi muftis. Knowing the opposing school's position is essential for accurate fatwa, especially in multi-madhhab contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his madhhab
The text identifies Ibn al-Sabbagh as a Shafi'i judge and teacher. Note that he is not a Hanafi scholar, but his works are relevant across madhhabs.
The title 'al-Qadi' indicates he served as a judge.
2
Extract his key biographical dates
He was born in 400 AH and died in 477 AH. These dates place him in the 5th century AH, a period of rich scholarly activity.
Knowing the era helps contextualize his works relative to other scholars.
3
List his notable works
The text lists several works, including 'al-Shamil fi al-Furu'' (comprehensive fiqh), 'al-Tariq al-Salim' (hadith and tasawwuf), and crucially 'al-Kamil fi al-Khilaf bayna al-Shafi'iyya wa al-Hanafiyya' (the complete work on differences between Shafi'is and Hanafis).
The work on khilaf is especially relevant for Hanafi muftis.
4
Connect his work on khilaf to Hanafi ifta'
A Hanafi mufti may need to address questions involving Shafi'i rulings. Ibn al-Sabbagh's 'al-Kamil fi al-Khilaf' provides an authoritative presentation of Shafi'i positions for comparison.
This resource helps ensure that fatwas accurately represent the opposing view.
5
Recognize the source of the entry
The entry is cited from 'Hadiyyat al-'Arifin', a biographical dictionary. Such entries are common in ifta' literature as references for scholarly authority.
Knowing the source aids in assessing reliability.

Biography of 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib: Narrator Criticism in Fatwa
Biographical entry for a hadith narrator used in fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a narrator's biography (teachers, students, evaluations) and explain why narrator reliability (jarh wa ta'dil) is essential for fatwa methodology.

Core Idea
A narrator's memory decline (ikhtilat) affects the reliability of his hadith, which in turn impacts fatwa.

This lesson presents the biography of 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib, a prominent Kufan hadith narrator from the Tabi'un. Although not a jurist himself, his inclusion in Imam al-Nawawi's 'Adab al-Fatwa' highlights the critical link between hadith criticism and fatwa. Understanding a narrator's chain of transmission, his teachers and students, and scholarly evaluations (especially regarding memory deterioration) is essential for a mufti to weigh hadith evidence correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator's full name and lineage
Read the first sentence to learn his name, kunya, nisbah, and status. This establishes his identity.
2
List his teachers and students
Note the key narrators he learned from and those who narrated from him. This helps assess his chain position.
Teachers: his father, Ibn Abi Awfa, Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami. Students: Shu'ba, Hammad (two), Sufyan (two), Ali ibn Asim, etc.
3
Analyze scholarly evaluations
Examine the quotes from Ahmad and Abu Hatim. Ahmad praises him but notes memory decline towards the end; Abu Hatim says Hammad heard him before he changed.
This is critical for jarh wa ta'dil – later narrations after his memory decline are considered weak.
4
Connect to fatwa methodology
Understand why a mufti needs to know such details: a hadith from 'Ata' after memory decline cannot be used as strong evidence without corroboration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۹ - عطاء بن السائب : هو أبو السائب عطاء بن السائب الثقفي، الكوفي، أحد الأعلام ، تابعی مشهور، حسن الحديث، محدّث الكوفة، روى عن أبيه، وابن أبي أوفى، وأبى عبد الرحمن السلمي، وعنه شعبة والحمادان والسفيانان، وعلى ابن عاصم وأمم . قال أحمد : "ثقة ثقة، رجل صالح يختم القرآن كل ليلة، ساء حفظه بآخره " . قال أبو حاتم : "سمع منه حماد بن زيد قبل أن يتغير " . مات سنة ١٣٦هـ. 39 - 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib: He is Abu al-Sa'ib 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib al-Thaqafi, al-Kufi, one of the prominent figures, a famous Tabi'i, has good hadith, the hadith scholar of Kufa. He narrated from his father, Ibn Abi Awfa, and Abu 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami. From him narrated Shu'ba, Hammad (two), Sufyan (two), 'Ali ibn 'Asim, and many others. Ahmad said: 'Thiqah, thiqah, a righteous man who would complete the Quran every night, but his memory deteriorated at the end.' Abu Hatim said: 'Hammad ibn Zaid heard from him before he changed.' He died in 136 AH. (al-Kashif: 2/265, Siyar A'lam al-Nubala': 6/336)
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This entry is from the biographical index of Imam al-Nawawi's 'Adab al-Fatwa'. It covers 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib, a notable hadith narrator from the Tabi'un. Although not a jurist himself, his mention in this index is relevant because the science of fatwa depends heavily on reliable hadith transmission. The entry gives his teachers, students, and evaluations from critics like Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Abu Hatim. The note about his memory deterioration (ikhtilat) is important for hadith criticism.

Key Terms
عطاء بن السائب ('Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib): A Kufan hadith narrator from the Tabi'un, considered trustworthy but later suffered memory decline.
اختلاط (ikhtilat): Memory mixing or deterioration in a narrator, causing later narrations to be considered weak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib's memory deterioration significant for hadith criticism?
A) It means all his narrations are unreliable
B) It means only narrations from before the deterioration are generally considered reliable
C) It means he never narrated authentic hadith
D) It means he was a liar

Key Takeaway
A narrator's memory deterioration (ikhtilat) is a critical factor in hadith criticism; it affects the legal weight of his narrations and must be considered by a mufti.

Imam al-Ghazali: A Colossus of Islamic Scholarship
Biographical entry for the celebrated Shafi'i scholar and Hujjat al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state key biographical facts about Imam al-Ghazali and explain why a Hanafi mufti studies his works.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali, though Shafi'i, is essential reading for a Hanafi mufti in usul and fatwa.

This short biography introduces you to Imam al-Ghazali, one of the most brilliant minds in Islamic history. Though he belonged to the Shafi'i madhhab, his contributions to usul al-fiqh, theology, and spiritual revival are studied across all schools, including our Hanafi tradition. Pay close attention to his education under Imam al-Haramayn and his lasting impact on the field of ifta'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and title
Notice the honorifics: 'Hujjat al-Islam' and 'Zayn al-Din'. This tells you his stature in the Muslim community.
His full name is Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Tusi.
2
Trace his early life and education
He was born in Tus in 450 AH, lost his father early, and was recommended to attend madrasa for fiqh. He studied under Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili and then Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni.
His journey from poverty to becoming the most perceptive scholar of his time is remarkable.
3
Note his relationship with his teacher
Imam al-Haramayn praised him outwardly but had inner reservations due to Ghazali's quick expression and strong nature.
This reflects scholarly dynamics of the time.
4
Identify falsely attributed works
Two works, 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' and 'al-Madmun bihi 'ala Ghayr Ahlihi', are incorrectly attributed to al-Ghazali.
Be cautious when citing his works.
5
Note his death and legacy
He died on 14 Jumada al-Akhira 505 AH at age 55 in Tus. His most famous work is 'Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din'.
His 'al-Mustasfa' is crucial for usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٩ - الغزالي : هو الإمام حجة الإسلام زين الدين أبو حامد، محمد بن محمد بن محمد الطوسى ،الغزالي إمام باسمه تنشرح الصدور، وتحيى النفوس، وبرسمه تفتخر المحابر وتهتز الطروس، ولسماعه تخشع الأصوات وتخضع الرؤوس . ولد بطوس، سنة خمسين وأربع مائة ، وكان والده يغزل الصوف ويبيعه في حانوته، فلما احتضر أوصى به وبأخيه أحمد إلى صديق له صوفي صالح ، فعلمهما الخط وأدبهما ، ثم نفذ منه ما خلفه أبوهما ، وتعذر عليهما القوت فقال : أرى لكما أن تلجأ إلى المدرسة قال الغزالي : فصرنا إلى المدرسة نطلب الفقه لتحصيل القوت، قاشتغل بها مدة ثم ارتحل إلى أبي نصر الإسماعيلي بجرجان ثم إلى إمام الحرمين بنيسابور، فاشتغل عليه ولازمه حتى صار أنظر أهل زمانه، وجلس للإقراء في حياة إمامه وصنف . وكان الإمام في الظاهر، يظهر التبجح به، وفي الباطن عنده منه شيء، لما يصدر منه من سرعة العبارة وقوة الطبع، وينسب إليه تصنيفان ليسا له بل وضعا عليه، وهما : "السر المكتوم " و المضمون به على غير أهله . وله تصانيف، من أشهرها "الإحياء". وكانت وفاته بطوس، صبيحة يوم الاثنين، رابع عشر جمادى الآخرة، سنة خمس وخمسمائة، عمره خمس وخمسون سنة . (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٢٤٢/٢-٢٤٤)
39 - al-Ghazali: He is the Imam, Hujjat al-Islam, Zayn al-Din Abu Hamid, Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Tusi, al-Ghazali, an Imam by whose name hearts open and souls revive, and by whose fame inkpots are proud and pages quiver, and at hearing him voices humble and heads bow. He was born in Tus in the year 450 AH. His father used to spin wool and sell it in his shop. When he was dying, he entrusted him and his brother Ahmad to a righteous Sufi friend of his, who taught them writing and discipline. Then the wealth their father left them ran out, and sustenance became difficult for them, so he said: 'I think you should go to the madrasa.' Al-Ghazali said: So we went to the madrasa seeking fiqh for sustenance. He studied there for a time, then traveled to Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili in Jurjan, then to Imam al-Haramayn in Nishapur. He studied with him and accompanied him until he became the most perceptive of his time, and he sat for teaching during his imam's lifetime and authored works. The imam outwardly showed pride in him, but inwardly had something against him because of his quick expression and strong nature. Two works are attributed to him falsely: 'al-Sirr al-Maktum' and 'al-Madmun bihi 'ala Ghayr Ahlihi'. He has many works, the most famous being 'al-Ihya'. His death was in Tus, on the morning of Monday, 14 Jumada al-Akhira in the year 505 AH, at the age of 55 years. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnavi: 2/242-244)
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This is a lengthy biographical entry for Imam al-Ghazali, one of the most influential scholars in Islamic history. Though a Shafi'i jurist, his works on usul al-fiqh, philosophy, and spirituality are referenced across madhhabs. The entry details his early life, education under Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, and his rise to prominence. It also notes the false attribution of two works to him. His 'Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din' is a masterpiece. He died in 505 AH. This biography is included in the index of 'Adab al-Fatwa' because his works, particularly on usul and fatwa, are essential.

Key Terms
الغزالي (al-Ghazali): Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, a Shafi'i scholar, theologian, mystic, and author of 'Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) al-Mustasfa
B) al-Sirr al-Maktum
C) al-Ihya
D) al-Madmun bihi 'ala Ghayr Ahlihi

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ghazali was a Shafi'i scholar whose works on usul and spirituality are essential references for Hanafi fatwa methodology.

The Character of a Mufti: Lessons from a Qayrawani Scholar
Biographical entry for a Qayrawani scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key virtues of a classical Hanafi scholar and explain how these virtues relate to the adab of a mufti.

Core Idea
A mufti's authority rests on both knowledge and character — zuhd and wara' are essential.

This biography from Tadhkirat al-Huffaz presents a Qayrawani scholar whose life exemplifies the qualities needed for iftaa. Although his name is lost, the text preserves his legacy of piety, deep learning, and devoted teaching. For the student of usul al-iftaa, this entry serves as a reminder that the mufti is not merely a conveyor of rulings but a living embodiment of the tradition's ethical standards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's teachers and students
Note whom he studied under (Abu Zayd, Abu Muhammad al-Asili) and who studied under him (Abu Imran al-Fasi, etc.). This shows the chain of transmission and the scholarly network.
The chain connects him to Sahih al-Bukhari through Meccan teachers.
2
Extract the character traits mentioned
Hatem al-Tarabulsi describes him as 'zahid' (ascetic) and 'wari'' (scrupulous). These are not just personal virtues but professional requirements for a mufti.
Wara' is the careful avoidance of doubtful matters, critical for issuing fatwas.
3
List his authored works
He wrote al-Mumahhad fi al-Fiqh, al-Munqidh min Shubh al-Ta'wil, and Kitab al-Manasik wa Aqa'id. This shows his range from fiqh to theology.
Al-Munqidh suggests engagement with heresiographical refutation, relevant for iftaa in times of theological deviation.
4
Reflect on the description of his funeral
Many people spent the night at his grave, tents were pitched, and poets eulogized him. This indicates the high esteem in which he was held by the community.
Community trust is a key indicator of a mufti's acceptance.
5
Connect to adab al-mufti
The virtues of zuhd and wara', coupled with deep learning, are foundational for anyone undertaking iftaa. This biography illustrates the ideal mufti character.
See al-Adab al-Mufti by Ibn al-Salah and later Hanafi works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصحيح بمكة على أبي زيد وصاحبه أبو محمد الأصيلي. ذكره حاتم الطرابلسي فقال : "كان زاهداً ورعاً ، لم أر بالقيروان أحدا إلا معترفًا بفضله". تفقه عليه أبو عمران الفاسي، وأبو القاسم الكبيدى، وعتيق السوسي وغيرهم. وله تواليف بديعة ككتاب الممهد في الفقه و أحكام الديانات" و "المنقذ من شبه التأويل" و "كتاب المناسك و عقائد وسوى ذلك . ارتحل سنة اثنتين وخمسين فغاب خمسة أعوام. قال حاتم : توفي في ربيع الآخر سنة ثلاث وأربع مائة بمدينة القيروان، وبات عند قبره خلق كثير، وضربت الأخبية لهم، ورثته الشعراء رحمه الله تعالى . (تذكرة الحفاظ : ۱۰۷۹/۳-۱۰۸۰)
He heard Sahih in Mecca from Abu Zayd and his companion Abu Muhammad al-Asili. Hatem al-Tarabulsi mentioned him and said: 'He was a zahid and wari', I have not seen in Qayrawan anyone except acknowledging his virtue.' Abu Imran al-Fasi, Abu al-Qasim al-Kabidi, Atiq al-Susi and others studied under him. He had wonderful compositions such as 'al-Mumahhad fi al-Fiqh wa Ahkam al-Diyanat' and 'al-Munqidh min Shubh al-Ta'wil' and 'Kitab al-Manasik wa Aqa'id' and others. He set out in the year 52 [meaning 352?] and was absent for five years. Hatem said: He died in Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 403 AH in the city of Qayrawan, and many people spent the night at his grave, and tents were pitched for them, and poets eulogized him, may Allah have mercy on him. (Tadhkirat al-Huffaz 3/1079-1080).
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This is a biographical entry about a scholar from Qayrawan. Though unnamed in the surviving text, he was a notable figure: he studied Sahih al-Bukhari in Mecca under Abu Zayd and Abu Muhammad al-Asili. Hatem al-Tarabulsi praised his zuhd and wara'. Prominent students like Abu Imran al-Fasi studied under him. He authored several works including al-Mumahhad fi al-Fiqh and al-Munqidh min Shubh al-Ta'wil. He traveled in the year 352? and was absent for five years. He died in Qayrawan in Rabi' al-Akhir 403 AH, and his funeral drew a large gathering. The source is Tadhkirat al-Huffaz.

Key Terms
زاهد (zahid): One who practices asceticism, abstaining from worldly pleasures for the sake of worship.
ورع (wari'): Scrupulousness, avoiding doubtful matters.
تواليف (tawa'lif): Compositions or authored works.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biographical entry with praise from a well-known scholar.

A single biography reveals the scholarly network of the Hanafi school.

This lesson introduces Qadi Abu al-Tayyib al-Armani, a Hanafi judge from Armenia who studied in Baghdad. Though brief, his biography illustrates the movement of scholars and the transmission of fiqh across the Islamic world.
